1 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Terhaar v. Joint Class A Sch. Dist.


No. 8240


Supreme Court of Idaho


77 Idaho 112; 289 P.2d 623; 1955 Ida. LEXIS 324



October 6, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 22, 1955.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen sought review of a judgment rendered by the trial court (Idaho), which dismissed his complaint filed against defendants, school district and two county governments. The citizen claimed on appeal that the trial court improperly dismissed his complaint that the school district that was formed between the two counties was based upon a law that was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The citizen filed a complaint, seeking an injunction against a school district and two county governments. The citizen claimed that the school district that was formed between the two counties was based on a law that was unconstitutional. The trial court denied the injunction and dismissed the lawsuit. Subsequent to the denial of the injunction, a bond election was held and a proposed bond issue was rejected by the voters of the district. Thereafter, by proceedings subsequent to this appeal, the school district was divided and two new districts were created out of its territory. It did not appear that the legality of the new districts was dependent on that of the old. On appeal, the court held that the citizen's appeal had become moot and there was no need to determine the constitutionality of the law upon which the school district was to be formed.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal on the grounds of mootness.

 

2 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Yellowstone Pipe Line Co. v. Drummond


No. 8198


Supreme Court of Idaho


77 Idaho 36; 287 P.2d 288; 1955 Ida. LEXIS 315



July 12, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 14, 1955.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants mineral rights owners challenged an order of the trial court (Idaho), which granted appellee pipeline company's request for possession of a right-of-way to construct a pipeline and affixed compensation.


OVERVIEW: The pipeline company sought to build a pipeline for the purpose of transporting petroleum. The pipeline company filed a motion seeking possession of the right of way under Idaho Code § 7-717. The trial court affixed compensation based on the owner's affidavit as to value and damages. The owners contended that § 7-717 was unconstitutional and void as it violated Idaho Const. art. I, §§ 13,14. The court found that the provisions in § 7-717 that the pipeline company may file an affidavit appraising damages and that the court upon such affidavit could enter an order that upon the payment of double such amount, the pipeline company could take possession, did not proved the owner's with due process of law. The court further determined that the notice provision in § 7-717 was also defective in that it did not provide for either actual service or constructive service of notice of motion for possession. The court determined that because it would have been inequitable to force the pipeline company to dig up its pipeline and surrender possession of the right of way the pipeline company was permitted to retain possession pending a final determination as to just compensation to the owners.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order of possession and remanded to the trial court with instructions to enter an order permitting the pipeline company to continue possession of the right-of-way sought to be condemned until a final determination was reached as to just compensation.

 

3 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Berry v. Summers


No. 8221


Supreme Court of Idaho


76 Idaho 446; 283 P.2d 1093; 1955 Ida. LEXIS 301



May 4, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 9, 1955.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, dental mechanics or technicians, sought review of a judgment of the trial court (Idaho), which upheld the constitutionality of 1953 Idaho Sess. Laws ch. 105, § 1 and which permanently enjoined appellants from constructing, correcting, repairing, or relining dental prosthetic appliances or dentures without first complying with Idaho Code tit. 54, ch. 9 and from engaging in the acts that constituted the practice of dentistry.


OVERVIEW: Prior to and after the effective date of 1953 Idaho Sess. Laws ch. 105, § 1, appellants performed mechanical work for wearers of artificial dentures, including relining and repairing broken denture plates. Appellants performed such services in their dental laboratories, and neither they nor any of their craftsmen performed any work whatever in the oral cavity of any person. The court held that the requirement that a person performing services such as those performed by appellants be trained and licensed as a dentist was not reasonably necessary for the protection of the public. In addition, pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Idaho Const. art. I, §§ 1 and 13, the legislature could not do away with the vested rights of appellants and others similarly situated by prohibiting them from following an occupation that had been legislatively recognized as an independent calling for 34 years. Accordingly, the court held that so far as 1953 Idaho Sess. Laws ch. 105, § 1 affected or was intended to affect the independent occupation of dental mechanic or technician in the performance of mechanical work upon inert matter in a dental laboratory, it was unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court with instructions to dissolve the injunction and to enter judgment in favor of appellants.

 

4 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Grange Mut. Life Co. v. State Tax Comm'n


No. 8113


Supreme Court of Idaho


76 Idaho 303; 283 P.2d 187; 1955 Ida. LEXIS 271



March 30, 1955 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal to the Idaho Supreme Court from a trial court decision declaring that plaintiff corporation did not owe state taxes on interest income received from United States Government bonds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, state tax collector, sought to collect on an alleged tax deficiency of plaintiff, a life insurance corporation. Case centered around interest that plaintiff received from certain United States Government bonds; defendant claimed interest income was taxable, plaintiff claimed it was not. Plaintiff brought an action in the trial court seeking to avoid payment of the alleged deficiencies; plaintiff prevailed in the trial court, resulting in an appeal to the state supreme court. That court reversed, rejecting plaintiff's argument that prior version of statute, which exempted interest from federal bonds, still controlled due to statutory compiler's erroneous exclusion of that exemption during statutory codification process, inasmuch as legislature acted after compiler's efforts, and thus ratified the change; and further turned aside plaintiff's contention that states lack the authority to enact such taxes of federal bond interest, citing significant precedent to the contrary.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; plaintiff owed tax deficiency, as state legislature deliberately modified state tax statute to remove previous exemption for interest income received from United States Government bonds.

 

5 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Garden City


Nos. 8045, 8046


Supreme Court of Idaho


74 Idaho 513; 265 P.2d 328; 1953 Ida. LEXIS 315



December 23, 1953 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and various individuals, appealed a decree of the trial court (Idaho), which ruled that defendants were maintaining and carrying on illegal lotteries in violation of Idaho Const. art. 3, § 20 and enjoined defendants from maintaining gambling places. The trial court also order the seizure and sale of the various individuals' personal property, closed their places of business, and placed liens on their real estate.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were operating gambling places pursuant to two statutes that purported to legalize slot machines and the operation of punchboards, chance spindles, and chance prize games. Plaintiff State brought suit to have such activities enjoined, claiming that such operations were illegal and injurious to the public morals. The trial court granted injunctive relief and imposed certain penalties. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the gambling devices by whatever name they were called were lotteries and, as such, were constitutionally prohibited. The challenged statutes purporting to legalize such gambling devises were unconstitutional attempts on the part of the legislature to legalize lotteries by simply defining lotteries by other names. Such gambling devices were lotteries, and the legislative act authorizing, or attempting to authorize their operation, in any manner was unconstitutional. The court modified the judgment so as to strike to penalty provisions, finding that such penalties would have worked a hardship on those who acted in good faith and relied on the validity of the challenged statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decree except those portions allowing the seizure and sale of the personal property, placing a lien on the real estate; and closing defendants' places in which the gambling devices were operated and maintained. The court struck such penalty provisions from the decree and affirmed the decree as modified.

 

6 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Schmidt v. Village of Kimberly


No. 7983


Supreme Court of Idaho


74 Idaho 48; 256 P.2d 515; 1953 Ida. LEXIS 251



April 22, 1953 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross-appeals were taken from a declaratory judgment of an Idaho trial court, which, at the request of plaintiff taxpayer, ruled upon the validity of the Revenue Bond Act, 1951 Idaho Sess. Laws ch. 47, and defendant village's ordinances in respect thereto.


OVERVIEW: The Revenue Bond Act authorized municipalities to issue bonds for the construction of water and sewer facilities. The village passed an ordinance providing for a sewage collection system and sewage treatment plant. Municipal voters approved the bond proposal. The village intended to use a portion of the revenue bond funds to purchase property outside the city upon which to construct the sewage treatment and disposal plant. The trial court upheld the validity of the statute but found Kimberly, Idaho, Ordinance No. 139 to be invalid in three respects. The court affirmed in part, holding that Idaho Const. art. 8, § 3, as amended, expressly empowered the village to acquire land outside its corporate limits. The revenue from the village's existing water system could be applied under Idaho Code § 50-2818 to the redemption of the bond issue. The trial court erred, however, in holding that the village could not provide parity of lien for subsequent bonds; prior bondholders' priority of lien under Idaho Code § 50-2824 could be waived. The issue of whether the village could compel tenants to connect to the sewer was not ripe for decision. The disconnection charges were reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that upheld the validity of the statute and reversed the rulings that had found portions of the ordinance to be invalid.

 

7 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Newland v. Child


No. 7869


Supreme Court of Idaho


73 Idaho 530; 254 P.2d 1066; 1953 Ida. LEXIS 241



March 16, 1953 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband and wife, were recipients of old-age assistance benefits pursuant to the Public Assistance Law. They sought review of a judgment of the trial court (Idaho) which found that appellee state had a lien on their real property pursuant to Idaho Code § 56-224a.


OVERVIEW:  Idaho Code § 56-224a required recipients of old-age benefits who owned real property to grant the state a lien in their real property. Appellants challenged the constitutionality of § 56-224a. The court held that the statute was constitutional and that the state had a lien on appellants' real property. The court held: (1) appellants' right to possess property under Idaho Const. art. 1, § 1 was subject to reasonable limitations imposed by the state in the interests of the common welfare; (2) the state had constitutional or common-law duty to provide support to appellants; (3) appellants had no vested right to receive old-age assistance benefits; (4) appellants were not denied equal protection of the law in violation of Idaho Const. art. 1, §2 even though recipients who only owned only personal property were not required to grant a lien upon their personal property to the state; and (5) § 56-224a was not a local and special law violative of Idaho Const. art. 3, §19 because it was applicable to all persons throughout the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment holding that the state had a lien on appellant's real property.

 

8 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Petty


Nos. 7778, 7780


Supreme Court of Idaho


73 Idaho 136; 248 P.2d 218; 1952 Ida. LEXIS 221



July 23, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 6, 1952.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the judgment from the trial court (Idaho) that sustained the demurrers of defendants, which were filed alleging that Idaho Code § 18-6607 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were separately charged by information with the crime of lewd and lascivious acts under Idaho Code § 18-6607. The trial court sustained defendants' demurrers on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional. In reversing, the court held that the informations charged the specific intent required by Idaho Code § 18-6607 and the specific intent required as an element of assault with intent to rape, under Idaho Code §§ 18-901, 18-907, and 18-6101. The other elements of both crimes being sufficiently alleged, the informations charged both lewd and lascivious conduct and assault with intent to commit rape. Acts leading to rape or assault with intent to rape, would be lewd and lascivious and would evince the intent described in Idaho Code § 18-6607 where an offense could not be committed without necessarily committing another offense, and, thus, the latter was a necessarily included offense. The statutory rule against charging more than one offense, Idaho Code § 19-1413 and Idaho Code § 19-1703, does not apply to included offenses.


OUTCOME: The court held that the demurrers should have been overruled and reversed the judgment from the trial court.

 

9 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Boise City v. Better Homes


No. 7842


Supreme Court of Idaho


72 Idaho 441; 243 P.2d 303; 1952 Ida. LEXIS 190



April 4, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected on Denial of Rehearing May 1, 1952.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed suit against defendant landowner to prevent the landowner from maintaining a lumberyard on its property. It argued that the lumberyard was in violation of a zoning ordinance. An Idaho trial court entered judgment in favor of the city. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner answered the city's allegations with a general denial. At trial, the landowner sought to prove that it had used the property as a lumberyard before the effective date of the zoning restrictions. The city's objection to this proof as "new matter" was sustained. The landowner then sought leave to amend its answer, which was denied on the ground of surprise. The court stated that to state a cause of action, the city had to prove that the landowner's nonconforming use did not exist when the restrictions became effective. The allegations of the complaint, though ambiguous, had to be construed to allege that the use commenced after the effective date of the restrictions. The general denial, therefore, put in issue the question of the prior existence of the nonconforming use. As for the city's claim of surprise, in its case in chief, the city offered evidence as to when the lumberyard business commenced, as it was required to do. There was no showing to support the assertion of surprise, and the city, by its ambiguous pleading, helped to create the situation out of which the claim of surprise arose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment. It remanded the case with directions for the trial court to permit the parties to offer further evidence on the issue of whether the use complained of existed before the effective date of the zoning restrictions.

 

10 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Heitz


No. 7765


Supreme Court of Idaho


72 Idaho 107; 238 P.2d 439; 1951 Ida. LEXIS 227



November 20, 1951 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of a district court (Idaho), which upheld his conviction in the justice court of the crime of driving a motor vehicle upon a public highway of the state, loaded in excess of weight limitations as promulgated, posted, and prescribed by the Commissioner of Public Works under authority of Idaho Code § 49-606. Defendant contended that Idaho Code §§ 49-605, 49-606, 49-609, 49-611 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of operating a truck and trailer in excess of the posted maximum load limits that were prescribed pursuant to the powers conferred on the Commissioner of Public Works by Idaho Code § 49-606. Although a legislative body could not delegate legislative power to make laws to another body, such rule did not preclude conferring the power upon the Commissioner of Public Works to prescribe or vary regulations concerning motor vehicles used on public highways within definite limits fixed by the legislative body. Limitations of size and weight were manifestly subjects within the broad range of legislative discretion and the police power of the state that were not repugnant to the commerce clause. The court rejected defendant's contention that Idaho Code § 49-606 had to be construed in pari materia with other provisions of the act and declared unconstitutional if Idaho Code §§ 49-605, 49-611 were unconstitutional. Defendant was not in a class against whom discrimination operated to question Idaho Code §§ 49-605, 49-611, and the court concluded that such constitutional questions did not affect the constitutionality of the section under which defendant was convicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

11 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Common Sch. Dist. v. Lunden


No. 7744


Supreme Court of Idaho


71 Idaho 486; 233 P.2d 806; 1951 Ida. LEXIS 310



July 17, 1951 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county board of commissioners appealed a judgment of the trial court (Idaho), which issued the writ of prohibition filed by plaintiffs, a school district, its trustees, and three taxpayers, to prohibit the commissioners from calling an election or proceeding further with the proposed reorganization of the school system because the transcript did not contain or show proof of service of notice of appeal, required by Idaho Code § 13-202.


OVERVIEW: The commissioners adopted a proposal to form a new school district. Plaintiffs made application to the trial court for a writ prohibiting the commissioners from calling an election or proceeding further with the proposed reorganization. The trial court issued the writ. The commissioners appealed, arguing that plaintiffs had an adequate remedy on appeal, that the acts prohibited were purely ministerial, and thus, the prohibition did not lie. The court held that an appeal was available to plaintiffs. Thus, if the appeal was an adequate remedy, plaintiffs were not entitled to a writ of prohibition. The legislature provided for an appeal from all actions or orders of the commissioners whether they were ministerial or not. Under Idaho Code § 33-519, the remedy provided by an appeal would be broad. Thus, the remedy was adequate and plaintiffs were not entitled to a writ of prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's issuance of a writ and dismissed the action.

 

12 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Poffenroth v. Culinary Workers Union


No. 7695


Supreme Court of Idaho


71 Idaho 412; 232 P.2d 968; 1951 Ida. LEXIS 298; 28 L.R.R.M. 2318; 20 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P66,404



June 27, 1951 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent employer secured a temporary injunction and show cause order from the district court (Idaho) to prevent appellants, a labor union and its officers, from picketing the employer's boarding house in an attempt to persuade employees to join the union. The union resisted the injunction upon the ground that Idaho Code § 44-712 was unconstitutional as denying a minority group, less than 50 percent of employees, their constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The employer's complaint in the action for injunctive relief stated a cause of action under Idaho Code § 44-712, alleging none of its employees were members of the union and that the union had not been authorized by any of the employees to represent them; thus, no labor dispute as defined by the statute was involved and the inhibiting provisions of Idaho Code §§ 44-703 and -706 did not apply. None of the employees were joined in the action or joined with the union in resisting the issuance of the injunction and none of the employees urging that Idaho Code § 44-712 was unconstitutional. On appeal of the issuance of the injunction, the court pointed out that the union was not claiming anything as minority employees, merely as a labor union entirely disconnected from the employer and, therefore, not within the orbit of the statute in any particular. The union merely projected a contingency not in existence, and whatever might be the effect of the statute in the future on supposititious cases not in the instant record, the union, not being employees of any kind, could not challenge the statute as discriminating against minority employees.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

13 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Robb v. Nielson


No. 7735


Supreme Court of Idaho


71 Idaho 222; 229 P.2d 981; 1951 Ida. LEXIS 268



April 3, 1951 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff County Auditor of Valley County filed an application for a writ of mandate requiring defendant Auditor of the State of Idaho to issue a warrant on the Fish and Game Fund for payment of a state voucher in lieu of taxes upon land acquired by the Idaho Fish and Game Department.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Idaho Code para. 5, § 36-104, the department acquired land in the county for game farms, a public use. Title to and ownership of the lands were in the state. Plaintiff caused a state voucher to be drawn to be paid by the state in lieu of taxes on the land. The voucher was approved by the director of the department and was presented to defendant for payment. Defendant refused to draw a warrant on the fund for payment of the voucher. Plaintiff filed an application for a writ of mandate requiring defendant to issue the warrant. The court issued an alternative writ of mandate requiring defendant to issue the warrant or show cause why he should not do so. Defendant filed an answer challenging the constitutionality of Idaho Code § 36-125. The court denied the application for the writ of mandate and held that § 36-125 sought to accomplish the same result as taxation of the state's land, so was void because of its conflict with Idaho Const. art. VII, § 4. The fact that the base for computation of the sums to be paid was fixed at the assessed value of the lands at the time they were dropped from the assessment roll, did not divest the proceedings of their character as a tax.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiff's application for a writ of mandate and quashed the alternative writ of mandate.

 

14 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. Schultz


No. 7667


Supreme Court of Idaho


71 Idaho 145; 227 P.2d 586; 1951 Ida. LEXIS 259



February 3, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 27, 1951.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtors appealed from a judgment of foreclosure by a trial court (Idaho) and denied that they were in default under the terms of a note and mortgage and affirmatively alleged that the note, mortgage, and lease constituted one agreement and that such agreement was illegal and unenforceable.


OVERVIEW: Appellants executed a promissory note in favor of respondents and the parties contemporaneously entered into a mortgage and lease of the premises so secured. Appellants failed to pay the insurance and the same was paid by respondents who invoked immediate payment under the agreement. When payment was not made respondents instituted foreclosure proceedings. Appellants contended that note, mortgage, and lease constituted one agreement and that such agreement was illegal and unenforceable. On review, the court held that any illegal provisions of a contract were properly severable and did not bar recovery for the lawful provisions of the agreement. Accordingly, the decision in favor of foreclosure was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

15 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Campbell


No. 7631


Supreme Court of Idaho


70 Idaho 408; 219 P.2d 956; 1950 Ida. LEXIS 189



June 26, 1950 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 11, 1950.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of a trial court in Ada County (Idaho) that convicted him of the crime of issuing a check without funds under the provisions of Idaho Code § 18-3106.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the verdict was contrary to the evidence because the salesperson to whom he offered the check did not accept it or part with anything of value. He also argued that § 18-3106 was unconstitutional on the ground of vagueness. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, concluding that evidence that he presented a check to the salesperson, which was drawn on an account at which defendant did not maintain an account, was sufficient to support the conviction. The court explained that the making or uttering of the check was sufficient although the payee might reject the check such that there was no completed delivery. The court found that the completion of the crime under § 18-3106 did not depend upon the success of the enterprise. The court held that § 18-3106 was sufficiently definite and certain in the words used and in so defining the offense of issuing a check without funds as to convey to a person of ordinary understanding an adequate description of the evil intended to be prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

16 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Boughton v. Price


No. 7603


Supreme Court of Idaho


70 Idaho 243; 215 P.2d 286; 1950 Ida. LEXIS 167



February 23, 1950 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Secretary of State filed a demurrer to plaintiff candidate's mandamus action. The candidate, through his mandamus action, sought an order declaring a portion of the Judge's Retirement Act contained in Idaho Code § 1-2007, as amended by 1949 Idaho Sess. Laws 130, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The candidate's term as district court judge was set to expire, therefore, the candidate wanted to seek reelection to the office of district court judge. However, the candidate would be more than 70 years of age before the termination of his term. The candidate informed the Secretary of State that the candidate intended to run for reelection. The Secretary of State informed the candidate that the candidate was not eligible to run for reelection because the candidate was too old. The Judge's Retirement Act contained in Idaho Code § 1-2007, as amended by 1949 Idaho Sess. Laws 130, provided that no person shall be eligible for appointment or election to the office of district judge after attaining the age of 70 years. The candidate argued that the Idaho Code § 1-2007, by adding an additional qualification for the office of district judge, was in conflict with Idaho Const. art. V, § 23. The court held that Idaho Const. art. V, § 23 did not restrict the power of the legislature to add additional reasonable qualifications for the office of district judgment. Therefore, the court held that Idaho Code § 1-2007 was not in conflict with Idaho Const. art. V, § 23.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the Secretary of State's demurrer and dismissed the candidate's action.

 

17 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Barth v. De Coursey


No. 7529


Supreme Court of Idaho


69 Idaho 469; 207 P.2d 1165; 1949 Ida. LEXIS 260



July 6, 1949 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Peremptory writ of mandate granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff proprietor sought relief in mandamus to compel defendants, a county and its commissioners, to issue him a license for the retail sale of beer, which they had refused.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the proprietor argued that the county's resolution improperly restricted the issuance of county licenses only to establishments located within the incorporated limits of any village or town. In granting relief, the court ruled that Idaho Code § 23-1014 authorized municipalities and counties to license and regulate places of business where beer was sold at retail and that Idaho Code § 23-1015 prohibited such sales without a county license. The court ruled further that Idaho Code § 23-1009 required the county to issue a license if the application conformed to the statutory provisions. The court held that the use of the word, "shall," in § 23-1009 made issuance of the license a duty of the county with such conditions and terms permitted by Idaho Code § 23-1015 and that such terms and conditions adopted by the county were not permitted to be unreasonable, unjust, or unduly oppressive. The court also held that the authority to regulate sales of beer impliedly withheld the power to prohibit sales and that the county's resolution restricting licenses to incorporated areas was inconsistent with and contrary to the state law legalizing the sale of beer.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate.

 

18 of 696 DOCUMENTS


In re Kaufman


No. 7528


Supreme Court of Idaho


69 Idaho 297; 206 P.2d 528; 1949 Ida. LEXIS 238



May 16, 1949 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Applications denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant law school graduates sought summary admission to the Bar of the Supreme Court pursuant to Idaho Code § 3-101, as amended by 1949 Idaho Sess. Laws ch. 73, p. 126, which provided that residents of the state who graduated from the University of Idaho School of Law were entitled to be admitted as attorneys and counselors without being required to pass any examination as to their qualifications with respect to learning and ability.


OVERVIEW: The law school graduates applied for admission to the Bar under an amendment to Idaho Code Ann. § 3-101, which provided that state residents who graduated from the University of Idaho School of Law were entitled to be admitted as attorneys without being required to pass an examination as to their qualifications with respect to learning and ability. The Board of Commissioners of the State Bar opposed the application, claiming that the admission or exclusion of attorneys to practice involved the exercise of a judicial function and that the amendment represented a legislative invasion of judicial powers violative of the constitutional separation of legislative and judicial powers. The court held that its role in admitting or excluding attorneys was not merely ministerial and, while the legislature could impose minimum standards under its police power in order to protect public interests, those standards did not constitute the ultimate qualifications beyond which the court could not go in fixing additional qualifications that it deemed necessary for the proper administration of judicial functions. Accordingly, the statute invaded the judicial power in violation of the constitution.


OUTCOME: The applications were denied.

 

19 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Casselman


Nos. 7502, 7503, 7504, 7505


Supreme Court of Idaho


69 Idaho 237; 205 P.2d 1131; 1949 Ida. LEXIS 231; 24 L.R.R.M. 2056; 16 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P65,126



May 2, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Third Judicial District, Ada County; Charles E. Winstead, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Third Judicial District Court of Ada County (Idaho), which convicted defendants of secondary boycotts.


OVERVIEW: After the settlement and ending of a strike against a telephone company, defendants, employees of an electric company, continued picketing, carrying the same placards, and employees of the telephone company therefore declined to work and its service was restricted. Defendants were convicted of secondary boycotts and appealed their convictions. They argued that the secondary picketing statutes were unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that where claims of behalf of free speech were met with claims on behalf of the authority of the state to impose reasonable regulations for the protection of the community of a while, the duty of the court was plain. Whenever state action was challenged as a denial of liberty, the question always was whether the state violated the essential attributes of that liberty. The court stated that there was nothing in the decree that restrained defendants from informing the public of any labor dispute they might have with the peddlers by any lawful means of dissemination of information. Under those circumstances the court held that the decree did not contravene defendants' free speech rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for secondary boycotting.

 

20 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Garde


No. 7418


Supreme Court of Idaho


69 Idaho 209; 205 P.2d 504; 1949 Ida. LEXIS 227



April 18, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Seventh Judicial District, Canyon County; Thomas E. Buckner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified by vacating sentence for a felony and cause remanded with directions to impose sentence for a misdemeanor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for the sale of liquor from a judgment of the District Court, Seventh Judicial District, Canyon County (Idaho) and from the order denying his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendant had sold a bottle of whiskey to an investigator in the presence of another officer and some friends. On appeal of his conviction, defendant argued that testimony of the prosecution's witnesses established entrapment and that he was entitled to an instruction on that defense. Defendant also argued that at the time of the alleged sale, such conduct constituted a misdemeanor only. The court found the evidence showed that defendant was not entrapped because he was given the opportunity either to make a sale or refuse to do so, and that he chose to sell. Therefore, he was not entitled to instructions on that defense. The court agreed that the statute under which the State charged defendant was not fully operative at the time he was arrested. The court found, however, that defendant was not entitled to be discharged because the essential act charged against him constituted the misdemeanor crime of the unlawful sale of intoxicating liquor; therefore, the court remanded for imposition of a misdemeanor sentence.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment by vacating the sentence for a felony and remanded the case with directions to impose sentence for a misdemeanor.

 

21 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Glanzman


No. 7468


Supreme Court of Idaho


69 Idaho 46; 202 P.2d 407; 1949 Ida. LEXIS 206



January 26, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Third District, Ada County; Charles E. Winstead, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Ada County District Court (Idaho) that convicted him of driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, arguing that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction and that the district court erred in denying his request to charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with driving while under the influence of alcohol. At trial, the arresting officer testified that he stopped defendant because he was driving poorly, that defendant smelled of alcohol, that defendant could not stand without leaning against something, that defendant resisted when officers attempted to look at his driver's license, that defendant he kicked the bars and made a disturbance when placed in a jail cell, and that he believed defendant to have been intoxicated. Defendant was convicted as charged, and he appealed his conviction. In affirming, the court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to justify the verdict. Even though reasonable minds might differ as to the conclusion to be drawn therefrom, it was within the province of the jury to reach the conclusion that defendant was intoxicated. Further, the district court did not err in refusing to give defendant's requested instruction where it placed a burden on the State not authorized by Idaho Code § 48-502. The question was not to what extent defendant was under the influence of liquor but whether he was under the under the influence of alcohol while operating his vehicle.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

O'Connor v. Moscow


No. 7458


Supreme Court of Idaho


69 Idaho 37; 202 P.2d 401; 1949 Ida. LEXIS 205; 9 A.L.R.2d 1031



January 25, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Second Judicial District, Latah County; Albert H. Featherstone, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Moscow challenged a decree of the District Court, Second Judicial District, Latah County (Idaho) that granted the requested relief in the declaratory judgment action in which respondent realty owners, who ran a combined pool hall, card room, and beer parlor, challenged the validity of a zoning ordinance that precluded the owners' successors-in-interest from operating a similar business.


OVERVIEW: The judgment was based on the findings that the ordinance was an arbitrary and unreasonable exercise of the City's police power and deprived them of their property without due process of law. The court affirmed the decree and awarded appellate costs to the owners, concluding that the ordinance violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Idaho Const. art. I, § 13 by depriving the owners of the use of their property by the business's sale and restricting the leasing of the realty. The ordinance's declaration that an ownership change was a new business was an arbitrary and unreasonable exercise of police power by preventing the sale of an existing business that constituted a lawful, although non-conforming, use of the realty. The ordinance did not support the stated goals of facilitating policing and health inspections and preventing loitering and nuisances because the city authorities still needed to continue to police and inspect the businesses in the area to which the ordinance applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree for the owners in the declaratory judgment action against the City that alleged that the ordinance was invalid. The court also awarded appellate fees to the owner.

 

23 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Keenan v. Price


No. 7464


Supreme Court of Idaho


68 Idaho 423; 195 P.2d 662; 1948 Ida. LEXIS 145



June 30, 1948 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Alternative writ quashed and permanent writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original proceeding for a writ of mandate, plaintiff candidate sought an order compelling defendant secretary of state to accept and file his declaration and petitions for candidacy for the office of governor.


OVERVIEW: The candidate challenged an amendment of Idaho Const. art. IV, § 1, which changed the terms of state officers from two to four years, and sought a writ compelling the secretary of state to accept his petitions for candidacy for the office of governor. The candidate argued that the amendment violated art. XX, § 1 because there was a conflict in the amendment as proposed and as ratified by the electorate, in that the words "state auditor" were included in the list of state officers in the question submitted to the voters but were omitted from the amendment after it was approved. The court, which had issued an alternative writ directing the secretary of state to show cause, quashed the alternative writ and denied the candidate's application for a permanent writ. The legislative history of the amendment indicated that the legislature did not amend the resolution as introduced to eliminate the state auditor from art. IV, § 1. The omission of these words was purely a clerical error by the engrossing clerk, and the title and content of the resolution disclosed an intent to retain such officer as a constitutional officer.


OUTCOME: The court denied the candidate's application for a writ of mandate compelling the secretary of state to accept and file his declaration and petitions for candidacy for the office of governor.

Wanke v. Ziebarth Constr. Co.


No. 7411


Supreme Court of Idaho


69 Idaho 64; 202 P.2d 384; 1948 Ida. LEXIS 164



June 24, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On Rehearing February 3, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Industrial Accident Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of an order of the Idaho Industrial Accident Board, which dismissed his application for additional compensation and recoupment of disbursements for medical treatment.


OVERVIEW: The claimant sustained an accidental personal injury in the course of his employment. He was awarded a lump sum by the Board two years later. After nearly two more years passed, the claimant applied for modification of the award. The Board awarded the claimant a specified sum for the increase in his permanent disability and required respondent employer to tender the claimant for an operation. More than six months later, the claimant filed a petition for hearing, claiming that he was permanently and totally unable to work and applying for benefits due of change in condition and error in the Board's previous modification in not awarding such benefits previously. The Board held that additional compensation was barred by Idaho Code § 43-1407. On appeal, the court found that § 43-1407 did not violate any of the claimant's constitutional rights as any defects or imperfections relative to § 43-1407 were cured by its re-enactment. The claimant's current petition could not be considered as a continuing application for modification of award; thus, it was not timely brought within the four-year time limit provided by § 43-1407.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's order.

 

25 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Nielson v. Lindstrom


No. 7403


Supreme Court of Idaho


68 Idaho 226; 191 P.2d 1009; 1948 Ida. LEXIS 122



April 1, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Second Judicial District; Clearwater County; A. L. Morgan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to 1947 Idaho Sess. Laws 237, part of the Public Assistance Law, appellant State of Idaho brought suit against respondent executor to recover amounts paid in old-age assistance to the decedent during his lifetime. The District Court, Second Judicial District, Clearwater County (Idaho) sustained the executor's demurrer to the complaint and dismissed the action. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The executor argued that granting assistance to the decedent was in effect a loan, thereby violating Idaho Const. art. VIII, § 2 that stated the credit of the State was not to be given or loaned to any person. The court stated that the grant was unconditional as far as a recipient was concerned. It created no obligation for him to repay public assistance to which he was lawfully entitled. The granting of aid by a state to its needy aged was a well-recognized obligation; it followed that the granting of such aid was not within constitutional inhibitions unless the recovery features of the statute made the law subject to such inhibitions. The liability of the State was not increased by the recovery provision. The State received the benefit of the recovery provisions and should be classified as a recipient of credit rather than as a giver thereof. Furthermore, the State could impose conditions upon the exercise of the right to dispose of one's property after death. Next, the recovery provision was not local or special legislation in violation of Idaho Const. art. III, § 19. The provision operated upon all the aged needy and their estates in like situations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision. It ordered the trial court to overrule the executor's demurrer to the complaint.

Mc Kinney v. State


Docket No. 22750, 1999 Opinion No. 126


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


133 Idaho 695; 992 P.2d 144; 1999 Ida. LEXIS 131



December 13, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 4, 2000.
Writ of certiorari denied McKinney v. Idaho, 530 U.S. 1208, 120 S. Ct. 2207, 147 L. Ed. 2d 240, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3724 (May 30, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonneville County. Hon. James C. Herndon, District Judge.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of October 4, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Ida. LEXIS 122.
McKinney v. State, 1999 Ida. LEXIS 122 (Idaho, Oct. 4, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed the order of the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonneville County, dismissing his second amended petition for post-conviction relief in a capital case.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and related offenses and was sentenced to death. His first petition for post-conviction relief was denied. The district court dismissed defendant's second petition for post-conviction relief since all the facts presented reasonably should have been known by the time he filed his first petition. On appeal, the court found the district court properly dismissed defendant's claim predicated on judicial delay in carrying out the death sentence. The limitations of Idaho Code § 19-2719 applied to defendant's second petition; thus, defendant waived all claims for relief that reasonably should have been known when he filed his first petition. Ineffective assistance of counsel in defendant's first post-conviction proceeding did not excuse his failure to raise issues that should reasonably have been known. The district court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a default judgment. The court affirmed the dismissal.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing defendant's petition for post-conviction relief affirmed because defendant waived all claims for relief that reasonably should have been known when he filed his first petition.

State v. Hairston


Docket No. 23414/24225, 1999 Opinion No. 94


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


133 Idaho 496; 988 P.2d 1170; 1999 Ida. LEXIS 100



August 24, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied May 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3498. Released for Publication November 17, 1999.
Writ of certiorari denied Hairston v. Idaho, 529 U.S. 1134, 120 S. Ct. 2014, 146 L. Ed. 2d 963, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3498 (2000)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Motion granted by Hairston v. State, 2007 Ida. LEXIS 78 (Idaho, Mar. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Bannock County. Honorable Peter D. McDermott, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of conviction and capital punishment imposed for first degree murder, affirmed. Order denying post-conviction relief, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed from a death sentence imposed by the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Bannock County following his conviction for murder. Defendant also appealed denial of his application for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant appealed from a death sentence following his conviction for murder and also challenged denial of his application for post-conviction relief. Defendant argued the trial court erred, among a host of other things, in admitting evidence of defendant's uncharged prior bad act and for imposing death when the sentence was not proportionate or just and the death penalty structure was unconstitutional. The court found Idaho R. Evid. 404(b) allowed admission of the evidence because it was relevant to impeachment and defendant opened the door to admission of the evidence by testifying he had never fired the murder weapon. Also, the court found that invalidation of one or more aggravating circumstances did not implicate proportionality because the lower court had determined that any one of the aggravating circumstance, standing alone, outweighed all the mitigating circumstances, thus the death sentence was justified. Defendant's presented evidence failed to support his unconstitutionality argument.


OUTCOME: Death sentence and denial of post-conviction relief affirmed; the court found the lower court did not abuse its discretion in admitting into evidence defendant's uncharged prior bad acts, nor did they err in imposing death where mitigation was considered in relation to each aggravating circumstance leading to the death penalty.

Levin v. Idaho State Bd. of Med.


Docket No. 24680, 1999 Opinion No. 93


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


133 Idaho 413; 987 P.2d 1028; 1999 Ida. LEXIS 102



August 24, 1999, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Joel D. Horton, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order suspending license to practice medicine affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensed osteopathic physician appealed the decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, affirming a disciplinary order issued by respondent Board of Professional Discipline of the Idaho State Board of Medicine against appellant.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Board of Professional Discipline of the Idaho State Board of Medicine (Board) issued a disciplinary order against appellant licensed physician. Appellant contended that the Board's order was not supported by substantial evidence, that administrative regulations IDAPA 22.01.01.101.03.d and IDAPA 22.01.01.101.04.d, adopted by the Board, were unconstitutional, and that he was subjected to selective enforcement by the Board. The court found the record contained substantial evidence to support the Board's factual findings, and no basis to conclude that appellant was treated differently from any other licensed physician, and that regulation IDAPA 22.01.01.101.04 was constitutional. However, the court held that IDAPA 22.01.01101.03.d, designating sexual contact, misconduct, exploitation or intercourse as a measure to gauge the provision of health care, was not within the scope of Idaho Code § 54-1814(7), and therefore was in excess of the authority of the Board to promulgate.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed in part, finding substantial evidence of sexual relations between appellant and patient, and vacated in part, holding respondent Idaho State Board of Medicine exceeded its authority by adopting a regulation designating "sexual contact, misconduct, exploitation or intercourse" as a measure to gauge the provision of health care.

Lamar Corp. v. City of Twin Falls


Docket No. 24304, 1999 Opinion No. 68


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


133 Idaho 36; 981 P.2d 1146; 1999 Ida. LEXIS 72



June 11, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 16, 1999. As Corrected October 4, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. Daniel B. Meehl, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city council and city, appealed a judgment from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County, that reversed a zoning decision by defendant city council, and denied its request to delete certain items from the transcript for the record on appeal. Plaintiff cross-appealed in order to determine whether sufficient evidence supported defendant city's action, and it requested attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the order denying defendant city's request to delete some documents from the record for the appeal because it served judicial economy and was mandated by Idaho App. R. 25(c) and 28(b). The court reversed the judgment that overturned defendant city council's denial of a special use permit. The court found the requirement of Idaho Code § 10-9-2(M)(4)(c) was not an unconstitutional prior restraint on commercial free speech because it had sufficiently objective and definite standards to guide zoning officials to make zoning decisions. The court affirmed the finding that substantial evidence supported defendant city council's denial of a special use permit. Photographs and sketches were introduced of the area with the proposed billboard. The record showed that city council members viewed the photographs supplied and applied their reasoned judgment when they denied the permit. The court concluded that because defendant city council denied the special use permit, plaintiff was not the prevailing party and was not entitled to attorney fees under Idaho Code § 12-117. Defendants were not entitled to attorney fees because plaintiff presented legitimate issues on appeal.


OUTCOME: The order overturning the denial of a special use permit was reversed because the city code's requirements were not an unconstitutional prior restraint on commercial free speech. The court affirmed the finding that substantial evidence supported the city counsel's denial of a special use permit because the record showed that photographs were viewed and reasoned judgment applied before the permit was denied.

Idaho State Ins. Fund v. Van Tine


Docket No. 24723, 1999 Opinion No. 65


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


132 Idaho 902; 980 P.2d 566; 1999 Ida. LEXIS 67



June 9, 1999, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. D. Duff McKee, District Judge.

Appeal from dismissal of counterclaim seeking damages against worker's compensation surety arising out of surety's subrogation claim.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which dismissed his counterclaim seeking damages against respondent, a worker's compensation surety, for breach of the duty of good faith and fair dealing arising out of respondent's subrogation claim.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was injured during the course of his employment when the vehicle he was driving was struck by a semi-truck. Appellant submitted a workers' compensation claim to his employer's workers' compensation surety, respondent. Appellant reached a settlement with the semi-truck's driver. Respondent claimed subrogation and filed a complaint for declaratory judgment. Appellant filed a counterclaim alleging that respondent waived the subrogation claim, it would be unconstitutional for respondent to maintain a claim for subrogation, and that respondent breached its duty of good faith and fair dealing. The lower court granted both parties' summary judgment motions. Appellant sought review of the dismissal of his counterclaim. The court ruled the lower court properly dismissed appellant's counterclaim. The lower court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to address appellant's count of alleging breach of the duty of good faith and fair dealing. The court found that appellant's equal protection rights had not been violated. The court affirmed the lower court's denial of appellant's request for discretionary costs and attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing appellant's counterclaim because the lower court lacked jurisdiction to hear appellant's claim relating to respondent's unreasonableness in failing to compensate, appellant failed to show that his equal protection rights had been violated, lower court had not abused its discretion in denying his request for attorney fees, and lower court properly dismissed his breach of the duty of good faith claim.

Aberdeen-Springfield Canal Co. v. Peiper


Docket No. 23912


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


133 Idaho 82; 982 P.2d 917; 1999 Ida. LEXIS 57



May 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Filed June 15, 1999. Petition for Rehearing Denied August 18, 1999. Released for Publication August 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bingham County. Hon. James C. Herndon, District Judge; appeal from the Snake River Basin Adjudication Court of the Fifth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. Daniel C. Hurlbutt, District Judge.

Appeal from motion granting summary judgment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners, sued by plaintiff water supplier for failing to pay irrigation maintenance costs, appealed the rulings of the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District, Bingham County, Idaho, and of the Snake River Basin Adjudication Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Twin Falls County, Idaho, favoring plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff water supplier sued defendant landowners, seeking foreclosure on liens levied due to defendants' failure to pay irrigation maintain costs. Defendants counterclaimed on grounds of forfeiture, statutory unconstitutionality, civil rights violations, and unjust enrichment. The cases were adjudicated in stages before different trial courts because of jurisdictional concerns. Those courts found in favor of plaintiff and against defendants. On appeal, those rulings were affirmed. The court held the assessment of irrigation maintain costs on the subject properties was proper given the benefit inuring to those properties, including those properties not requiring irrigation systems, in water-scarce areas. In addition, since the statutes in question did not violate either substantive or procedural due process, plaintiffs lacked a viable civil rights complaint. Finally, the court found no error in the rejection of defendants' forfeiture-of-water-rights claim because such a claim was disfavored. The court also found that defendants' failure-to-prosecute counterclaim was properly denied due to lack of prejudice.


OUTCOME: Trial courts' orders favoring plaintiff were affirmed. The court found that plaintiff possessed the right to impose irrigation maintenance costs on defendants even though defendants were not using plaintiff's water because of the benefit to defendants from increase in their neighbors' property values as a result of the water use. The court found that defendants' counterclaims lacked merit.

Idaho Watersheds Project v. State Bd. of Land Comm'Rs


Docket No. 24367, 1999 Opinion No. 39


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


133 Idaho 64; 982 P.2d 367; 1999 Ida. LEXIS 39



April 2, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. D. Duff McKee, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from judgment affirming decisions of the State Board of Land Commissioners. Reversed and remanded to the Land Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant organization challenged a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which upheld a decision of appellee board rejecting appellant as a qualified bidder and disqualifying appellant from bidding on expiring state endowment land leases.


OVERVIEW: Appellant organization submitted 24 conflict grazing lease applications for expiring state endowment land leases. Appellee board decided that appellant was a qualified applicant for three lease auctions, but later disqualified appellant as the high bidder in two of them. After receiving no lease awards, appellant filed suit against appellee, arguing that Idaho Code § 58-310B was unconstitutional and applied by appellee in an arbitrary and discriminatory manner. Appellant then challenged a trial court ruling which upheld appellee's decision. The appeals court reversed and remanded the matter to appellee for new auctions of the leases on which appellant was not allowed to bid. The court ruled that the statute violated Idaho Const. art. IX, § 8, because it removed much of appellee's broad discretion by impermissibly directing appellee to focus on the schools, the state, and the Idaho livestock industry in assessing lease applications, all to the detriment of other potential bidders who might provide "maximum long term financial return" to the schools, but not to the state and the Idaho livestock industry.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the matter to appellee board for new auctions of the leases on which appellant was not allowed to bid. The court ruled that state statute violated the Idaho Constitution because it removed much of appellee's broad discretion by directing the focus to schools, the state, and the Idaho livestock industry, instead of only the "maximum long term financial return" to the schools, as mandated by the Idaho Constitution.

Idaho Watersheds Project v. State Bd. of Land Comm'Ns (in Re Verified Petition for Writ of Prohibition)


Docket No. 25125, 1999 Opinion No. 40


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


133 Idaho 55; 982 P.2d 358; 1999 Ida. LEXIS 40



April 2, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied August 3, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ida. LEXIS 91. Released for Publication August 3, 1999.



DISPOSITION: Verified Petition for Writ of Prohibition challenging procedures by which House Joint Resolution No. 6 (H.J.R. 6), an amendment to Article 9, § 4 and § 8 of the Idaho Constitution, was presented to the electorate. Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought a writ of prohibition challenging the constitutionality of a congressional resolution, approved by the electorate, amending Idaho Const. art. 9, §§ 4 and 8.


OVERVIEW: A house joint resolution proposing to amend Idaho Const. art. 9, §§ 4 and 8, was adopted by the state legislation and was approved by the electorate. Petitioners sought a writ of prohibition barring the implementation of the resolution, claiming that the issue was illegally presented to the voters. On review, the state supreme court concluded that because the alleged procedural defects were not misleading, the petitioners' statutory and constitutional challenges to the procedures were time barred where they were not presented before the election. However, in granting the requested relief, the court concluded that because the proposed amendments to the two sections did not in any way depend upon one another, they were incongruous and essentially unrelated. Consequently, they should have been submitted separately to the voters, and the amendments proposed by the single resolution violated the single subject rule of Idaho Const. art. 20, § 2, which required that if two or more amendments were proposed, they must be submitted in such a manner that the voters could vote for or against each proposed amendment separately.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of prohibition was granted, for the house joint resolution was improperly submitted to the electorate in violation of the single subject rule of Idaho Const. art. 20, § 2, where it presented essentially unrelated issues in a single resolution for voter consideration.

36 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kuzmichev


Docket No. 23890, 1999 Opinion No. 36


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


132 Idaho 536; 976 P.2d 462; 1999 Ida. LEXIS 36



April 2, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Alan Schwartzman, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction and sentence for murder in the second degree entered in the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District (Idaho) convicting him of murder in the second degree, contending that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the testimony of an informant and in denying his motion to suppress his statements to police.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's wife was murdered, defendant presented himself to police to inquire whether he was a suspect and whether he could leave the country to visit family. Following an interview with police, defendant was arrested for his wife's murder. He appealed his second-degree murder conviction, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress informant testimony and his statements to police. In affirming, the appellate court concluded that the informant's testimony was properly admitted, as the informant did not unconstitutionally interrogate defendant to obtain a confession. The informant had no relevant contact with the police before defendant made his admissions; he was thus not acting as a police agent, and his testimony was not suppressible. Further, the appellate court rejected defendant's argument that his statements to police should have been suppressed where he was not given his Miranda rights. It was unnecessary for the police to give Miranda rights where defendant was not in police custody but voluntarily presented himself for an interview; the non-custodial statements were voluntarily made and were admissible.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of second-degree murder was affirmed, as the informant's testimony regarding defendant's admissions was properly admitted where the informant was not acting as an agent of the police. Further, defendant's admissions to police were properly admitted where they were voluntarily made during a non-custodial interview.

Ag Air v. Idaho State Tax Comm'n


Docket No. 24204, 1999 Opinion No. 3


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


132 Idaho 345; 972 P.2d 313; 1999 Ida. LEXIS 3



February 4, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Minidoka County. Hon. J. William Hart, District Judge. Appeal from an order of the district court granting summary judgement in favor of the Tax Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged a judgment of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Minidoka County (Idaho), which granted appellee agency's motion for summary judgment in appellant's case alleging that Idaho Code § 63-3622D violated appellant's equal protection rights guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. XIV regarding payment of use tax.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation received notices of deficiency determinations (NODs) from appellee agency for use taxes. Appellant timely protested the NODs and, following the hearing, the assessed tax penalty was upheld and appellant filed a petition for judicial review. Appellant contended that Idaho Code § 63-3622D discriminated against it by requiring a use tax. Appellee moved to dismiss because appellant failed to comply with Idaho Code § 63-3049(b) and make a 20 percent deposit to appellee within 91 days of receiving notice of appellee's decision. The trial court granted appellee's motion, however, appellant was permitted to amend its petition and request a declaratory judgment regarding the statute's unconstitutionality. Appellee was granted summary judgment and appellant challenged the decision. The court affirmed the trial court's decision and reasoned that because appellant's complaint dealt with appellee's use tax decision, allowing appellant to amend its petition to seek a declaratory judgment, without requiring compliance with Idaho Code § 63-3049 (b), would not be fair. Moreover, the trial court lacked the authority to permit appellant's amendment of its petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, granting appellee agency's motion for summary judgment in appellant's equal protection violation action, was affirmed. The court reasoned that the trial court lacked the authority to permit appellant to amend its petition to seek declaratory relief because appellant failed to comply with the statutory requirements in order to seek judicial review of appellee agency's use tax determination.
