Idaho Schs. for Equal Educ. Opportunity v. State


Docket No. 24445, 1998 Opinion No. 131


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


132 Idaho 559; 976 P.2d 913; 1998 Ida. LEXIS 147



December 30, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Filed January 6, 1999. Petition for Rehearing Denied May 17, 1999. Released for Publication May 17, 1999. As Corrected July 1, 1999.
Rehearing denied by, 05/17/1999
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Idaho Schs. for Equal Educ. Opportunity v. State, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 166 (Idaho, Aug. 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Daniel T. Eismann, District Judge.
Idaho Sch. for Equal Educ. Opportunity v. Idaho State Bd. of Educ., 128 Idaho 276, 912 P.2d 644, 1996 Ida. LEXIS 24 (Idaho, 1996)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from summary judgment dismissing claims. Affirmed, in part; vacated, in part, and remanded. Cross-appeal from denial of filing third-party complaint and from denial of dismissal. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs student, parent, and school district appealed from summary judgment by the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, dismissing claims that the school funding system violated Idaho Const. art. IX, § 1. Defendant, State of Idaho, cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court erred in granting summary judgment on a claim alleging that the legislature had to provide a means for school districts to fund facilities that provided a safe environment conducive to learning. A safe environment conducive to learning was inherently a part of the thorough system of public, free common schools that Idaho Const. art. IX, § 1 required the legislature to establish and maintain. The legislature's constitutional obligation could not be read to allow unsafe schools, unconducive to learning. The state did not present evidence showing the existing school facilities provided a safe environment, conducive to learning. The State did not eliminate genuine issues of material fact. Plaintiffs' claims that the education funding scheme was unconstitutionally unequal failed because Idaho Const. art. IX, § 1 did not apply to funding. The trial court did not abuse discretion in not allowing a State third-party complaint against superintendents of the school districts that were plaintiffs. The trial court did not err in denying a State request that the trial court dismiss individual plaintiffs whose school districts were unnamed as plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was vacated in part, affirmed in part, and the case was remanded.

 

39 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cobb


Supreme Court No. 23898, Supreme Court No. 23994, 1998 Opinion No. 125


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


132 Idaho 195; 969 P.2d 244; 1998 Ida. LEXIS 142



December 2, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 24, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Daniel T. Eismann, District Judge; Hon. E. Kay Hamilton, Magistrate, in case no. 23898. Hon. Alan Schwartzman, District Judge; Hon. Carolyn Minder, Magistrate, in case no. 23994.



DISPOSITION: Magistrate decisions holding Boise City's municipal ordinance defining disorderly conduct unconstitutional, reversed. Cases remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Ada County (Idaho), which held that the city ordinance against disorderly conduct, under which defendants were cited, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged the trial court judgment which held the disorderly conduct ordinance, under which defendants were cited, to be constitutional. They claimed that the ordinance was vague on its face because it provided no clear guidelines to persons subject to it and to those who must enforce it in a fair and nondiscriminatory manner. They argued that using the word "may" rather than a word such as "shall," which would denote a mandatory inclusion of the five examples as criminal acts, rendered the ordinance uncertain and incapable of fair and nondiscriminatory enforcement. The state urged the court to apply a "vague as applied" analysis by determining that the conduct with which defendants were charged was clearly conduct that was proscribed by the ordinance. The court affirmed the district court and found the ordinance to be constitutional. The list of examples in the disorderly conduct ordinance provided guidelines for citizens seeking to conform their conduct to the ordinance and for the police to enforce the ordinance in a fair and unbiased manner. Use of the word "may" demonstrated that a police officer, exercising discretion, may find other acts to violate the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment that held the disorderly conduct ordinance to be constitutional and remanded to the magistrate. The ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague because the ordinance listed several acts which would constitute disorderly conduct, thereby providing guidelines for citizens seeking to conform their conduct to the ordinance and for the police to enforce the ordinance in a fair and unbiased manner.

 

40 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Estes v. Barry


Docket No. 23797, 1998 Opinion No. 114


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


132 Idaho 82; 967 P.2d 284; 1998 Ida. LEXIS 128



October 26, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Daniel T. Eismann, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the respondents is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District (Idaho) granting summary judgment to defendants in a breach of contract action arising out of a real estate transaction. Plaintiff argued the court erred in ruling that the parol evidence rule and the doctrine of merger precluded her breach of contract claim.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff entered into a real estate purchase agreement with defendants, under which she agreed to assume defendants' FHA loan. The agreement provided that defendants would convey title free of all liens and encumbrances except for the loan. After the purchase was competed, plaintiff discovered that the property was subject to a recapture obligation that accrued during defendants' period of ownership. When defendants refused to compensate plaintiff for the amount of the obligation, she filed suit for breach of contract and breach of the covenant of good faith and fair dealing. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. On review, plaintiff argued the trial court erred in ruling that the parol evidence rule and the doctrine of merger precluded her breach of contract claim. The appeals court affirmed. The court reasoned that the express terms of the warranty deed indicated that the conveyance was subject to the loan and the recapture obligation. Because an agreement that plaintiff would only assume the loan was inconsistent with the agreement in the deed, the doctrine of merger barred the claim.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court judgment granting summary judgment to defendants in a breach of contract action arising out of a real estate transaction because the doctrine of merger precluded recovery by plaintiff. The court ruled that because the terms of the warranty deed differed from the purchase agreement, the words of the deed determined the rights of the parties.

 

41 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wood


Docket No. 21057/22375, 1998 Opinion No. 107


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


132 Idaho 88; 967 P.2d 702; 1998 Ida. LEXIS 121



October 9, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied May 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 3319.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bannock County. Hon. Lynn B. Winmill, District Judge.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of June 19, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Ida. LEXIS 76.



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the district court imposing the death penalty and denying post-conviction relief are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Sixth Judicial District, Bannock County (Idaho), dismissing his petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant claimed his murder conviction was reversible because, inter alia, the trial court improperly failed to disqualify itself and because he received ineffective assistance of trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to murder. The death sentence was imposed. Defendant's post-conviction relief petition was denied. Defendant appealed, claiming the trial court improperly failed to disqualify itself and that his counsel was ineffective. The appellate court vacated the trial court's finding of a third aggravating factor and affirmed. Although the judge was affiliated with the victims through his church, this alone was not a reasonable basis for disqualification. Defense counsel's decision not to move to disqualify the judge based on the belief that the judge be less inclined to impose the death penalty was a rational tactical decision that could not second-guessed on review. Further, because defendant failed to prove that but for counsel's various errors, the result of the proceedings would have been different, no ineffectiveness was shown. However, where counsel did not know whether a psychiatric report was favorable or unfavorable, his failure to object to its admission constituted ineffective assistance. Thus, an aggravating factor based on the report was vacated. Remand was unnecessary because the omission of this factor would not alter the sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment of sentence imposing the death penalty against defendant. Although the judge was affiliated with people involved in the case through his church, this alone was insufficient to justify disqualification. Although defense counsel allegedly committed some errors, because the result would not have been different without the errors, defendant's murder conviction and death sentence were upheld.

 

42 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Creech


Docket No. 22006/23482, 1998 Opinion No. 97.


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


132 Idaho 1; 966 P.2d 1; 1998 Ida. LEXIS 110



August 19, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied October 23, 1998; Released for Publication October 23, 1998. Certiorari Denied June 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 3720.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Robert G. Newhouse, District Judge. Appeal from a death sentence imposed upon entry of guilty plea to first degree murder, and appeal from a denial of petition for post-conviction relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a death sentence imposed upon his guilty plea to first degree murder and the denial of petition for post-conviction relief from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, arguing, inter alia, that the district court committed reversible error by significantly changing its findings in support of the death sentence in violation of the Double Jeopardy Clause of the Fifth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: On remand of the case to allow defendant to present mitigating evidence, which he was not allowed to do at a sentencing hearing, the district court changed a mitigating factor to an aggravating factor upon resentencing. On appeal, the court held that the district court was not barred by the Double Jeopardy Clause from reconsidering existing information, changing mitigating factors, and weighing evidence differently at a resentencing hearing. The court explained that the district court consistently imposed the death penalty at both the defendant's original sentencing and resentencing hearings. The only difference at the resentencing was that after the court received additional information from an updated presentence report, which was compiled at defendant's request, it reinterpreted its finding with respect to the circumstances surrounding the attack of the victim. Thus, it was not error for the district court to change its finding where the district court considered all of the evidence presented and simply reinterpreted its earlier mitigation finding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction, the imposition of the death sentence and the denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief. The court denied the state's request for attorney fees and costs on the post-conviction appeal.

Tupper v. State Farm Ins.


Docket No. 23623, 1998 Opinion No. 89


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


131 Idaho 724; 963 P.2d 1161; 1998 Ida. LEXIS 101



August 5, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho. Appeal from an Industrial Commission decision denying worker's compensation benefits.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the order from the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho, which denied her worker's compensation benefits in her action against respondent employer.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked as a telephone receptionist for an insurance company. In October 1994, she went to her doctor and complained that she was having intermittent pain in her neck, and that she'd had the pain for two years. The doctor recommended physical therapy. The next day she filed with her employer a Notice of Injury and Claim for Benefits, noting that she had pain in her neck and shoulders. The next month she reported to her doctor that she was better because she was wearing a headset but that the physical therapy was not working. She missed no time from work due to her ailment. In November 1995, she filed an unsuccessful worker's compensation complaint with the commission seeking medical benefits for pain to her left shoulder and upper back. On appeal, the court affirmed, agreeing with the commission's finding that because the employee's impairment did not actually and totally incapacitate her from performing her employment duties, she was not disabled; therefore, under Idaho Code §§ 72-102(21) (Supp. 1998) and 72-437, she was not entitled to benefits for an occupational disease. The court also found the statutes constitutional under the rational basis test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's order denying worker's compensation benefits to the employee.

 

44 of 696 DOCUMENTS



State v. Merwin


Docket No. 23467, 1998 Opinion No. 77


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


131 Idaho 642; 962 P.2d 1026; 1998 Ida. LEXIS 88



July 1, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 23, 1998. Released for Publication July 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. James F. Judd, District Judge. Appeal from conviction and sentence.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, which convicted him of felony injury to a child after his child died from head injuries.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it denied his motion for acquittal and motion in limine, and when it allowed the state's expert to testify regarding the possible causes of the child's head injury. The court stated that on review of a denial of a motion for acquittal the court must look at all facts and inferences and determine whether there was substantial evidence to support the conviction. The court noted that the state's expert stated that it was unlikely that the child's injuries occurred from an earlier unobserved fall because the child would have exhibited some sign of injury. The court held that the evidence supported the jury's verdict because reasonable minds could have concluded that defendant's hypothesis of an earlier injury was unreasonable thus defendant's motion of acquittal was properly denied. The court stated that defendant's motion in limine was properly denied because the trial court refused to allow the state's experts to testify as to whether the injuries could have been accidental. The court found that the reports used by the state's experts possessed sufficient indicia of reliability under Idaho R. Evid. 702 and were properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted the defendant of felony injury to a child.

Phinney v. Shoshone Med. Ctr.


Docket No. 23659, 1998 Opinion No. 72


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


131 Idaho 529; 960 P.2d 1258; 1998 Ida. LEXIS 84



June 30, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 22, 1998. As Corrected November 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Industrial Commission's order with respect to the claimant's motion for determination of the Industrial Special Indemnity Fund's benefit assessment. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee appealed the judgment of the Idaho Industrial Commission in a workers' compensation claim, which awarded benefits for the employee's total permanent disability.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued, inter alia, that the Commission erred in calculating her benefits, because Idaho Code §§ 72-408 and 72-409 violated equal protection, because they treated workers earning a lower rate of pay differently than workers earning a higher rate of pay. The supreme court disagreed. Because the amount of the employee's financial loss was dependent upon the employee's wages prior to her injury, it was reasonable for the legislature to consider the employee's average weekly wage in determining benefits under Idaho Code §§ 72-408 and 72-409. The difference in benefits between workers earning higher rates of pay and workers earning lower rates of pay was rationally related to the legislature's legitimate goal of compensating injured workers in proportion to their financial loss. Thus, Idaho Code §§ 72-408 and 72-409 did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Meisner v. Potlatch Corp.


Docket No. 22974, 1998 Opinion No. 17


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


131 Idaho 258; 954 P.2d 676; 1998 Ida. LEXIS 23



February 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 12, 1998. Released for Publication March 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Clearwater County. Hon. George Reinhardt, III, District Judge.

Appeal from the district court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the defendants.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, in her individual capacity and as the administrator of the deceased employee's estate, appealed a judgment from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho that granted defendant employer summary judgment on the representative's negligence and wrongful death claims arising from the decedent's death. The district court dismissed the claims for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was killed when, while working for the employer, stacks of wood fell on him. In the administrator's suit for negligence and wrongful death, the district court dismissed the claims for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The district court also rejected the administrator's claims that worker's compensation statutes, which denied certain benefits to certain classes of children of deceased worker's, were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court ruled that the district court properly concluded that the worker's compensation statutes, Idaho Code §§ 72-201 and 72-221, were the exclusive remedy for claims for injuries arising out of and sustained during the course of employment. The administrator's wrongful death and negligence claims thus were properly dismissed. The court next rejected the administrator's claim that Idaho Code §72-413, which provided dependent, but not adult independent, children of a deceased worker a benefit, violated the equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions. The court ruled that the different treatment of classes of children was rationally related to the state's goal of providing monetary relief to dependent children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that granted the employer summary judgment on the administrator's wrongful death and negligence claims. The court upheld as constitutional the state's worker's compensation statutes that denied certain benefits to adult children, or children generally, of a deceased worker.

State v. Hagerman Water Right Owners (in Re Srba Case No. 39576)


DOCKET NO. 23071, 1997 Opinion No. 118


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


130 Idaho 718; 947 P.2d 391; 1997 Ida. LEXIS 126



September 10, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 29, 1998. Released for Publication October 2, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. Daniel C. Hurlbutt, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court's award of attorney fees against the State pursuant to the private attorney general doctrine is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state appealed the order of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County, which granted respondent environmental organization attorney fees pursuant to the private attorney general doctrine.


OVERVIEW: The attorney fees awarded to the environmental organization by the trial court was based on the trial judge's conclusion that the state's activities in administrative proceedings held to determine water rights in a river basin were activities permitting compensation under the private attorney general doctrine. The state disagreed and appealed. On appeal, the court reversed. It held that the totality of the circumstances did not permit the granting of attorney fees to the environmental organization, inasmuch as the organization neither secured relief for the public nor was an organization formed to protect the public's interests. As both of those matters were essential prerequisites to the awarding of attorney fees, their absence was fatal to the environmental organization's claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment below, which entered an award for attorney fees to the environmental organization based on the private attorney general doctrine, was reversed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant facility owners sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which affirmed the findings of fact and conclusions of law issued by respondent Ada County Board of County Commissioners (board) subsequent to a remand from the court. The board had denied county indigency assistance to three of the residential care facility's residents.


OVERVIEW: Three of the residential care facility's residents applied for county indigency assistance. The district court affirmed the board's denial of assistance to the residents. The court vacated the board's order and remanded the matter to the board. Upon remand, the board issued findings regarding the indigency status of the residents and once again denied county assistance to them. The facility owners appealed the board's decision to the district court. The district court affirmed the board's decision. The court affirmed the district court's decision. The court held in part that (1) the board's finding that the residents were not indigent under Idaho Code § 31-3502 was supported by substantial and competent evidence, as the income and assets available to the residents met the residential care facility's reasonable costs of care; and that (2) although the board determined that the residents were "sick" persons under § 31-3502(6), Idaho counties were not obligated to "care for and maintain" sick persons in need of assistance pursuant to § 31-3503.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's affirmance of the board's denial of indigency assistance to three of the residential care facility's residents.

Dep't of Fin. v. Res. Serv. Co.


Docket No. 22211, 1997 Opinion No. 109


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


130 Idaho 877; 950 P.2d 249; 1997 Ida. LEXIS 114



September 2, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 5, 1998. Released for Publication February 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Elmore County. Hon. Robert M. Rowett, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court's decision on summary judgment that Resource Services Company's services are securities is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a company and its owner, sought review of an order of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Elmore County, which, based upon a determination that the company was marketing a security in violation of various provisions of the Idaho Securities Act, Idaho Code §§ 30-1401 to 30-1458, granted summary judgment in favor of respondent Idaho Department of Finance.


OVERVIEW: The company solicited a fee from customers to enter their names in a Bureau of Land Management lottery for gas and oil leases. A portion of the payment was profit to the company for preparing and filing customer applications in the lottery, and a portion was combined with like payments from 19 other customers and applied to the payment of a $ 75 filing fee and advance lease payment on government-owned lands. The program was marketed as having the potential for obtaining valuable oil and gas reserves. The district court determined that the company was marketing an "investment contract" constituting a security and granted summary judgment to the department on various claims.The company appealed, and the owner appealed the court's determination that he was personally liable, pursuant to Idaho Code § 30-1442(3), for any violations of the act by the company. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the economic realities of the transaction did not amount to investing, as customers simply paid a fee to the company for its service of entering their names in a lottery. The court further held that the district court erred in determining that the company was marketing a security.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's decisions, which held that the company violated the Idaho Securities Act and extended personal liability for those violations to the owner. The court awarded costs to the company but no attorney's fees.

Writ of certiorari denied Porter v. Idaho, 523 U.S. 1126, 140 L. Ed. 2d 951, 118 S. Ct. 1813, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 3236 (1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Porter v. State, 136 Idaho 257, 32 P.3d 151, 2001 Ida. LEXIS 98 (Idaho, 2001)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Porter v. State, 80 P.3d 1021, 2003 Ida. LEXIS 191 (Idaho, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Porter v. State, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 185 (Idaho, Oct. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Lewis County. Hon. George R. Reinhardt III, District Judge.

Appeal from first-degree murder conviction and sentence of death.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of February 4, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 Ida. LEXIS 25.
State v. Porter, 1997 Ida. LEXIS 25 (Idaho, Feb. 4, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On direct appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District (Idaho), defendant challenged his conviction for first-degree murder for violently beating a woman who previously had been his girlfriend, the denial of his post-conviction petition, and the imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder for violently beating his former girlfriend to death. On direct appeal from the trial court, defendant contended that it was error to deny him a second court-appointed attorney. The court determined from the record that the district court acted within its permitted discretion in denying the request for a second attorney and in finding that there was no right to a second attorney in a capital case. Defendant's allegation that the state prejudiced his case by allowing the cremation of the victim's body was found to be a meritless claim by the court on appeal because there was no indication that defendant was prejudiced by that alleged destruction of evidence. The court also affirmed the death penalty sentence because the evidence in the record supported it. Accordingly, the court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and his death sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder for the beating death of his former girlfriend, the denial of his post-conviction petition, and the imposition of the death penalty because the decisions of the trial court were supported by the evidence and no error was found.

Simpson v. Cenarrusa (in Re Writ of Prohibition & Declaratory Judgment)


Docket No. 23526, 1997 Opinion No. 99


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


130 Idaho 609; 944 P.2d 1372; 1997 Ida. LEXIS 102



August 7, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Order and Opinion granting Petition for Writ of Prohibition in part.



DISPOSITION: Because of the mixed result, we award no costs. We find no basis to award petitioners attorney fees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner legislators filed an action for declaratory judgment concerning the constitutionality of a proposition regarding term limits, and sought a writ of prohibition against respondent Secretary of State of the State of Idaho (secretary) barring the implementation of the proposition.


OVERVIEW: The proposal instructed the state's legislators to use their powers to pass an amendment imposing term limits on legislators and included a pledge for non-incumbent candidates to support the measure. The secretary was given the responsibility to review the legislators' records and identify them in the legend of reelection ballots if they did not support the measure. The proposition was challenged as unconstitutional. The court held that the ballot legend and pledge portions of the proposition were unconstitutional and issued a writ of prohibition as to them. The ballot legend was an unconstitutional state-imposed consequence for speech and debate in the legislature. The pledge was an attempt by the state to govern political speech without showing any flagrant abuse of the right by compelling candidates to take a stance on the proposed amendment. The instructions were held not to be an unconstitutional attempt to allow the voters to ratify a federal constitutional amendment. The ballot legends and the non-incumbent candidate pledge were not integral or indispensable to the proposition, therefore the remaining portions of the proposition remained in effect.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the ballot legends and the pledge were unconstitutional and issued a writ of prohibition that prohibited the secretary from carrying them out. The court declared that the instructions in the proposition were not unconstitutional and severed them from the unconstitutional portions.

 

53 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Roell v. Boise City


Docket No. 23002, 1997 Opinion No. 71


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


130 Idaho 199; 938 P.2d 1237; 1997 Ida. LEXIS 77



June 9, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 1, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Robert M. Rowett, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from a district court's order granting summary judgment. Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lot owner filed an action for trespass and conversion against defendants, a city, an employee, and unidentified persons, after the city removed items from the owner's property on the grounds that they were litter, junk, or garbage. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, granted summary judgment to the city. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: After being cited for zoning, housing, and litter ordinance violations, the owner did not respond to the citations. Eventually, the city authorized a clean-up of the property, and a contractor removed lawn mowers that were in pieces, bike parts, bike tires, a rusty oil barrel, more than 60 tires, various construction materials, and tree limbs from the property. The owner then filed his present action. He claimed that the items removed had value. The court stated that the city had the authority to control litter and nuisances within its limits under Idaho Code §§ 50-317 and 50-334 and Boise, Idaho, City Code §§ 6-16-14 and 8-8-2. The city was entitled to determine whether certain items were litter or trash, but in making this determination, it ran the risk of being sued for taking property of value from the owner. Here, the owner's affidavit and deposition raised a genuine issue of material fact as to whether the items were trash, garbage, or litter. The owner indicated that he intended to use the items and that they were not discarded. Thus, the trial court erred in granting summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the district court's grant of summary judgment. It remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

54 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mathews


Docket Nos. 20154, 21127, 1997 Opinion No. 35


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


129 Idaho 865; 934 P.2d 931; 1997 Ida. LEXIS 38



March 20, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Filed July 22, 1994. Released for Publication April 11, 1997. As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Nez Perce County. Hon. Ron Schilling, District Judge. On rehearing, appeal from an order of the district court denying appellant's motion to suppress. Remanded. On appeal from order denying appellant's motion for post-conviction relief.

This Opinion Substituted on Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of July 18, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Ida. LEXIS 101 



DISPOSITION: Vacated and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of an order of the Second Judicial District Court of Nez Perce County (Idaho), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief. The imate had been convicted of first degree murder for the death of his estranged wife. The district court held that an unsigned search warrant was valid.


OVERVIEW: The police executed the search warrant at a home on the Nez Perce Reservation without obtaining prior approval of a county judge. The police conferred with the Bureau of Indian Management, the tribal prosecutor, the Idaho Attorney General and, the United States Attorney before executing the warrant. The search uncovered the murder weapon and shoes matching footprints at the crime scene. The homeowner had questioned the validity of the search warrant by pointing out that it was not signed or dated. On appeal, the court vacated and remanded. In a case of first impression, the court held that, under Idaho Const. art. I, § 17, a search warrant must conform strictly to the constitution and applicable statutes. Moreover, Idaho Code §§ 19-4401, -4406, and -4407 created a substantive right in a citizen to refuse to permit a search pursuant to an unsigned warrant. The requirement of a signed warrant enabled a citizen to know that the search was authorized and was not the whim of the officer. Once the lack of a signature was discovered, the police should have stopped the search. The homeowner had exercised her right to question the warrant's validity, thus, the evidence was inadmissible.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and held that the district court erred in summarily disposing of the inmate's post-conviction application. The court remanded to the district court.

 

55 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Puetz


Docket No. 22616, 1997 Opinion No. 32


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


129 Idaho 842; 934 P.2d 15; 1997 Ida. LEXIS 34



March 13, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah A. Bail, District Judge. Appeal from a conviction of trafficking in heroin pursuant to I.C. Section 37-2732B (a) (5 (C).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which convicted defendant of trafficking in heroin and sentenced defendant to a fixed term of 15 years as required by Idaho Code § 37-2732B(a)(5)(C).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for trafficking in heroin after he sold heroin to a police informant. Defendant was convicted and sentenced to a fixed term of 15 years as required by Idaho Code § 37-2732B(a)(5)(C). Defendant appealed, arguing that § 37-2732B(a)(8), which provided the mandatory minimum sentencing, was unconstitutional. The court held that in 1978, the legislature proposed and the people ratified an amendment to Idaho Const. art. V. § 13 that stated that any mandatory minimum sentence could not be reduced. An appellate court found that § 37-2732(a)(8) was unconstitutional because it allowed for the reduction on statutory minimums. In 1995 Idaho Legislature amended § 37-2732B by deleting subsection (a)(8). Section 37-2732B, after the 1995 amendment, fully complied with the requirement of Idaho Const. art. V, § 13 that mandatory minimum sentences should not be reduced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Capital Care Ctr. v. Idaho Dep't of Health & Welfare

129 Idaho 773; 932 P.2d 896; 1997 Ida. LEXIS 30

Appeal from order affirming administrative decision.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant health care facility sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, affirming a decision of respondent department of health and welfare, which denied reimbursement to the facility that sought a related-party reimbursement.


OVERVIEW: The department received the facility's initial cost report, which acknowledged that it had engaged in a related-party transaction, but indicated that it fell under an exception that allowed full Medicaid reimbursement in a related-party transaction. The department concluded that a contract rate used violated both the related-party and reasonable-cost rules, and refused to accept the report. After modifying the rate, the department found that there was a related-party transaction and that the facility did not qualify for an exemption to the related-party rules. The trial court affirmed the department's judgment. The court affirmed, holding that the department correctly denied reimbursement based on the contract rate. In order to qualify for the exception, the facility was required to have qualified for the exception at the time the contract was executed. The court held that the department's regulatory scheme for Medicaid reimbursements was not unconstitutionally vague. The regulation set forth in Idaho Code § 56-110(a) was sufficiently clear.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

57 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Avelar


Docket No. 23240, 1997 Opinion No. 6


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


129 Idaho 700; 931 P.2d 1218; 1997 Ida. LEXIS 10



January 22, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended. Released for Publication February 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. Daniel B. Meehl, District Judge.

Appeal from the district court's denial of appellant's motion to dismiss due to violation of the statutory speedy trial rule, Idaho Code Section 19-3501.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County, which denied his motion to dismiss due to the violation of the statutory speedy trial rule under Idaho Code § 19-3501.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with delivery of a controlled substance. A jury found him guilty, and defendant successfully appealed the conviction. The second trial began more than six months later, and the district court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the case on the ground of a violation of § 19-3501. Defendant sought review of his second conviction on the speedy trial issue, and the court of appeals affirmed the conviction and sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. The court held that § 19-3501 did not apply to the instant case, a retrial following a successful appeal. The court stated that drawing a line between defendants awaiting their first trials and those awaiting retrial following successful appeal bore a rational relationship to legitimate government objectives and did not offend equal protection principles of the state constitution. The court stated that the district court erred, when it concluded that § 19-3501 applied to the instant case, and affirmed the district court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss because defendant did not have a statutory right to a speedy retrial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

Fremont-Madison Irrigation Dist. & Mitigation Group v. Idaho Ground Water Appropriators (in Re Srba Case No. 39576)


Docket No. 22354 and 22355, 1996 Opinion No. 122


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


129 Idaho 454; 926 P.2d 1301; 1996 Ida. LEXIS 128



October 2, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 24, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Honorable Daniel C. Hurlbutt, Jr., District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court that the "amnesty statutes" are constitutional is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Twin Falls County (Idaho) entered in favor of respondents in an action challenging the constitutionality of statutes relating to water rights. The district court held that Idaho Code §§ 42-1425, 42-1426, and 42-1427 were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The district court held that Idaho Code §§ 42-1425, 42-1426, and 42-1427, which were referred to as the amnesty statutes, were constitutional. The statutes were designed to protect water users who had failed to follow statutory procedures when the acquired certain water rights. On appeal, the court affirmed the district court's decision. The court held: (1) Idaho Code § 42-1425 was constitutional because the limitations in the statute protected other water users from injury; (2) the provision for enlargements of existing water rights contained in Idaho Code § 42-1426 was constitutional; (3) the mitigation provisions of § 42-1426 did not violate the principles of separation of power; and (4) Idaho Code § 42-1427 was constitutional as written because it did not provide for an enlargement of existing water rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court entered in favor of respondents upholding the constitutionality of the statutes governing water rights.

State v. Oar


Docket No. 21930, 1996 Opinion No. 110


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


129 Idaho 337; 924 P.2d 599; 1996 Ida. LEXIS 115



August 20, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied October 28, 1996. Released for Publication October 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Nez Perce County. Hon. Ron Schilling, District Judge.

Appeal from district court's denial of motion to dismiss, motion for a new trial, and motion to reduce sentence.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, which denied defendant's motion to dismiss, motion for a new trial, and motion to reduce sentence, and convicted defendant of sexual battery of a minor child sixteen or seventeen years of age in violation of Idaho Code § 18-1508A and of being a persistent violator of the law pursuant to Idaho Code § 19-2514.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested at a motel after climbing out of the bathroom window of his room, where he had participated in the sexual assault of two girls aged 16 and 17. Defendant had met the girls at an adults-only dance club and lured the girls to his motel room on the pretense that he wanted the girls to do some modeling for his business. Defendant had requested jury instructions at trial regarding the defenses of consent by the girls and defendant's mistake as to the age of the girls. The trial court denied defendant's requests and convicted defendant. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that defendant was not entitled to claim that he mistakenly believed that the girls were 18 years of age, because the mistake of fact defense provided in Idaho Code § 18-201(1) was no defense to the charge of sexual battery of a minor child 16 or 17 years of age. The court held that consent of the minor was not a legal defense to Idaho Code § 18-1508A. The court held that § 18-1508A was not unconstitutionally vague because the statute gave notice of what sexual contact was, provided guidelines, and imposed sufficient discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order convicting defendant of sexual battery of a minor child 16 or 17 years of age and of being a persistent violator of the law.

State v. Zichko


NO. 21815, 1996 Opinion No. 94


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


129 Idaho 259; 923 P.2d 966; 1996 Ida. LEXIS 98



July 29, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Honorable James Judd, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction and sentence of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho convicted defendant of failing to register with the county sheriff's office pursuant to Idaho Code § 18-8304, the Sex Offender Registration Act. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. Defendant argued: (1) § 18-8304 was void for vagueness; (2) he was arrested prematurely because the five-day statutory registration period did not include Saturday and Sunday; and (3) he was prevented from complying with the act because the place of registration was within a three-mile radius of his former wife's place of employment, and thus was within an area he was prohibited from entering pursuant to a civil protection order. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it gave defendant adequate notice of the obligation it imposed. The court held that defendant's arrest was not premature and did not violate standards of equal protection because the evidence showed that he had five full working days to register even if Saturday and Sunday were excluded. The court held that defendant was not legally prevented from complying with § 18-8304 because an officer would have come to him to get him registered. In addition, during the period for registration the protection order was modified and he could have registered at the license bureau had he had elected to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's judgment of conviction and sentence.

V-1 Oil Co. v. Idaho Petroleum Clean Water Trust Fund


Docket No. 21222


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


128 Idaho 890; 920 P.2d 909; 1996 Ida. LEXIS 89



July 2, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied July 2, 1996. Released for Publication July 24, 1996. Certiorari Denied December 2, 1996, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7207.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonneville County. Hon. Ted V. Wood, District Judge. Appeal from partial summary judgment declaring dedication of petroleum transfer fee to non-highway purposes unconstitutional.

This Opinion Substituted on Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of April 16, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Ida. LEXIS 40.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Idaho Petroleum Clean Water Trust Fund (fund) sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonneville County, which entered partial summary judgment in favor of respondent oil company declaring dedication of petroleum transfer fee to non-highway purposes unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The oil company filed an action against the fund, seeking an order that the petroleum transfer fee charged under the Idaho Petroleum Clean Water Trust Fund Act, Idaho Code § 41-4908(7), constituted a gasoline tax. Because the Idaho Constitution required that proceeds of any tax on gasoline were to be dedicated exclusively to the construction, repair, maintenance, and traffic supervision of public highways, the oil company sought to obtain a refund of fees paid and to have the fee declared unconstitutional. The trial court entered partial summary judgment in favor of the oil company. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that, to the extent that the petroleum transfer fee was assessed against gasoline and like motor vehicle fuels, the allocation of the proceeds of that fee to the fund violated Idaho Const. art. VII, § 17. However, the oil company was not entitled to a refund because the creation and collection of the transfer fee was not unconstitutional. Rather, the appropriation of the revenue, raised from the transfer fee, to the fund was unconstitutional. Thus, the revenue was to be appropriated by the legislature for uses consistent with Idaho Const. art. VII, § 17.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had entered partial summary judgment in favor of the oil company and against the trust fund and declared that the dedication of the petroleum transfer fee to non-highway purposes was unconstitutional.

Higuera v. Hiestand


Docket No. 21558, 1996 Opinion No. 75


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


128 Idaho 700; 918 P.2d 284; 1996 Ida. LEXIS 78



June 19, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 11, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Fremont County. Hon. Brent Moss, District Judge.

Appeal from denial of motion for new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of an order of the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Fremont County, which denied his motion for a new trial after the jury rendered a verdict in favor of respondent physician in the patient's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: After the jury rendered its verdict in favor of the physician, the patient filed a motion for new trial on the ground that the county's jury selection procedure systematically excluded Hispanic persons in violation of Idaho Code § 2-213 and his constitutional rights to a fair and impartial jury. The district court denied the motion and the patient appealed. The court noted that there was no question that the patient failed to comply with the time limitations imposed by § 2-213. The patient contended that if § 2-213 was interpreted to preclude his separate constitutional challenges, the application of that provision resulted in a denial of due process. The court disagreed and affirmed the denial of the motion, holding that a civil litigant was required to raise his objections to a jury panel in the manner prescribed by statute. Because § 2-213 provided civil litigants timely notice and a meaningful opportunity to be heard on issues relating to jury selection, the court held that it did not effect a denial of due process to require the patient to present his challenge to the jury selection process within the provisions of § 2-213.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's denial of the motion for new trial.

Rincover v. Dep't of Fin.

SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO

June 4, 1996, Filed

Appeal from the grant of summary judgment and from the dismissal of certain claims for failure to state a claim upon which relief may be granted.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicants brought a cause of action against defendant state and state officials alleging negligence, malicious prosecution, defamation, and civil rights violations. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District (Idaho) granted the state and the state officials' motions for summary judgment and dismissal of the claims for failure to state claim upon which relief could be granted. The applicants sought review of the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The applicants both applied to become registered securities salespersons. Based upon the fact that the applicants had been investigated for professional violations, their applications were denied. Upon review, the supreme court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The supreme court found that the state officials were entitled to absolute immunity from the applicants' claims because the acts of the officials that were complained of by the applicants were clearly accomplished during the performance of their prosecutorial and adjudicatory functions. The applicants' tort claims were properly dismissed because the applicants failed to establish that the state and its employees acted with gross negligence. The state's conduct in denying the applicant wife's application was not grossly negligent. The applicant husband was precluded by operation of the doctrine of collateral estoppel from raising the issue of the reasonableness of the state's conduct because the issue had already been litigated in a prior proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Boundary Backpackers v. Boundary County


Docket No. 21287, 1996 Opinion No. 26


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


128 Idaho 371; 913 P.2d 1141; 1996 Ida. LEXIS 26



March 18, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied April 18, 1996. Released for Publication April 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Boundary County. Hon. James R. Michaud, District Judge.

Appeal from order granting summary judgment and award of attorney fees.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to summary judgment; reversed as to attorney fees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board appealed from the order of the District Court of the First Judicial District, Boundary County (Idaho), which granted summary judgment and an award of attorney fees to plaintiff environmental groups in a case which concerned a county ordinance that required all federal and state agencies to comply with a county land use policy plan.


OVERVIEW: Defendant enacted an ordinance intended to protect the rights of private landowners. Plaintiff brought a declaratory judgment action and the trial court granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that plaintiff had standing and that the case was ripe for judicial review. The court found that the provisions of the ordinance were preempted by federal law because they imposed restrictions on federal agencies that were inconsistent with federal laws authorizing acquisition of land. The court found that the ordinance conflicted with the authority of federal agencies concerning the withdrawal of federal land. The court noted that none of the federal land laws gave local governmental units veto power over decisions by federal agencies charged with managing federal land. Defendant's attempted veto power was contrary to the provisions of the Endangered Species Act of 1973, 16 U.S.C.S. §§ 1531-1543; the Wild and Scenic Rivers Act, 16 U.S.C.S. §§ 1275-1276; and the Wilderness Act, 16 U.S.C.S. § 1132.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as to summary judgment but reversed as to attorney fees because the ordinance was unconstitutional because federal law preempted portions of the ordinance and that the entire ordinance was invalid because the unconstitutional portions were not severable.

Buchin v. Lance (in Re Writ of Prohibition Entitled "ballot Title Challenge Oral Argument Requested.")


Docket No. 22395, 1995 Opinion No. 150


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


128 Idaho 266; 912 P.2d 634; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 166



December 22, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Prohibition pursuant to I.C. § 34-1809, from the Idaho Attorney General's short and long titles for an initiative petition. Hon. Alan G. Lance, Attorney General. Boise, November, 1995 Term.



DISPOSITION: Petition for Writ of Prohibition challenging the short and long titles for initiative. Ballot title not certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizens sought a writ of prohibition under Idaho Code § 34-1809, in connection with allegedly invalid titles for a proposed ballot initiative, to prevent respondent Secretary of State of Idaho from approving for circulation any petitions containing the titles, accepting any signatures containing the titles, and utilizing the titles in any publication, including voter's pamphlets or ballots.


OVERVIEW: The citizens sought a writ of prohibition under Idaho Code § 34-1809 to prevent a proposed ballot initiative, which would have restricted certain abortion procedures, from being presented for election on the grounds that respondent attorney general's short ballot titles failed to provide a distinctive statement by which the measure would be described and that the long title failed to describe the initiative's purpose. The court issued the writ, found that the attorney general's short and long ballot titles were insufficient under § 34-1809, and ruled that the signatures collected on the petitions with the defective titles were invalid. Because the initiative would have amended existing statutory law, the attorney general had a duty under § 34-1809 to include in the short title the fact that the initiative would delete and add exceptions to Idaho's existing ban on post-viability abortions and to set forth in the short title what distinguished the initiative from existing law. The court found that the long title failed to provide voters with an accurate description of the purposes of the initiative, and the court provided acceptable short and long title language.


OUTCOME: The court granted the citizens' petition for a writ of prohibition challenging the short and long titles for the initiative, declared the ballot title not certified, and invalidated the signatures collected on the petitions with the defective titles.

Estate of Kirk v. Seideman

SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO

Appeal by decedent's nephew from a district court order affirming the magistrate court's order that the decedent's inter vivos trust was a valid, enforceable trust and that the various specific gifts should be delivered to the designated beneficiaries.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee trustee filed a petition following the decedent's death for construction of her will and trust. Appellant nephew of the decedent (nephew) sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, which affirmed the magistrate court's order that the decedent's inter vivos trust was a valid, enforceable trust.


OVERVIEW: The trustee contended that a document handwritten by the decedent was a valid amendment to her trust and that her estate should be distributed in accordance with the document. The district court, in affirming the magistrate court's decision validating the document, held that while the document violated the Idaho mortmain statute, Idaho Code § 15-2-615, the statute was unconstitutional due to a violation of equal protection. The court held first that § 15-2-615 was inapplicable to the case because the statute referred to gifts made to charities through a will, not a trust. The court held further that the magistrate did not err in admitting certain extrinsic and parol evidence because the language of the decedent's estate plan with respect to the meaning of the document was ambiguous. Further, the court held that the magistrate's reliance on certain parol evidence did not violate the statute of frauds, Idaho Code § 9-503, because all of the trust documents were in writing and that the magistrate properly admitted and relied upon the decedent's prior wills to show her intent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

68 of 696 DOCUMENTS


In re Srba Case No. 39576


Docket No. 22039, 1995 Opinion No. 139


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


127 Idaho 688; 905 P.2d 89; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 152



November 3, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 27, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. Daniel C. Hurlbutt, Jr., District Judge.

Appeal from denial of motion to dismiss.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Idaho Department of Water Resources (IDWR) sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Twin Falls County (Idaho), which denied its motion to dismiss a suit brought by respondent canal companies, seeking declaratory relief under Idaho Code § 67-5278 (1995) to declare IDWR's rules concerning conjunctive management of ground water and surface water rights for the entire state invalid.


OVERVIEW: IDWR adopted administrative rules concerning conjunctive management of ground water and surface water rights for the entire state. The canal companies filed a petition against IDWR in the Snake River Basin Adjudication (SRBA) seeking declaratory relief pursuant to Idaho Code § 67-5278 (1995) declaring the rules invalid. IDWR moved to dismiss the petition on the ground that the SRBA district court did not have subject matter jurisdiction to hear the petition for declaratory relief. The SRBA district court denied IDWR's motion and an appeal was taken. The court held that the canal companies could not seek declaratory relief in SRBA against the IDWR because IDWR could not be joined as a party to SRBA. Under Idaho Code § 42-1401A(4), the director of IDWR was defined to include the IDWR, and therefore the canal companies could not pursue their action for declaratory judgment as part of SRBA. The legislature had removed the director as a party to the adjudication. The court noted that IDWR was required to be a party to the action, and IDWR was not and could not be a party to SRBA.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

69 of 696 DOCUMENTS


In re Srba Case No. 39576


DOCKET NO. 21869, 1995 Opinion No. 120


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


128 Idaho 246; 912 P.2d 614; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 131



September 1, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied August 3, 1995. Released for Publication September 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. Daniel C. Hurlbutt, Jr., District Judge.

Appeal from decision and order from district court on basin-wide issues two and three in the Snake River Basin Adjudication.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of June 23, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Ida. LEXIS 85. Withdrawal Order of September 1, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ida. LEXIS 132.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the judgment of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County, which held in favor of appellee federal government that certain statutes regarding the powers and duties of the director of water resources were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: State legislature, in response to a general adjudication of water rights, set forth statutes that defined the duties of the director of water resources. Those statutes were later amended. Inter alia, the trial court determined that the amended statutes were unconstitutional, unseverable, and had no effect on the previous statutes. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The legislature's direction that the contents of the director's report would constitute prima facie evidence of some water right claims was a permissible. Idaho Code § 42-1423 (1994), which prohibited an award of attorney fees, was a legitimate exercise of the legislature's substantive authority. The director could be withdrawn as a party through the amendment of the statute that gave him that designation. To the extent that Idaho Code § 42-1401B(1) constituted a legislative determination as to the director's status as an expert, that provision was of no effect. Because striking the unconstitutional portions did not prevent the remaining provisions of that legislation from functioning as intended, the unconstitutional provisions could be severed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.
