Idaho Conservation League v. State (in Re Srba - Case No. 39576)


DOCKET NO. 21144, 1995 Opinion No. 116


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


128 Idaho 155; 911 P.2d 748; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 136



August 31, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied November 8, 1995. Released for Publication November 8, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. Daniel C. Hurlbutt, Jr., District Judge.

Appeal from order denying Conservation Groups' motion to intervene to assert the public trust doctrine in Snake River Basin Adjudication.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of July 8, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Ida. LEXIS 95.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Cross appeal from order denying Conservation Groups' motion to intervene to assert the Local Public Interest. Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant conservation groups sought review of an order from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District (Idaho), which denied their motion to intervene in a Snake River Basin Adjudication (SRBA) based on the public trust doctrine. Respondents, state, irrigation districts, and other water users, cross-appealed the order that found the conservation groups could intervene on the statutory doctrine of local public interest.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that its limited jurisdiction as an SRBA court did not provide it with the authority to consider the public trust doctrine when decreeing water rights. Upon review, the court affirmed in part and vacated in part. It found that the trial court correctly concluded that the public trust doctrine was not an element of a water right that should be used to determine the priority of that right in relation to competing claims of other water right claimants. The court observed that the legislature eliminated the need for an SRBA court to consider the local public interest in determining the nature and extent of expanded or changed water rights by repealing portions of the Idaho Code. Because the grounds upon which the conservation groups were granted limited intervention were repealed, the court vacated their motion to intervene.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the conservation groups' petition to intervene to assert the public trust doctrine. The court vacated the order granting the conservation groups petition to intervene to assert the local public interest.

 

71 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sivak


Docket Nos. 20212/20681, 1995 Opinion No. 105


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


127 Idaho 387; 901 P.2d 494; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 116



August 18, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied August 18, 1995. Released for Publication September 11, 1995. Certiorari Denied December 1, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7175.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Robert G. Newhouse, District Judge.

Review of death sentence imposed after a conviction for first-degree murder.

This Opinion Substituted on Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of August 19, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Ida. LEXIS 117.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death in the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Defendant's conviction was affirmed on appeal three time, and his case was remanded twice for resentencing. During the last remand for resentencing, defendant was again sentenced to death. Defendant again appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that, after a careful examination of the record, the district court did not err by denying both of defendant's motions to disqualify the district court judge from presiding over the resentencing and the post-conviction relief hearing. Additionally, the jury instruction on the definition of reasonable doubt, particularly the use of the phrases "moral evidence" and "moral certainty," were not unconstitutional in the context of the jury instructions as a whole. And, the district court did not violate either Idaho Ct. R. 32(e) or Idaho Code § 19-2516 by considering during sentencing a co-defendant's statement, which was included in the presentence report. The court refused to adopt the absolute position that statements from a co-defendant were inherently unreliable. There was independent evidence of motive, intent, and a connection to the murder weapon that provided at least some minimum indicia of reliability in that it tended to corroborate the co-defendant's statement that defendant committed the murder. Thus, defendant was not denied due process by the consideration of the co-defendant's statement. The court affirmed the sentence of death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.

 

72 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Gafford v. State (in Re Gafford)


Docket No. 21472, 1995 Opinion No. 98


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


127 Idaho 472; 903 P.2d 61; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 109



August 16, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 17, 1995. Released for Publication October 17, 1995. Certiorari Denied March 18, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1788.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bingham County. Hon. James C. Herndon, District Judge; Hon. James L. Martsch, Magistrate Judge.

Appeal from magistrate's grant of petition for writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insanity acquittee sought review of a judgment from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, which reversed the magistrate's grant of appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus that sought release from commitment on the ground that he was no longer mentally ill.


OVERVIEW: The insanity acquittee had filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus that sought release from commitment on the ground that he was no longer mentally ill. The magistrate had granted the petition because Idaho Code § 66-337(d), which allowed for the continued confinement of an insanity acquittee on the basis of dangerous alone, was unconstitutional in light of a recent state supreme court decision. The district court had reversed the magistrate's decision because it found § 66-337(d) was constitutional, and the state supreme court decision could not be applied retroactively to this case. On appeal, the court agreed with the decision of the magistrate, and found § 66-337(d) was unconstitutional. The court found the burden that was placed on the insanity by § 66-337(d) for gaining release by proving that he was without danger to himself or others was unconstitutional, and violated due process. Next, the court rejected the state's arguments of retroactivity, collateral estoppel, and equitable estoppel because the court found that they had no application in this case. Finally, the court held that the insanity acquittee was entitled to immediate release.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment, and affirmed the decision of the magistrate that granted the insanity acquittee's petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The court found the insanity acquittee was entitled to release from commitment on the ground that he was no longer mentally ill.

 

73 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Henry v. State (in Re Henry)


Docket No. 21470, 1995 Opinion No. 99


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


127 Idaho 349; 900 P.2d 1360; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 110



August 16, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 8, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bingham County. Hon. James C. Herndon, District Judge; Hon. James L. Martsch, Magistrate Judge.

Appeal from magistrate's denial of petition for writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a man acquitted of criminal charges by reason of insanity but confined to a state mental institution, sought review of a decision of the Seventh Judicial District Court of Bingham County (Idaho), which affirmed a decision of a magistrate judge denying the man's petition for habeas corpus in which he sought release from confinement on the ground that he was no longer mentally ill, and ruled that petitioner was a dangerous person.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner applied for a writ of habeas corpus seeking release from hospital confinement, claiming he was no longer mentally ill. A magistrate determined that Idaho Code § 66-337(d), which allowed for continued confinement of insanity acquittees on the basis of dangerousness alone, was unconstitutional. Although petitioner's mental state was such that he was not civilly committable, the magistrate found that he continued to suffer from the mental condition that was the basis for the acquittal. Finding petitioner to be dangerous, he denied the petition, the district court agreed and, on appeal, the court affirmed. Substantial evidence supported the finding of dangerousness, given petitioner's predatory tendencies with regard to children. Moreover, competent evidence showed that he continued to suffer from a mental condition that was the basis of his acquittal. Thus, continued confinement was not objectionable on due process grounds. Finally, the entry into evidence of documentation showing dangerousness was harmless error, being duplicative of testimony presented.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the magistrate's denial of petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus seeking release from confinement in a state mental institution.

 

74 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Nielsen v. State (in Re Nielsen)


Docket No. 21471, 1995 Opinion No. 100


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


127 Idaho 449; 902 P.2d 474; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 111



August 16, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied October 5, 1995. Released for Publication October 5, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bingham County. Hon. James C. Herndon, District Judge. Hon. James L. Martsch, Magistrate Judge.

Appeal from magistrate's grant of petition for writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was acquitted of charges of first degree murder by reason of insanity in 1972. He filed a petition for habeas corpus in the magistrate court on the basis of a U.S. Supreme Court decision prohibiting confinement based on dangerousness alone. The magistrate declared Idaho Code § 66-337(d), the confinement statute, unconstitutional. The Seventh Judicial District Court, Bingham County (Idaho), reversed. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The magistrate found, and the district court agreed, that under Foucha v. Louisiana, Idaho Code § 66-337(d) was unconstitutional because it allowed the continued confinement of insanity acquittees on the basis of dangerousness alone. In this case, the magistrate's finding that the petitioner was still dangerous was supported by substantial and competent evidence. In addition, the evidence demonstrated that petitioner had a very fixed personality disorder that was unchanged from the time of acquittal. The magistrate's finding that petitioner's mental condition had changed was clearly erroneous. Because the basis for petitioner's criminal acquittal and commitment persisted, Foucha did not require that he be released, and it did not require that his continued commitment be justified anew by civil commitment proceedings. The court concluded that the mental condition of petitioner was constitutionally sufficient to justify his automatic commitment upon acquittal, and it remained sufficient to justify his continued commitment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's determination that the writ of habeas corpus should be granted, and held that although the Idaho confinement statute was unconstitutional, the finding that petitioner continued to be dangerous required the denial of the writ of habeas corpus.

 

75 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Weaver


Docket No. 21673, 1995 Opinion No. 88


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


127 Idaho 288; 900 P.2d 196; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 98



July 25, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 16, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. Gary M. Haman, District Judge.

Sua sponte review of a Court of Appeals decision affirming the district court's order denying appellant's motion to suppress evidence.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court, acting sua sponte, reviewed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Idaho), which affirmed a district court's order denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence. Defendant was charged with unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon. The appellate court held that the arresting officer's decision that impoundment of the vehicle defendant was driving when arrested was necessary was reasonable at the time it was made.


OVERVIEW: Police officers received information that defendant and his 70-year-old mother were coming into the state in order to kill someone. The authorities from the other state advised that defendant was wanted for parole violations. When defendant's car was stopped and he was arrested, the officer concluded that the mother was physically incapable of driving the car. He impounded the vehicle. The handgun at issue was found during the inventory search. The court held that the officer's decision was not reasonable. The policies of the officer's jurisdiction provided that an officer did not have authority to impound a vehicle if the owner of the vehicle was not under arrest, had a valid driver's license, and claimed to be capable of driving. The officer did not take the time to ascertain, as a person of reasonable caution would do, whether the mother, who was not under arrest, had a valid driver's license and claimed to be capable of driving. Therefore, the impoundment was not reasonable and the warrantless search did not fall within the inventory exception to the warrant requirement of the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower courts' denial of defendant's motion to suppress the evidence discovered in the warrantless search.

State v. Valdez-Molina


Docket No. 20595, 1995 Opinion No. 66


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


127 Idaho 102; 897 P.2d 993; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 76



June 15, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 7, 1995. As Amended August 21, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Jim R. Doolittle, District Judge.

Appeal from convictions for cocaine possession and sentences for cocaine trafficking.



DISPOSITION: Convictions, affirmed; sentences, vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged a judgment of the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County, that convicted them of trafficking in cocaine, conspiring to traffic in cocaine, and possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. Defendants were sentenced pursuant to Idaho Code § 37-2732B(a)(2)(C) to 10 to 15 years for trafficking and to concurrent terms for the other charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, an uncle and nephew, were arrested by agents for the immigration and naturalization service (INS) who were posing as cocaine buyers as part of an investigation of two other men who had arranged for defendants to transport cocaine from California to Idaho. The four men were tried together. Defendants claimed that they were entrapped, that the voluntariness of their statements was improperly submitted to a jury, and that § 37-2732B was unconstitutional. The court agreed with their third claim based upon a case decided after defendants were sentenced. It vacated the sentences, remanded for resentencing, and affirmed the convictions. Defendants preserved their claim that they were entrapped by raising it in a motion to acquit, but they lacked standing because they were not the direct targets of the INS investigation. INS agents did not know defendants existed until the cocaine sale occurred. Whether an arrestee's Miranda waiver or statement was knowingly and voluntarily given was a question to be decided by the judge, not the jury, but any error of the trial court in submitting the question to the jury was harmless pursuant to Idaho Crim. R. 52 (1994).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for trafficking in cocaine, conspiring to traffic in cocaine, and possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. Defendants' sentences were vacated and the case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

Malmin


Docket No. 21595, 1995 Opinion No. 51


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


126 Idaho 1024; 895 P.2d 1217; 1995 Ida. LEXIS 66



May 24, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 15, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for review of informal discipline imposed by the Idaho State Bar.
Malmin v. Engler, 124 Idaho 733, 864 P.2d 179, 1993 Ida. App. LEXIS 178 (Idaho Ct. App., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner lawyer applied for judicial review of, inter alia, the decision of respondent hearing committee to uphold respondent bar counsel's decision to issue a private reprimand to the lawyer for violating Idaho Rules of Professional Conduct Rule 3.3(d) by failing to advise a magistrate of settlement negotiations with opposing counsel in a child support proceeding where opposing counsel failed to appear.


OVERVIEW: The lawyer represented a mother who sought an increase in child support from her ex-husband. The lawyer and the ex-husband's attorney tentatively reached an oral settlement agreement and neither the ex-husband nor his attorney appeared at the modification hearing. The lawyer did not inform the presiding magistrate judge that they had reached a tentative agreement. Accordingly, a default judgment was entered for the mother for the full amount sought. An ethics complaint was filed, and bar counsel determined that the lawyer had violated Rule 3.3(d) by failing to inform the magistrate judge of the negotiations and tentative agreement. The hearing committee upheld the imposition of a private reprimand. In denying the lawyer a petition for review, the supreme court ruled, inter alia, that the finding that the lawyer violated Rule 3.3(d) was not clearly erroneous because the proceeding was considered an ex parte proceeding when the ex-husband's attorney failed to appear, giving rise to a duty of candor toward the magistrate judge. Bar counsel's authority to impose discipline came from a delegation by the supreme court, not the executive or legislative branches.


OUTCOME: The lawyer's petition for judicial review of the issuance of a private reprimand against her for violating the ethical rule regarding candor before a tribunal was denied.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the District Court of the Second Judicial District (Idaho), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion for post-conviction relief as well as his amended motion for such relief were dismissed on the ground that such relief was barred because the issues raised therein did not satisfy the requirements of Idaho Code § 19-2719. Defendant appealed and the State filed a motion to dismiss defendant's appeal on the grounds that § 19-2719 divested the trial court of jurisdiction to consider defendant's claims. The court held that neither the allegations in defendant's petition nor the documents filed in support of that petition satisfied the burden established by § 19-2719. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to disqualify the trial judge on the basis that the judge was a potential witness to the claims raised in defendant's amended petition, however, defendant presented no evidence that the possibility that the trial judge might have been a potential witness interfered with the trial court's ability to determine whether the jurisdictional bar of § 19-2719 precluded defendant's petition. Defendant therefore failed to meet the prima facie requirements for maintaining an action for post-conviction relief under § 19-2719.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorneys filed objections to the findings and recommendations of the Hearing Committee of the Professional Conduct Board of the Idaho State Bar.


OVERVIEW: The hearing committee recommended that the attorneys be suspended from the practice of law for 60 days. The court adopted the hearing committee's recommendation and suspended the attorneys for 60 days. The court found that the attorneys violated Idaho Rules of Prof'l Conduct R. 1.3 and 1.4 by failing to represent their clients with reasonable diligence and promptness and by failing to keep their clients informed about the status of the matters they were representing the clients on. OUTCOME: The court adopted the recommendations of the hearing committee and suspended the attorneys from the practice of law for 60 days.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Kootenai County, which convicted and sentenced defendant for attempted first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with attempted first degree murder for the shooting of his estranged wife. He was tried to a jury and convicted. The trial court denied his motion for a new trial and sentenced him to a fixed term of seven years followed by an indeterminate term of eight years. State v. Casey


Docket No. 20703, 1994 Opinion No. 70


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


125 Idaho 856; 876 P.2d 138; 1994 Ida. LEXIS 75



June 10, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Blaine County. Hon. James J. May, District Judge; Hon. John F. Varin, Magistrate Judge.

Appeal from a judgment of conviction.



DISPOSITION: Conviction vacated


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Blaine County, which affirmed the trial court's judgment that found defendant guilty of violating Idaho Code § 36-1510(1)(c) and imposed a monetary fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Idaho Code § 36-1510(1)(c), which prohibited interference with hunting, fishing, and predator control, was unconstitutional on its face as a content-based regulation of speech and that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad. On appeal, the court vacated the conviction. In so ruling, the court concluded that although the statute did not specifically prohibit speech or the expression of viewpoints of any specific interest group, it did reach substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct based on its prohibition against someone entering or remaining on property with the "intent to interfere" with lawful hunting of wildlife. The court ruled that § 36-1510(1)(c) was unconstitutionally overbroad because it did not require physical interference and it was not limited to prohibiting unprotected speech, such as fighting words or obscenity; thus the statute compromised expression protected by the First Amendment. The court further concluded that § 36-1510(1)(c) was not an indispensable part of the statute and could be stricken therefrom, leaving the rest of the statute is fully operative.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's judgment of conviction.

State v. Hansen


S. CT. NO. 20045, 1994 Opinion No. 69


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


125 Idaho 927; 877 P.2d 898; 1994 Ida. LEXIS 74



June 9, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 1, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Clearwater County. Hon. Linda Copple Trout, District Judge.

Appeal of judgment and sentence on racketeering charges stemming from Rule 11 plea agreement.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; sentence affirmed in part, vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Second Judicial District Court, Clearwater County (Idaho), which convicted him of racketeering.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted upon a conditional plea of guilty of racketeering stemming from his participation in the growing and processing of marijuana. Defendant appealed. The court held that: (1) there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction as there was a common or shared purpose, continuity of structure and personnel, and an ascertainable structure distinct from the inherent conduct of the pattern of racketeering activity itself; (2) the Racketeering Act, Idaho Code § 18-7801 et seq., was not constitutionally void for vagueness; (3) defendant's sentence did not violate the equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions as the trial court properly considered the likelihood of defendant committing a future crime, his flight to Canada and Mexico to avoid prosecution, and the role he played in the enterprise; and (4) the trial court abused its discretion by ordering that defendant pay restitution to the county as defendant was not convicted of a felony violation under the controlled substances act. Defendant's conviction was affirmed, the order of restitution was vacated, and the remainder of defendant's sentence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on the charge of racketeering, vacated the order of restitution, and affirmed the remainder of defendant's sentence.

 

84 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Idaho Dep't of Law Enforcement by & ex rel. Cade v. Real Property Located in Minidoka County


Docket No. 20626, 1994 Opinion No. 66


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


126 Idaho 422; 885 P.2d 381; 1994 Ida. LEXIS 73



June 8, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Minidoka County. Hon. J. William Hart, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from denial of motion to dismiss, grant of summary judgment and forfeiture order; summary judgment reversed; forfeiture order vacated; and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners disputed decisions of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Minidoka County (Idaho), which denied their motion to dismiss a forfeiture proceeding brought under Idaho Code § 37-2744A, granted summary judgment for respondent Idaho Department of Law Enforcement (department), and issued a civil forfeiture order. The court considered whether § 37-2744A violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII or Idaho Const. art. I, § 7.


OVERVIEW: One of the homeowners pled guilty to a charge that, in the bedroom of the home, she delivered one-quarter ounce of marijuana, valued at $ 60, to a police informant. On appeal, the court noted that § 37-2744A was modeled on, and virtually identical to, 21 U.S.C.S. §§ 881(a)(4) and (a)(7). The Excessive Fines Clause of U.S. Const. amend. VIII applied to civil in rem forfeitures under the federal statute. The court held that the civil designation of § 37-2744A was not dispositive, and the statute was punitive at least in part. So, the Excessive Fines Clause applied to in rem forfeitures made pursuant to § 37-2744A, and summary judgment was improperly granted on that issue. The court held that Idaho Code § 37-2744A(e) did not preclude the possibility that the forfeiture could be excessive. The court remanded the case to the district court for an initial determination under circumstances where the excessiveness issue could be fully litigated. Further, the court held that, based on art. I, § 7, there was a right to jury trial for forfeiture proceedings under § 37-2744A. The court struck the subsection denying the right to a jury trial as unconstitutional. But, dismissal was not required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's grant of the department's summary judgment motion, vacated the forfeiture order, and remanded the case to the district court.

State v. Sarabia


Docket Nos. 20440, 20576, 20583, 1994 Opinion No. 62


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


125 Idaho 815; 875 P.2d 227; 1994 Ida. LEXIS 68



June 3, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bannock and Power Counties. Hon. B. Lynn Winmill (Perez and Hoadley cases) and Hon. Peter D. McDermott (Sarabia case), District Judges. Appeal from sentences for drug trafficking.



DISPOSITION: Sentence of Perez to a term of years, affirmed. Fixed term sentences of Hoadley and Sarabia, vacated and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three defendants sought review of the decisions of the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bannock and Power Counties that sentenced defendant one to a fixed term of seven years, followed by an indeterminate term of thirteen years, sentenced defendant two to a fixed term of three years, followed by an indeterminate term of two years, and sentenced defendant three to a fixed term of five years.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of violating Idaho's drug trafficking statute, Idaho Code § 37-2732B. Defendant one and defendant two were also assessed fines. Defendants argued that the portion of § 37-2732B that provided minimum fixed terms of imprisonment from which the trial court could deviate only upon motion of the prosecuting attorney violated the separation of powers doctrine contained in Idaho Const. art. 5, § 12 by taking away the inherent power of the sentencing judge to impose a lesser sentence or to suspend a portion of the fixed sentence. The court agreed and modified the sentences of defendant two and defendant three accordingly. Because defendant one received a fixed sentence in excess of the sentences provided for in Idaho Code § 37-2732B, the court concluded that its holding did not apply to him and affirmed his sentence. The court did not address the claim raised by defendant two and defendant three that the fines assessed against them were excessive, concluding that, because they failed to raise the issue at the trial court, it would not consider the issue because the imposition of the fines was not fundamental error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant one's sentence. The court vacated the fixed term sentences of defendant two and defendant three and remanded their causes for resentencing.

Miller v. Echohawk


Docket No. 20398, 1994 Opinion No. 53


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


126 Idaho 47; 878 P.2d 746; 1994 Ida. LEXIS 56



April 25, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 25, 1994. Released for Publication August 25, 1994. As Corrected October 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Robert G. Newhouse, District Judge. Award of attorney fees to respondent.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, which awarded attorney fees to respondent voter under the private attorney general doctrine in a reapportionment action. The district court denied the attorney general's motion to reconsider the award. The secretary of state and leaders of the Idaho Legislature joined the attorney general's brief.


OVERVIEW: The Idaho legislature was obligated to reapportion itself based on the census data. The legislature began working on reapportionment, but few people believed that a plan would be adopted quickly. A voter brought an action under the private attorney general doctrine to, among other things, set a date for the legislature to adopt a reapportionment plan or have the court determine reapportionment. Subsequently, the legislature passed a reapportionment bill that was signed by the governor. Consequently, the district court vacated the proceedings for court constructed reapportionment, issued its final judgment, and dismissed the matter without prejudice. The district court awarded of fees to the voter. On review, the court held the district court's exercise of discretion in awarding fees turned on whether the district court's factual determination was clearly erroneous. The court held that the legislature's self-imposed deadline for reapportioning itself was in direct response to the lawsuit. The district court was not clearly erroneous in its determination that private enforcement was needed. The district court did not abuse its discretion in awarding fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Post-conviction relief denied at Pratt v. State, 134 Idaho 581, 6 P.3d 831, 2000 Ida. LEXIS 72 (Idaho, 2000)

Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Pratt, 2014 Ida. App. Unpub. LEXIS 566 (Idaho Ct. App., Dec. 9, 2014)

State v. Pratt, 125 Idaho 546, 873 P.2d 800, 1993 Ida. LEXIS 141 (Idaho, 1993)
State v. Pratt, 1993 Ida. LEXIS 140 (Idaho, July 27, 1993)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of conviction and sentences on several counts, including first degree murder are affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonner County of first degree burglary, robbery, second degree kidnapping, ten counts of aggravated assault, aggravated assault upon a law enforcement officer, attempted first degree murder, and first degree murder. He appealed his convictions and sentence.

I, § 7; and (4) based upon the record, the sentences imposed were not excessive under any reasonable view of the facts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for first degree burglary, robbery, second degree kidnapping, aggravated assault, aggravated assault upon a law enforcement officer, and first degree murder and vacated defendant's conviction for attempted felony murder.

 

88 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Owner-Operator Indep. Drivers Ass'n v. Idaho Puc


Docket No. 20428, 1994 Opinion No. 33


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


125 Idaho 401; 871 P.2d 818; 1994 Ida. LEXIS 35



March 16, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 31, 1994. Released for Publication April 7, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Robert G. Newhouse, District Judge. Appeal and cross-appeal from partial summary judgment entered in favor of both parties.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for further action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both appellant carriers and respondent State challenged a decision from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which entered partial summary judgment in favor of both parties, determining that certain interstate motor carriers were entitled to a refund of a portion of the fees they paid to renew their registration of Interstate Commerce Commission operating authority; and attorney fees of 25 percent were awarded.


OVERVIEW: Although Idaho Code § 61-812 was violating the Commerce Clause when the suit was filed, it was subsequently amended to reduce the renewal fee, so the trial court did not have to declare it unconstitutional and did not enjoin its enforcement. The suit was certified as a class of all interstate carriers who paid the allegedly excessive fee. On review, the court agreed that two federal regulations were improperly combined to determine a permissible burden on interstate commerce. The court pointed out that regulations allowed the State to charge carriers a maximum of $ 10 to renew and $ 10 for vehicle identification, but the State had no law to charge interstate carriers for vehicle identification, and it had only adopted a $ 25 fee for interstate carrier registration, with no distinction between renewal or new registration. The court concluded that all carriers who paid the excessive fee were entitled to a $ 15 refund for each of the three years before the amendment. The court rejected the notion that the fees had to be paid under protest because although taxes funded public services at large, fees only covered the cost of the particular service the State provided to the individual.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's opinion by finding that it erroneously combined two federal regulations to determine the permissible burden on interstate commerce and that it miscalculated the refund due to the carriers. The court held that no fees or costs would be awarded to either party on appeal. The trial court's opinion was otherwise affirmed, and the court remanded for further action consistent with the court's opinion.

State v. Odiaga


S. CT. NO. 19681, 1994 Opinion No. 13


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 28, 1994. Released for Publication April 28, 1994.

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of second degree murder, one count of attempted first degree murder, and two counts of aggravated assault in the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho. He appealed his convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged numerous grounds of error on appeal, including arguments that the trial court erred in denying his motion to be taken off antipsychotic and psychotropic medications, in allowing the state to conduct a psychiatric evaluation of the defendant, and that the sentence was excessive. Mulch v. Mulch


No. 19840, 1994 Opinion No. 2


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


125 Idaho 93; 867 P.2d 967; 1994 Ida. LEXIS 3



January 11, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonner County. Hon. James R. Michaud, District Judge; Hon. Debra Heise, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from spousal maintenence award. Vacated and remanded. Appeal from award of attorney fees. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Bonner County (Idaho) that granted defendant wife a divorce on the grounds of extreme cruelty and awarded spousal maintenance in the amount of $ 1,700 per month for at least five years.


OVERVIEW: A husband challenged a trial court judgment awarding his wife spousal maintenance of $ 1,700 for at least five years. The trial court found that the husband had abused the wife and that she suffered from post-traumatic distress disorder because of his abuse, needed therapy, and was unable to work. The trial court divided the personal property equally, but found that even after the division of the community property, the wife lacked liquid assets to support herself. The court held that the substantial and competent evidence standard of review applied to the amount and duration of a maintenance award, and found that there was substantial and competent evidence to support the trial court's finding that the wife was entitled to spousal maintenance under Idaho Code § 32-705 for at least five years. However, the court concluded that the trial court did not make a specific finding concerning the amount awarded and that there was not substantial and competent evidence to support an implicit finding of need for the $ 1,700 awarded. Therefore, the court affirmed the award of spousal maintenance but vacated the amount awarded. The court also affirmed the award of attorney's fees to the wife.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that awarded the wife spousal maintenance, but vacated the amount of the award and remanded the case to the trial court for consideration of the amount to be paid as spousal maintenance based on the wife's need as supported by evidence in the record.

State v. Townsend


No. 18866, 1993 Opinion No. 139


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


124 Idaho 881; 865 P.2d 972; 1993 Ida. LEXIS 199



December 28, 1993  
December 28, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District, State of Idaho, Nez Perce County. Honorable Ron Schilling, District Judge. Appeal from sentencing order withholding judgment of conviction for aggravated battery.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of December 2, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Ida. LEXIS 174.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the District Court of the Second Judicial District (Idaho), which sentenced him pursuant to his conviction for felony aggravated battery and misdemeanor assault. The district court denied appellant's motion for a new trial and in effect granted his motion for acquittal on the simple assault conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant drove his pick-up truck into his wife's car, smashed her car window with a tire iron, and attacked her. He was convicted of aggravated battery on the first count and simple assault on the second count. The court vacated his conviction and remanded the matter for a new trial. The court found that the jury verdict was not inconsistent because the jury could have found that the tire iron was the instrumentality of the assault and either his vehicle or his hands were the instrumentality of the battery. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict of aggravated battery based upon appellant's use of his vehicle to strike the car which his wife was driving. The court held that the district court erred in permitting the jury to consider appellant's hands as deadly weapons in his attack upon his wife and vacated appellant's conviction. The court concluded that because the verdict did not specify whether the battery was committed by the use of appellant's hands or his vehicle, the cause had to be remanded for a new trial. The jury instructions as to the lesser included offenses were proper.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant's aggravated battery conviction and remanded for a new trial.

 

92 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Rhodes v. Industrial Comm'n


S. CT. NO. 20322


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


125 Idaho 139; 868 P.2d 467; 1993 Ida. LEXIS 188



December 3, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for peremptory writ of prohibition in an original proceeding before the Idaho Supreme Court.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, injured industrial workers (workers), attorneys, and others, sought an ex parte temporary stay and a peremptory writ of prohibition to prevent the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho (Commission) from implementing regulations restricting the amount of legal fees recoverable by attorneys representing injured workers. The workers argued that the commission exceeded its authority and the regulations violated due process.


OVERVIEW: In promulgating the regulations, the Commission had a major concern that fees charged by claimants' attorneys in workers' compensation cases were unduly high. The court initially granted the petition for ex parte stay pending the court hearing. In denying the petition for a peremptory writ of prohibition, the court first determined that the authority granted to the Commission under Idaho Code § 72-803, to "approve" attorney fees, did not conflict with the judicial penumbra affecting the practice of law. The regulation promulgated to foster ease, utility, and predictability in the application of § 72-803, did not overstep the legislative bounds of § 72-803, read in pari materia with the entire Workers' Compensation Act. The regulation restricting the amount of legal fees recoverable was not a fee schedule. It was a framework establishing uniform grounds for fee approval. The court then determined that the challenged regulation created no suspect or invidiously discriminatory classification, entangled no fundamental right, and did not restrain due process or equal protection under the United States or Idaho Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court denied the workers' petition for a peremptory writ of prohibition to prevent the Commission from implementing regulations restricting the amount of legal fees recoverable by attorneys representing injured workers.

Rincover v. State

Appeal from order denying application for registration of securities salesperson.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant appealed from an order of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which affirmed an order of respondent state department of finance denying the applicant's registration as a securities salesperson.


OVERVIEW: The applicant had been a registered securities salesperson for several years. The department conducted an investigation of the applicant's conduct as a securities salesperson. The court agreed and held that the notice to the applicant of the reasons for the denial prior to a hearing did not adequately notify the applicant of the reasons upon which the denial was based after a hearing. Nez Perce Tribe v. Cenarrusa


S.Ct. No. 20281, 1993 Opinion No. 113


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


125 Idaho 37; 867 P.2d 911; 1993 Ida. LEXIS 172



October 5, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On petition for writ of mandamus or other relief brought by members of the Nez Perce Tribe arising from the passage of an amendment to the Idaho Constitution. The Supreme Court, Trout, J., held that the amendment was submitted to the electorate in conformance with statutory and constitutional requirements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tribe challenged an order of the lower court (Idaho) that determined that a proposed amendment, which clarified the state's policy on gambling and specifically prohibited casino gambling within the state, Idaho Const. art. III, § 20, was appropriately submitted to the electorate.


OVERVIEW: The Idaho Legislature introduced a constitutional amendment addressing the issue of gambling. Tribe filed a petition for an extraordinary writ of mandamus to prohibit the proposed amendment, which declared that gambling was strictly prohibited, from being presented on the election ballot. The electorate voted in favor of the amendment and tribe challenged the results, arguing that the amendment violated Idaho Const. art. III, § 20. The court disagreed, finding that the amendment's meaning and purpose was properly prepared by the legislature. The amendment was broader than merely concerning Indian gaming and the language was not misleading or deceptive. Further, the court found that the amendment was properly presented to the electorate. The court disagreed with tribe's argument that the amendment involved multiple subject matter, which should have been presented separately. The issue was not merely whether the matters in an amendment could be divided into separate questions, but whether the matters were incongruous and essentially unrelated. Although the provisions might be separable, they did not appear to be incongruous and essentially unrelated.


OUTCOME: The court found that an amendment to the state constitution was properly presented for voter approval where the amendment adequately described its meaning and purpose in a statement for the electorate and while the issues in the amendment could be viewed as separable, they were not incongruous and essentially unrelated.

Lubcke v. Boise City/Ada County Hous. Auth.


No. 18691, 1993 Opinion No. 107


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


124 Idaho 450; 860 P.2d 653; 1993 Ida. LEXIS 165



September 9, 1993  
September 9, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 27, 1993. Rehearing Denied October 27, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ida. LEXIS 177.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Ada. Honorable Deborah A. Bail, District Judge. This 42 U.S.C. § 1983 action arose from respondent's termination from her position of employment with the Boise City/Ada County Housing Authority ("Housing Authority"). Defendants-appellants appeal from the judgment of the district court awarding respondent $ 182,703.00 in damages for breach of contract, deprivation of procedural due process, and deprivation of free speech. Defendants-appellants also appeal from the district court's denial of post-trial motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, new trial, and remittitur.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of April 3, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Ida. LEXIS 85.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, housing authority and executive director of the housing authority, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District (Idaho), which awarded respondent employee damages for breach of contract, deprivation of procedural due process, and deprivation of free speech. They also appealed the denial of post-trial motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, new trial, and remittitur.


OVERVIEW: The employee was publicly critical of her supervisor. When a new supervisor was hired, she fired the employee. The court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to grant a judgment notwithstanding the verdict or new trial on the issue of liability because there was sufficient evidence to show that the housing authority breached the employment contract, that it was acting under color of state law for purposes of the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim, that the employee was terminated without due process of law, and that the employee's right to free speech was infringed. The court held that the trial court erred in allowing the jury to decide the legal component of the qualified immunity test as it applied to the executive director. As to damages, the court found that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on reputational damages on the § 1983 claim. The court also found that the trial court did not engage in the proper analysis under Idaho R. Civ. P. 59(a)(5) as to the award of damages on the breach of contract and free speech claims. The court held that the employee was the prevailing party on her § 1983 claim for the purpose of an award of attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as to liability. The court remanded the case for a determination as to whether the executive director was entitled to qualified immunity on the free speech claim. The court vacated the award of damages on the procedural due process claim and remanded the case for determination of the amount of damages on all three claims and of the amount of attorney fees to which the employee was entitled.

State v. Raudebaugh


No. 19551, 1993 Opinion No. 106


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


124 Idaho 758; 864 P.2d 596; 1993 Ida. LEXIS 164



September 8, 1993  
September 8, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended September 14, 1993. Rehearing Denied December 29, 1993. Released for Publication December 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. James Judd, District Judge. Appeal from convictions of second-degree murder and use of a deadly weapon in the commission of the murder.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County, that convicted him on charges of second-degree murder and use of a deadly weapon in the commission of the murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second-degree murder and use of a deadly weapon in the commission of the murder. Defendant alleged that the acquittal instructions violated Idaho Code § 19-2132(c), that the prosecution's witness was improperly allowed to give expert testimony regarding blood spatter evidence, that testimony was improperly admitted to the effect that he was collecting a drug debt on the night of the murder, and that the prosecutor's closing argument constituted misconduct. The court affirmed, holding that under § 19-2132(c), the jury was properly instructed that it could not consider a lesser-included offense unless it found defendant not guilty as to each of the greater offenses. The court held that the district court did not abuse its discretion in allowing a witness to testify as an expert on blood spatter evidence, and that it properly balanced the prejudicial and probative value of the evidence before admitting testimony that defendant sought to collect a drug debt from the murder victim. The court found no fundamental error in the prosecutor's closing argument, which highlighted the conflict between defendant's testimony and the evidence produced at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court, which convicted defendant of second-degree murder and use of a deadly weapon in the commission of the murder.

 

97 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wood


S.Ct. NO. 19731, 1993 Opinion No. 104


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


125 Idaho 911; 876 P.2d 1352; 1993 Ida. LEXIS 162



September 2, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonner County. Honorable James R. Michaud, District Judge. Appeal from order denying motion to correct illegal sentence.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, which denied his motion to correct an illegal sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially charged with robbery and attempted first-degree murder in connection with a robbery and shooting of a store owner. Defendant was also charged with grand theft in connection with the theft of a gun on the day before the shooting. As part of a negotiated plea agreement, defendant pleaded guilty to attempted first-degree murder and the robbery and grand theft charges were dismissed. At sentencing, the trial court stated that while it had advised defendant prior to accepting his guilty plea that the maximum penalty for attempted first-degree murder was one-half of a life sentence, defendant had not been advised as to what that was in terms of years. The trial court then informed defendant what his sentence would be and offered defendant the opportunity to withdraw his plea. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the trial court was authorized to establish a base maximum sentence upon the conviction of an attempt to commit a crime punishable by life imprisonment. Furthermore, defendant's sentence was within the statutory limits and was legal because the trial court fixed a base maximum sentence based on defendant's life expectancy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.

ACLU v. Echohawk


Nos. 20613, 20618, 1993 Opinion No. 90


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


124 Idaho 147; 857 P.2d 626; 1993 Ida. LEXIS 148



August 3, 1993  
August 3, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Prohibition pursuant to I.C. § 34-1809, from the Idaho Attorney General's short and long titles for an initiative petition. Honorable Larry EchoHawk, Attorney General.



DISPOSITION: Titles certified, as written by the Attorney General, to the Secretary of State.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, American Civil Liberties Union (ACLU) and committee formed to stop special rights, sought writs of prohibition, claiming that respondent Attorney General of the State of Idaho (attorney general) did not provide proper short and long titles under Idaho Code § 34-1809 to an initiative proposed by a citizen's alliance on the treatment of homosexuality.


OVERVIEW: The citizen's alliance submitted a proposed initiative regarding state law treatment of homosexuality to the attorney general. The proposed initiative prohibited affording homosexuals minority status. The attorney general was required to draft short and long titles for the initiative under § 34-1809. Section 34-1809 required the short title to capture the distinctive nature of the initiative in a very limited number of words and the long title to convey the purpose of the measure. The attorney general drafted the titles. The ACLU filed a petition for a writ of prohibition, alleging that the titles were insufficient and unfair. The committee also filed a petition claiming that the long title could be understood to mean that the initiative gave special rights to minorities. The court certified the short and long titles as written. The court reasoned that the attorney general's short title was a true and impartial statement of the initiative and represented its distinctive characteristics. The court also explained that the long title expressed the purpose of the initiative without being argumentative or prejudicial even though there were other acceptable ways to write the title.


OUTCOME: The court certified the attorney general's short and long titles for the initiative as written in the ACLU and the committee's petitions for writs of prohibition.

 

99 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pratt


S. CT. NO. 18485, 1993 Opinion No. 83


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


1993 Ida. LEXIS 140



July 27, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended July 29, 1993. As Corrected August 5, 1993. Withdrawn March 18, 1994; Substituted Opinion Reported at: 1993 Ida. LEXIS 38.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bonner. Honorable Watt E. Prather, District Judge.

Appellant, Joseph Earl Pratt ("Pratt"), appeals from the judgments of conviction and sentences on several counts, including first degree murder.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a ruling from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho which, on a jury verdict, found defendant guilty of first degree burglary, robbery, second degree kidnapping, ten counts of aggravated assault, aggravated assault upon a law enforcement officer, attempted first degree murder, and first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: After the grand jury indicted defendant, the State gave notice of its intent to seek the death penalty; defendant pled not guilty to all counts. After the jury verdict, the trial court concluded that the death penalty would be unjust because defendant did not fire the fatal shots. For first degree murder, defendant received a life sentence, the first 25 years of which were fixed; the sentence would run consecutive to all other sentences that stemmed from the instant convictions. Defendant appealed pursuant to Idaho App. R. 11, and the court vacated defendant's conviction for attempted felony murder, holding that there was no such crime in Idaho. The sentences imposed were not excessive because defendant and his brother placed the lives of several people in danger, refused to surrender until a police officer was killed, and committed several other crimes in the process. Idaho Code § 19-2132 (1988) did not violate the right to a jury trial as guaranteed by Idaho Const. art. I, § 7; the jury still had to find defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of every fact necessary to constitute the crimes charged. The jury still had the power to find defendant guilty of a lesser offense.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction and sentence for attempted felony murder and affirmed the convictions and sentences on all other counts.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of burglary, robbery, kidnapping, aggravated assault, aggravated assault upon a law enforcement officer, attempted first degree murder, and first degree murder. The District Court of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bonner sentenced defendant to prison sentences and to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed a United States Forest Service officer (officer) and shot at another after he fled his attempted burglary. The court reversed the attempted felony murder conviction because that was not a crime. Though the death penalty was constitutional and properly considered by the trial court, the court reversed the death penalty sentence where defendant's nature was disproportional to the sentence under Idaho Code § 19-3827. OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the conviction for attempted felony murder and the death sentence. The court affirmed all other convictions and sentences.

State v. Dunlap


S. CT. NO. 19928, 1993 Opinion No. 84


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


125 Idaho 530; 873 P.2d 784; 1993 Ida. LEXIS 142



July 27, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 5, 1993. Rehearing Denied September 28, 1993. Released for Publication October 1, 1993.
Writ of certiorari denied Dunlap v. Idaho, 510 U.S. 1171, 114 S. Ct. 1207, 127 L. Ed. 2d 554, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 2036 (1994)
Post-conviction relief denied at Dunlap v. State, 146 Idaho 197, 192 P.3d 1021, 2008 Ida. LEXIS 205 (Idaho, 2008)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at, in part, Remanded by State v. Dunlap, 155 Idaho 345, 313 P.3d 1, 2013 Ida. LEXIS 262 (Idaho, 2013)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Dunlap v. State, 2015 Ida. LEXIS 273 (Idaho, Nov. 2, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Caribou. Honorable W.H. Woodland, District Judge. Plaintiff, Timothy Alan Dunlap ("Dunlap"), pled guilty to first degree murder and was sentenced to death for the killing of Tonya Crane. Dunlap appeals his sentence, arguing that the trial court's findings in aggravation are not supported by the evidence and that Idaho's death penalty statute, I.C. § 19-2515(c), is unconstitutional. Dunlap also argues that the sentence of death in this case was excessive and disproportionate.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence ordered in the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Caribou, which imposed the death penalty after defendant pled guilty to first degree murder for the killing of a bank employee during a robbery of the bank. Defendant appealed the trial court's finding of two aggravating circumstances under Idaho Code § 19-2515(g)(7), (g)(8).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for killing a woman in Ohio 10 days before killing a bank employee during a bank robbery in Idaho. Defendant was charged with first degree murder in Idaho and pled guilty. The trial court held a sentencing hearing, and defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed his sentence, asserting that the trial court's findings as to two aggravating circumstances were not proven beyond a reasonable doubt and that the death penalty statute, Idaho Code § 19-2515(c), was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the sentence, finding that two aggravating circumstances under § 19-2515(g)(7), (g)(8) existed beyond a reasonable doubt and outweighed the mitigating evidence. The overwhelming evidence demonstrated by any objective standard that the state proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had the specific intent to kill the victim and that he committed the robbery with the specific intent to kill. Evidence of the prior crime in Ohio was properly admitted at the sentencing hearing as proof of defendant's propensity to commit murder, causing him to be a threat to society and satisfying the requirements of the death penalty statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court sentencing defendant to death was affirmed.

Heck v. Comm'rs of Canyon County

DISPOSITION: Reversed, as to prohibition on the retail of safe and sane fireworks; vacated, as to the due process claim; and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff firework store owners appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Idaho), which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant county in the owner's declaratory judgment action challenging the validity of a county fireworks ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The owners operated a firework store in the county. The county passed an ordinance prohibiting the sale of safe and sane fireworks in the county. The county denied the owners' petition for a permit. The owners argued that the fireworks ordinance was in conflict with the Idaho State Fireworks Law, Idaho Code §§ 39-2605 to 39-2630, and that the county unlawfully applied the building code ordinance retroactively to an existing building. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the county. The court determined that because the legislature did not state any role for local government units in regulating the retail sale of safe and sane fireworks, the legislature intended to preempt the regulation of retail sales of safe and sane fireworks. The court further found that the trial court incorrectly dismissed the owner's claim that the portion of the ordinance regarding the building requirements was unconstitutional. The court determined that the question of the reasonableness of the requirements of the fireworks ordinance for issuing a permit to the owners was a question of fact that could not have been resolved on a motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court awarded costs, but not attorney fees, to the owners.

Frontier Fed. Sav. & Loan Ass'n v. Douglass


No. 18748


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


123 Idaho 808; 853 P.2d 553; 1993 Ida. LEXIS 128

Original Opinion of April 23, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ida. LEXIS 96.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, mortgagees, appealed the grant of summary judgment from the District Court of the First Judicial District (Idaho) in favor of plaintiff mortgagor in an action to recover a deficiency judgment after foreclosure on a deed of trust.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor brought an action against the mortgagees to recover a deficiency judgment after foreclosure on a deed of trust. Both parties moved for summary judgment. The trial court granted the mortgagor's motion for summary judgment and awarded attorney fees. The mortgagees appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that the mortgagor was not precluded from recovery under either estoppel or waiver theories. Also, mortgagees were not prejudiced by mortgagor's delay in depositing deed of trust with successor trustee. Further, the trustee was obligated to accept the bid of the only bidder at the foreclosure sale, even if the bidder was the mortgagor. Finally, the court stated that the mortgagor was entitled to recover attorney fees because the note provided that the mortgagees would pay such fees in the event an action was brought to collect on the note.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment entered in favor of the mortgagor to recover a deficiency judgment after foreclosure on a deed of trust was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant common law husband challenged the decision of the District Court, Fifth Judicial District, Blaine County (Idaho), which entered judgment on a jury verdict in favor of appellee abused common law wife, who had shared home and intimate relations for over 10 years with her common law husband, and awarded a large sum of compensatory damages for battery and intentional infliction of emotional distress, and $ 725,000 in punitive damages.

The court held that: 1. The claim of intentional infliction of emotional distress was a continuing tort for the purposes of the statute of limitations; 2. The evidence was sufficient to conclude that the common law husband's conduct toward the common law wife was beyond that which a reasonable person should be expected to tolerate or endure so as to a state a claim for intentional infliction of emotional distress; and 3. Remand was required due to the lower court's failure to adequately discuss findings necessary to rule on a motion for new trial based on the excessiveness of punitive damages where the lower court did not give any indication that it had a definite amount in mind when weighing the question of damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the lower court's decision which entered judgment on a jury verdict in favor of the abused common law wife on the wife's intentional infliction of emotional distress and battery claims. The court vacated as to the motion for new trial on the issue of excessive damages and remanded for further findings.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, the Honorable Gerald Schroeder, District Judge. The district court granted the respondents' motion to dismiss the appellants' complaints, which sought a judgment declaring Idaho's system of funding public schools to be unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, education association, school district and taxpayers, sought review of a decision from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District (Idaho) granting respondent states' motion to dismiss appellants' claims for failure to state a cause of action and for lack of standing. Appellants alleged the current system of funding public schools was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, education association, school district and taxpayers, filed a suit against respondent State of Idaho alleging that the current system of funding public schools was unconstitutional because it did not provide a thorough education. Appellants further alleged that the disparities in funding caused by the property-tax funded system resulted in a system that did not provide a uniform education and violated the equal protection clause. The court affirmed the district court's order dismissing the causes of action which alleged that the school funding system did not provide a uniform system of education and alleged a violation of the equal protection clause. The court held that judicial precedent mandated dismissal of appellants' uniformity and equal protection claims since a funding system which created unequal per student expenditures did not violate the constitution. The court reversed the dismissal of the causes of action alleging the funding system did not provide a thorough education and concluded appellants had alleged facts which, if proven at trial, would entitle them to relief. The order dismissing appellant taxpayers from the suit for lack of standing was affirmed.

The court reversed the dismissal of appellants' causes of action which alleged the funding system did not provide a thorough education. The order dismissing appellant taxpayer/citizens from the suit was also affirmed.

Harris v. Dep't of Health & Welfare


No. 19514, 1992 Opinion No. 149


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


123 Idaho 295; 847 P.2d 1156; 1992 Ida. LEXIS 189



December 31, 1992  
December 31, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 25, 1993. Released for Publication March 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bonneville. Honorable Ted V. Wood, District Judge. Appeal from the district court's grant of respondents' motion for summary judgment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho granted summary judgment, citing Idaho Code § 6-904A(2), to respondent State of Idaho, Department of Health and Welfare (department) in the claim appellant, an elderly victim of a violent and sexual crime, brought seeking to impose vicarious liability for injuries sustained from an allegedly negligently managed juvenile in the care and custody of the department.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was convicted of a crime against nature, rape, grand theft, and second-degree burglary, all perpetrated against the victim. The juvenile had no prior record involving sexual misconduct, violent aggression, or any felony. Evaluations revealed his angry nature and proclivity to aggression and the possibility of sexual crimes against his female peers. He was released to his parents, and the department lost touch with him shortly before the crimes. The court ruled that the evidence did not show the reckless, willful, and wanton conduct necessary for liability under § 6-903, noting that nothing in the juvenile's antecedent behavior or present comportment presaged the vicious exploits committed against the victim such that a reasonable person could have foreseen the need to restrain him. The most drastic prediction recorded was that the juvenile might have been an above average sexual risk to his female peers, which the victim was not. The court noted that the Youth Rehabilitation Act, Idaho Code § 16-1801, required the least restrictive setting necessary. Using the rational basis test, the court held the limitation of state liability in Idaho Code § 6-904A constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment granted the department on the basis of governmental immunity in the suit the victim brought to hold it vicariously liable for the injuries she suffered from the criminal acts of a juvenile who was in the department's custody.

State v. Beloit


No. 19240, 1992 Opinion No. 148


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


123 Idaho 36; 844 P.2d 18; 1992 Ida. LEXIS 187



December 30, 1992  
December 30, 1992, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Nez Perce County. Hon. Ron Schilling, District Judge.

Appeal from denial of motion in limine seeking to prevent admission of two prior DUI convictions; denial of motion to dismiss; conviction for felony DUI.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prior to entering his conditional plea of guilty, defendant brought a motion in limine that sought to prevent admission of two prior convictions for purposes of felony enhancement. The District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Nez Perce County, denied the motion and convicted defendant for driving under the influence of alcohol. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the lower court erred in denying his motion in limine. The court rejected this claim, held that the prior convictions were valid and properly considered by the lower court, and affirmed defendant's conviction. The court found that, at the hearing on his motion in limine, defendant did not present any evidence, but argued that, even though the state's documents showed that he waived his constitutional rights, the documents did not show that he did this knowingly and intelligently. The court found that, once the state made a prima facie showing of the validity of the prior convictions used to enhance a pending crime, defendant had the burden of going forward with proof that the convictions were defective because of the denial of some constitutional right. Because defendant failed to meet his burden of establishing that the prior convictions were defective, the court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion in limine and affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of driving under the influence of alcohol.

 

109 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Guzman


No. 17716


Supreme Court of Idaho


122 Idaho 981; 842 P.2d 660; 1992 Ida. LEXIS 163



November 5, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted January 25, 1991. Released for Publication November 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of November 19, 1990, Reported at: 1990 Ida. LEXIS 188.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the trial court's (Idaho) application of the Leon "good faith" exception to the exclusionary rule, which resulted in the admission of evidence obtained in violation of defendant's U.S. Const. amend. IV and Idaho Const. art. 1, § 17 rights. Defendant also challenged the trial court's refusal to order the state to disclose the identity of a confidential informant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's residence was searched pursuant to a search warrant that, under the "totality of the circumstances" test, the lower court found improper since the magistrate did not have sufficient facts necessary before him to find probable cause. The lower court, however, ruled that under the Leon "good faith" exception to the exclusionary rule set forth by the United States Supreme Court, evidence obtained pursuant to the warrant should not be excluded. On appeal, the court rejected the "good faith" exception to the exclusionary rule. The court found that, unlike the federal exclusionary rule, the state exclusionary rule was created for a greater purpose than mere deterrence. It was created to protect the integrity of the warrant issuing process as a whole. Thus, the court ruled that Idaho Const. art. I, § 17 conferred broader protection than did U.S. Const. amend. IV and that the evidence against defendant should have been suppressed. The court also ruled that denial of review by the court carried no more weight than denial of certiorari by the United States Supreme Court, thus rejecting the Hays "review denied" rule.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order from the lower court, ruling that Idaho did not abide by the "good faith" exception to the exclusionary rule and that, thus, defendant's motion to suppress was improperly denied. The court also expressly disavowed the Hays "review denied" rule.
