Mortimer v. Riviera Apartments


No. 19425, 1992 Opinion No. 119


Supreme Court of Idaho


122 Idaho 839; 840 P.2d 383; 1992 Ida. LEXIS 157



October 22, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Industrial Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant, who applied for worker's compensation benefits, appealed an order of the Industrial Commission (Idaho), which determined that the claimant was entitled to benefits but denied claimant's post-hearing motions to amend his pleading. Appellee employer filed a cross-appeal from the Commission's findings that the claimant was an employee who was acting within the scope of his employment at the time of the injury.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after the injury, the claimant was placed on the payroll of another company in which the employer was a majority stockholder. In determining that the claimant was an employee of the employer, the Commission rejected the employer's claims that the claimant was either the other company's employee or an independent contractor. After the commission determined the employer's liability, the claimant moved for an order to change the caption of his complaint to include the alleged owners of the employer's business as defendants. The Commission denied the motion on the ground that it was made after liability was determined. In vacating the order in part on appeal, the court held that the Commission erred in denying the claimant's motion to change the caption because there was no time limitation on such motions under the Commission's rules of procedure and there was no evidence that the amendment would have prejudiced the owners. The court affirmed the order in part, finding substantial evidence to support the commission's findings that the claimant was the employer's employee because the employer exercised control over the time, manner, method, and details of the claimant's work.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order in part with regard to, among other things, the findings that the claimant was the employer's employee and that the employer was liable. The court vacated the order in part with regard to the denial of the claimant's motion to change the caption of his complaint. The case was remanded for a determination as to whether an amendment of the caption would have prejudiced the owners.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner appealed from an order of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief. OVERVIEW: The prisoner filed a petition for post-conviction relief after his conviction was affirmed on appeal. The petition asserted 17 causes of action as grounds for relief. Bott v. Idaho State Bldg. Auth.


No. 18540, 1992 Opinion No. 105


Supreme Court of Idaho


122 Idaho 471; 835 P.2d 1282; 1992 Ida. LEXIS 142



August 7, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 31, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. The Honorable Deborah A. Bail, District Judge presiding.

Bott, Berg, and Hoar appeal the district court's grant of the Idaho State Building Authority's motion for a new trial on the issue of damages. The Authority cross-appeals the district court's denial of its motion for judgment n.o.v., and from the denial of its motion for a new trial on the issue of liability.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff architects sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which granted defendant Idaho State Building Authority's motion for a new trial on the issue of damages. The authority cross-appealed the district court's denial of its motion for judgment n.o.v. and the denial of its motion for a new trial on the issue of liability.


OVERVIEW: The architects and the authority entered into a contract providing that architects would provide architectural and other services for a building project. The architects were terminated before they were able to complete the construction phase of the project. After their termination, they brought an action seeking compensation for work they had completed in providing the project design. At trial, the jury found that the architects had substantially performed under the contract, that the authority had breached the contract, and it awarded damages. The trial court granted a new trial confined to the issue of the architects' damages. The architects appealed, and the authority cross-appealed. The court remanded and held that (1) since the trial court did not discuss whether substantial evidence supported the jury's award of damages to architects, and only addressed the jury's finding of liability, it did not adequately address the authority's motion for a judgment n.o.v.; (2) on remand the trial court must clarify the rationale utilized in granting a new trial on the issue of damages; and (3) the trial court's refusal to give the authority's requested jury instructions was proper.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the action to the district court for reconsideration of the authority's motion for judgment n.o.v. on the issue of damages and for clarification of the basis or bases for the new trial order.

Krueger v. Bd. of Prof'l Discipline of Idaho State Bd. of Med.


No. 19323, 1992 Opinion No. 96


Supreme Court of Idaho


122 Idaho 577; 836 P.2d 523; 1992 Ida. LEXIS 134



July 8, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1992. Released for Publication September 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable G.D. Carey, District Judge.

An appeal from an order of the district court remanding for further findings. The order of the district court is reversed as to patients A, B, C, D and E, and is affirmed as to patients F and H.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Professional Discipline of the Idaho State Board of Medicine (board) challenged an order of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which reversed the board's decision in a disciplinary proceeding against respondent doctor with regard to one patient and remanded for further findings and conclusions as to five other patients. The doctor cross-appealed the trial court's decision.


OVERVIEW: The board initiated disciplinary proceedings against the doctor for violations of Idaho Code § 54-1814(7), alleging incidents of breach of the standard of care. The board issued its findings of fact, conclusions of law, and final order, finding that the doctor had violated the community standard of care in the treatment of seven patients, and revoking his license, but staying the revocation under certain conditions. The doctor appealed that decision. The trial court remanded to the board for further findings and conclusions as to five of the patients involved in the complaints against the doctor, reversed the board with regard to its findings as to one of the patients, and affirmed the board as to an evidentiary ruling with regard to another patient's matter. Both sides appealed. Upon review, the court reversed the trial court's order remanding the decisions as to the five patients and affirmed the findings as to the other two patients. The court held, among other things, that § 54-1814(7) was not vague on its face, and affirmed the trial court's finding that the board correctly refused to consider a jury verdict in the doctor's favor in one patient's malpractice action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, remanding the decisions as to five patients, and affirmed the trial court's findings as to two patients.

Osick v. Public Employee Ret. Sys.


No. 18836, 1992 Opinion No. 84


Supreme Court of Idaho


122 Idaho 457; 835 P.2d 1268; 1992 Ida. LEXIS 116



June 8, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Alan M. Schwartzman, District Judge. Appeal from order affirming decision of Public Employee Retirement System of Idaho board offsetting workers' compensation benefits against disability retirement benefits.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an employee of a the highway department and a member of the Public Employee Retirement System (PERSI), sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which found in favor of PERSI on his action challenging a decision of the PERSI board upholding an offset against his disability retirement benefits the annual amount payable to him as workers' compensation.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured on the job and was awarded a lump sum plus monthly compensation. PERSI approved his application for disability retirement and, pursuant to Idaho Code. § 59-1320(1)(b), offset the workers' compensation payments against the disability retirement benefits. The board upheld the offset, the trial court upheld the board, and on appeal, he asserted that he was entitled to full payment of his disability retirement benefits and reimbursement of past amounts offset. The court affirmed, holding that § 72-318 did not prohibit the offset and that the offset did not violate the right to equal protection of the laws. The legislative goal in requiring the offset at issue was obviously the adequate funding and actuarial soundness of PERSI. The statute advanced that goal in a rational fashion.


OUTCOME: The judgment upholding the decision of the PERSI board was affirmed.

State v. Doyle

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Alan Schwartzman, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from district court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a guilty plea to the charge of felony child custody interference, and he appealed a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which denied his motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the crime of felony child custody interference pursuant to Idaho Code § 18-4506. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Defendant then entered a guilty plea to the charge, and appealed the ruling on the jurisdictional issue. The court held that even though defendant was not in Idaho before or after he refused to return custody of the child to the child's mother, the keeping or withholding and the deprivation of the custodial rights of the mother occurred in Idaho where the mother was a resident; thus Idaho had jurisdiction over the crime. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction the charge of felony child custody interference.

 

116 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Winn


No. 18786


Supreme Court of Idaho


121 Idaho 850; 828 P.2d 879; 1992 Ida. LEXIS 59



March 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 17, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bingham County. Honorable James C. Herndon, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from conviction of murder in the first degree. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District (Idaho), for first-degree murder in the poisoning death of her nine year old son.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that: (1) admitting photographs of the victim laying on an autopsy table was not improper because such evidence in a homicide case could aid the jury as proof of the corpus delicti, the extent of injury, the condition of the body, and the degree and atrociousness of the crime; (2) excluding the pastor's testimony as to "demonic possession" or defendant's mental condition was not improper because a foundation had not been laid and the witness's expertise had not been established; and (3) denying defendant's motion for change of venue was not improper because defendant did not have difficulty selecting a jury, did not challenge any juror for cause, and did not show that pretrial publicity affected the jurors. The court also concluded that a justiciable controversy did not exist to support a ruling on whether Idaho Code § 18-207(a), which eliminated the insanity defense, was unconstitutional because defendant failed to indicate that mental condition was an issue or to present evidence from the psychologist who examined defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder.

 

117 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Tiffany v. Payette


No. 18881


Supreme Court of Idaho


121 Idaho 396; 825 P.2d 493; 1992 Ida. LEXIS 13



January 30, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended February 4, 1992. Released for Publication February 21, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Payette. Honorable Gerald L. Weston, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the district court's denial of appellant's motion to amend. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a city employee, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of the Third Judicial District, in and for the County of Payette (Idaho), which found in favor of respondent employer on a claim alleging wrongful termination of employment, deprivation of civil rights, and violation of substantive due process rights. The employee also challenged the trial court's denial of a motion to amend findings.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who worked for the police department, was discharged after a hearing for failure to comply with the city's residency requirement. The requirement was clearly stated in the employee policy manual. The court determined that the trial court's finding that the employee was in breach of the residency requirement was not clearly erroneous. A city residency rule was a continuing residency requirement, not a durational residency requirement; hence, it did not affect the fundamental right to travel and was not evaluated under a strict scrutiny standard. Applying the rational basis standard, the court held that the residency requirement did not violate the employee's equal protection rights. Although the employee was not immediately discharged upon the discovery of her residency violation, the court ruled that the delay did not give rise to equitable estoppel or waiver. Because the employer followed its stated procedures in terminating the employee, she had no due process claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the employer and the denial of the employee's motion to amend findings.

State v. Card


No. 18313, 1991 Opinion No. 130


Supreme Court of Idaho


121 Idaho 425; 825 P.2d 1081; 1991 Ida. LEXIS 197



December 31, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 21, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: FILED SEPTEMBER 20, 1991 IS HEREBY WITHDRAWN AND THIS OPINION SUBSTITUTED THEREFOR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death by an Idaho trial court. The reviewing court undertook an automatic review of death penalty case, as required by Idaho Code § 19-2827. It also considered the defendant's grounds for appeal, including the constitutionality of the abolition of the insanity defense and of the language of Idaho Code § 19-2515.


OVERVIEW: The court reviewed all of the issues raised by the defendant and performed an independent review of the record as required by Idaho Code § 19-2827, and it found no reversible error. The court specifically upheld the validity of Idaho Code § 18-207 regarding the insanity defense, finding that there was no constitutionally basis requiring that a defendant have a right to an insanity defense. The court further found that the aggravating circumstances, pursuant to Idaho Code § 19-2515(g)(2), was sound and that the trial court appropriately balanced aggravating circumstances behind the crime with mitigating factors to reach its death penalty verdict. The court held that the victim impact statements contained in the presentence report were not error, and whereas the statements as to sentence were not considered by the trial judge in imposing the death penalty, there was no reversible error. The court held that the provisions of Idaho Code § 19-2719, which imposed a time limit on capital appeals, were constitutional and did not violate the defendant's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders of conviction and the death sentences for first degree murder against the defendant.

Habeas corpus proceeding at Leavitt v. Arave, 927 F. Supp. 394, 1996 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 10333 (D. Idaho, 1996)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at State v. Leavitt, 2005 Ida. LEXIS 96 (Idaho, June 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bingham County. Honorable H. Reynold George, District Judge.
Idaho v. Leavitt, 493 U.S. 923, 107 L. Ed. 2d 270, 110 S. Ct. 290, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 4964 (1989)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from imposition of death penalty. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the imposition of the death penalty entered by the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. On his first appeal, his conviction was affirmed, but the death penalty sentence was reversed. Upon remand, the district court, after weighing all the mitigating factors against the aggravating circumstance that the crime was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel, manifesting exceptional depravity as provided by Idaho Code § 19-2515(g)(5), and contemplating alternative sentencing possibilities as directed on remand, for a second time sentenced defendant to death. The court ruled that to make reference at sentencing to the evidence shown in the crime scene photographs and photographs of the victim's body was not error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's death penalty sentence imposed following his conviction for first degree murder.

State v. Card


No. 18313


Supreme Court of Idaho


1991 Ida. LEXIS 155



September 20, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Withdrawn on Denial of Rehearing, Reported at 1991 Ida. LEXIS 195.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Honorable Jim R. Doolittle, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from convictions of first degree murder and subsequent sentence of death. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of two counts of first-degree murder. The District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County, sentenced defendant to death. Defendant sought review of his convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of, and sentenced to death for, murdering two people in the parking lot of a convenience store. On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of the legislative abolishment of the insanity defense, Idaho Code § 18-207, the constitutionality of the state's capital sentencing procedures, and the limitations on petitions for post-conviction relief in capital cases, Idaho Code § 19-2719. The court affirmed the convictions and sentence, holding that (1) the due process provisions of the United States and Idaho Constitutions did not mandate that a defendant be allowed to present an insanity defense in a capital case, (2) the 42-day time limit set forth in Idaho Code § 19-2719 for post-conviction relief petitions was rationally related to the legitimate legislative purpose of expediting constitutionally imposed death sentences, (3) though it ultimately based its decision on other factors, the trial court was entitled to consider the victim impact statements in its sentencing decision, and (4) the "utter disregard for human life" aggravating circumstance, Idaho Code § 19-2515(g)(6), was not impermissibly vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' murder convictions and sentence of death.

State v. Rhoades


Nos. 17521, 18285


Supreme Court of Idaho


120 Idaho 795; 820 P.2d 665; 1991 Ida. LEXIS 147



September 12, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication October 11, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 12, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bingham. Honorable James C. Herndon, District Judge.

Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, first degree kidnapping robbery, and the use of firearms in the commission of these crimes. The death sentence was imposed. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bingham convicted defendant for first-degree murder, first-degree kidnapping robbery, and the use of firearms in the commission of those crimes. The trial court sentenced the defendant to death sentence. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of the defendant's conviction and death sentence, the issues were whether the legislative abolition of the defense of mental condition in criminal cases violated the Idaho or United States Constitutions; whether the trial court erroneously considered victim impact statements; whether the trial court erred in compelling a defense expert to prepare a written report or submit to an interview before testifying; and whether the death penalty was the death sentence was excessive. The court held that: (1) the trial court properly determined that the record did not create a justiciable controversy to support a ruling on the issue of the repeal of the insanity defense; (2) the trial court erred in admitting victim impact statements in the presentence investigation report, but the error was harmless because the victim impact statements did not influence the trial court in its imposition of sentence; (3) the trial court violated Idaho Crim. R. 16(c)(2) in ordering a defense expert to prepare a report for opposing counsel, but the error was harmless because it did not result in prejudice to the defendant; and (4) an adequate basis existed for imposing the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted the defendant for murder, kidnapping, and the use of firearms and sentenced him to death.

DISPOSITION: Appeal from the decision of the district court denying motion to suppress evidence and motion to dismiss charge of failure to comply with the Drug Tax Stamp Act. Affirmed in part; vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, County of Nez Perce, which denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence and defendant's motion to dismiss charge of failure to comply with the Drug Tax Stamp Act.


OVERVIEW: Following a preliminary hearing, defendant was bound over to the district court for trial on the charges of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and failure to affix controlled substance tax stamps to the cocaine. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the evidence found in his vehicle, and a motion to dismiss the tax stamp charge on the basis that the statute was unconstitutional. The court held that the 1989 version of the Illegal Drug Stamp Tax Act, which had required those unlawfully in possession of controlled substances to purchase and affix drug tax stamps to the substances or face civil and criminal penalties, was unconstitutional because it violated defendant's right against self-incrimination. The court also held that the relevant search was a valid search incident to arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision denying defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant's conviction on the charge of possession of a controlled substance was affirmed. Defendant's conviction for failure to purchase and affix a drug stamp under the 1989 version of the Illegal Drug Stamp Tax Act was vacated.

Grant v. Twin Falls


No. 17976


Supreme Court of Idaho


120 Idaho 69; 813 P.2d 880; 1991 Ida. LEXIS 99



June 26, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication July 18, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Honorable Daniel C. Hurlbutt, Jr., District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Curtis and Robert Grant appeal from an unfavorable jury verdict in their action based on 42 U.S.C. § 1983 and the tort claims authorized by the Idaho Tort Claims Act. The jury found no liability on the part of the defendant police officers for use of excessive force. The Grants contend that the jury instructions incorrectly stated the applicable law. Affirmed in part and reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of the decision of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District (Idaho), which rendered judgment against them on a jury's finding of no cause of action in their claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the Idaho Tort Claims Act against defendants, municipality and police officers. Plaintiffs argued that the police officers had used excessive force during their post-arrest detention.


OVERVIEW: The trial court instructed the jury that under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 it was to consider the need for the application of force, the relationship between the need and the amount of force, the extent of the injury, and whether the force was applied in a good faith effort to insure discipline, or maliciously or sadistically to harm. The jury found for the officers, and plaintiffs appealed. While pending, the United States Supreme Court held that § 1983 claims of excessive force were to be analyzed under Fourth Amendment concepts of objective reasonableness, rather than under a Fourteenth Amendment substantive due process approach; the subjective test used by the trial court. The court affirmed, holding that it was bound to apply the law in effect at the time it rendered its decision, and therefore, the new decision applied retroactively. Further, the court held that plaintiffs were arrestees and remanded for the trial court to instruct whether the Fourth Amendment's "objective reasonableness" standard, balancing the nature and quality of the intrusion upon Fourth Amendment interests against the interests of the officers in treating plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court on plaintiffs' claims authorized by the Idaho Tort Claims Act and vacated the judgment as to plaintiffs' § 1983 claim. The court remanded for proceedings consistent with its opinion.

State v. Broadhead


No. 18414


Supreme Court of Idaho


120 Idaho 141; 814 P.2d 401; 1991 Ida. LEXIS 85



May 30, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication August 27, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 27, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. George D. Carey, District Judge.

Appeal from sentence of life imprisonment, with fifteen years fixed, for second-degree murder conviction.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which sentenced him to life imprisonment, with 15 years fixed, after he was convicted of second-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: After defendant killed his father and was convicted of second-degree murder, he appealed from his sentence of life imprisonment, with 15 years fixed. The court affirmed. The sentence was not unreasonable. The sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment under either Idaho Const. art. I, § 6 or the Eighth Amendment of the United States Constitution. Reasonable minds might have differed as to whether a 15-year fixed term, or some lesser fixed term, was necessary to protect society from defendant. It was a reasonable view of the facts for the trial court to conclude that a 15-year fixed term was necessary to protect society. Under the circumstances, the court would not substitute its view of the appropriate term of confinement for the view of the trial court. The sentence was not out of all proportion to the gravity of the offense he committed, nor was it so severe as to shock the conscience of reasonable people. Defendant killed his father with a rifle. While some extenuating personal circumstances were involved, the murder was unprovoked and cruel. The sentence was not so disproportionate as to be cruel and unusual punishment under the eighth amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence of life imprisonment, with 15 years fixed, following his conviction for second-degree murder.

State v. Gascon


No. 18453


Supreme Court of Idaho


119 Idaho 932; 812 P.2d 239; 1991 Ida. LEXIS 49



April 4, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication June 27, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 27, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ida. LEXIS 103.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Petition for Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals of the state of Idaho, No. 17196, which affirmed a judgment of conviction from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Honorable Daniel C. Hurlbutt, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of the district court is affirmed, consistent with the opinion of the Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Idaho), which affirmed a judgment of conviction from the district court and its denial of defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence seized from his car when he was stopped at a roadblock. Defendant contended that the roadblock did not comply with Idaho Code §§ 19-621, 19-622, and that the stop of his car and the ensuing investigation of his car were improper.


OVERVIEW: A roadblock was set up following a bank robbery. A police officer stationed prior to entry into the roadblock observed defendant leaning over the passenger side of his car and reaching under the seat, and the officer alerted the police stationed in the roadblock to stop defendant's vehicle because he appeared to be acting suspiciously. Defendant sought to suppress a baseball cap, a jacket, and a bag of money that were discovered in a search of his car at the roadblock. The court found that the police were allowed to set up the roadblock pursuant to Idaho Code § 19-621 because they were not unreasonable in suspecting that a bank robber, about whom they had a description, would escape by driving over the bridge where they set up the roadblock because it was the quickest route to the interstate highway. The stop of defendant's car was proper based on his movements as he approached the roadblock that were aptly characterized as suspicious. The ensuing investigation of his car to make a protective search for weapons was also proper based upon a reasonable belief that defendant might have had a bomb because the robber who was sought by police had threatened to use a bomb in the robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence.

State v. Rhoades


Nos. 17521, 18285


Supreme Court of Idaho


1991 Ida. LEXIS 44



March 28, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 28, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bingham. Honorable James C. Herndon, District Judge.

This Opinion is Substituted for Withdrawn Opinion of February 15, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ida. LEXIS 18.



DISPOSITION: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, first degree kidnapping, robbery, and the use of firearms in the commission of these crimes. The death sentence was imposed. Defendant appealed. Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District, Bingham County (Idaho), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder, first-degree kidnapping, robbery, and the use of firearms in the commission of the crimes, and which imposed a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court declined to rule on the constitutionality of a statute that repealed the insanity defense. On review, the court found no error because the record did not contain sufficient evidence of insanity to establish that a justiciable controversy existed on that issue. The court held that the prosecution did not withhold exculpatory evidence where it provided the defense with a report regarding another person's confession to the crime, although other related reports were not provided to the defense. The court found no error in the trial court's decision to allow a jailhouse informant to testify, noting that it was the jury's responsibility to weigh the credibility of his testimony. The court found that statements made by defendant to the police were voluntary. The court found no equal protection or due process violations in Idaho Code § 19-2719, a statute providing for accelerated post-conviction proceedings. The court held that the use of victim impact statements at sentencing was error, but the court found that the error was harmless. The court found that the trial court properly considered sentencing alternatives, as well as mitigating and aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and affirmed the death sentence.

Loomis v. Hailey


No. 18321


Supreme Court of Idaho


119 Idaho 434; 807 P.2d 1272; 1991 Ida. LEXIS 43



March 21, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication April 12, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Blaine County. Honorable James J. May, District Judge.

Appellants Loomis and Grubb appeal the district court's order granting summary judgment in favor of the City of Hailey.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho granted summary judgment in favor of defendant city in plaintiff residents' action challenging the constitutionality of an ordinance providing for new water and sewer connection fees. The court also granted attorney fees to the city on the city's cross-claim alleging that the residents' action was frivolously brought. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under the ordinance, the city adopted an equity buy-in method of determining the amount of the connection fee by attempting to define the current value of the city's public water and sewer system and then apportioning a share of the value of that system to the new user. All revenue from the connection fee was placed in a separate special account and used only for replacement of existing system facilities and equipment. The residents argued that the ordinance violated the Idaho Revenue Bonding Act (act), Idaho Code § 50-1027 through § 50-1042. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's award of summary judgment to the city, but reversed the trial court's award of attorney fees to the city. The court held (1) that the fees were not taxes because they were not collected for general revenue-raising purposes and were specifically allocated in accordance with the act, and (2) that the fees were not arbitrary or unreasonable. As to the award of attorney fees, however, the court held that the residents' action was not brought frivolously, unreasonably, or without foundation because, inter alia, it presented a novel question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's judgment granting summary judgment to the city, but reversed the trial court's award of attorney fees to the city.

 

129 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rhoades


Nos. 17521, 18285


Supreme Court of Idaho


1991 Ida. LEXIS 18



February 15, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 28, 1991. Withdrawn March 28, 1991; Substituted Opinion Reported at 1991 Ida. LEXIS 44.
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at State v. Rhoades, 1991 Ida. LEXIS 44 (Idaho, Mar. 28, 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bingham. Hon. James C. Herndon, District Judge.
State v. Rhoades, 121 Idaho 63, 822 P.2d 960, 1991 Ida. LEXIS 15 (Idaho, 1991)
State v. Rhoades, 119 Idaho 594, 809 P.2d 455, 1991 Ida. LEXIS 22 (Idaho, 1991)



DISPOSITION: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, first degree kidnapping, robbery, and the use of firearms in the commission of these crimes. The death sentence was imposed. Defendant appealed. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bingham, which entered his conviction for the first degree murder of a convenience store clerk, first degree kidnapping, robbery, and the use of firearms in the commission of the crimes, and imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions, alleging, among other things, that because a juror commented that he looked guilty, he should have been granted a mistrial, the abolition of the insanity defense was unconstitutional, accelerated post-conviction procedures were unconstitutional, and victim impact statements were improperly considered in imposing the death penalty. The court affirmed, concluding that because no facts supported use of the insanity defense, there was no justiciable controversy to support a ruling on the constitutionality of the repeal of the defense. Further, the trial court inquired into the juror's comment and properly determined that defendant was not prejudiced thereby. Additionally, the court found that the post-conviction process of Idaho Code § 19-2719 did not violate due process rights, because it adequately ensured that death sentences were not carried out so as to arbitrarily deprive defendants of their lives, and successive petitions were allowed. Finally, although admitting victim impact statements of the murder victim's family was error, it was harmless error because the statements did not influence the imposition of sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder, first-degree kidnapping, and use of firearms, and also affirmed the sentence, finding that there existed an adequate basis for imposing the death penalty.

State v. Rhoades


S. Ct. Nos. 17437, 18039


Supreme Court of Idaho


121 Idaho 63; 822 P.2d 960; 1991 Ida. LEXIS 15



February 13, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 13, 1991. Second Correction February 28, 1991. Dissenting Opinion Withdrawn Per Court February 28, 1991. Rehearing Granted In Part, Denied In Part April 8, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ida. LEXIS 58.
Related proceeding at State v. Rhoades, 1991 Ida. LEXIS 18 (Idaho, Feb. 15, 1991)
Rehearing granted by, in part, Rehearing denied by, in part State v. Rhoades, 1991 Ida. LEXIS 58 (Idaho, Apr. 8, 1991)
On rehearing at State v. Rhoades, 1991 Ida. LEXIS 168 (Idaho, Nov. 14, 1991)
Writ of certiorari denied Rhoades v. Idaho, 506 U.S. 1047, 113 S. Ct. 962, 122 L. Ed. 2d 119, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 48 (1993)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Rhoades v. State, 2009 Ida. LEXIS 187 (Idaho, Oct. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District, in and for the County of Bonneville. Honorable Larry M. Boyle, District Judge.
State v. Rhoades, 119 Idaho 594, 809 P.2d 455, 1991 Ida. LEXIS 22 (Idaho, 1991)



DISPOSITION: The judgment entered and sentence imposed are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence for murder imposed by the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District, in and for the County of Bonneville (Idaho), asserting that Idaho Code § 18-207(a) abolishing the insanity defense was unconstitutional, that post-conviction procedure under Idaho Code § 19-2719 was unconstitutional, and that the trial court erred in ordering a defense expert to prepare a report for the prosecutor.


OVERVIEW: Following his conviction and death sentence for murder, defendant sought review, arguing, among 13 points for appeal, that Idaho Code § 18-207(a) abolishing the insanity defense was unconstitutional, that accelerated post-trial procedures under Idaho Code § 19-2719 for capital cases were unconstitutional, and that the trial court erred in ordering a defense expert to prepare a report for the prosecutor. The court affirmed. The court found no justiciable issue regarding the constitutionality of § 18-207(a) where defendant had not alleged any issue as to his sanity. The court ruled that the trial court properly declined to render a decision under the Declaratory Judgment Act, Idaho Code § 10-12. The court found that § 19-2719, providing for review by the trial court and then by the appellate court, provided an adequate opportunity for presentation and review of the issues raised and was not unconstitutional under due process analysis. The court held that Idaho R. Crim. P. 16(c)(2) allowed access to reports of experts which the defendant intended to introduce at trial, and the trial court's order to produce merely required production sufficiently in advance of trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence for murder. The court ruled that defendant had not raised a justiciable issue regarding the abolishment of the insanity defense, that the accelerated post-conviction procedure for capital cases was not unconstitutional, and that the trial court properly ordered timely production of an expert's report.

State v. Pizzuto


Nos. 16489, 17534


Supreme Court of Idaho


119 Idaho 742; 810 P.2d 680; 1991 Ida. LEXIS 5



January 15, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication June 5, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 25, 1991. Rehearing Denied June 5, 1991.
Stay granted by Pizzuto v. Idaho, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 4039 (U.S., June 28, 1991)
Writ of certiorari denied Pizzuto v. Idaho, 503 U.S. 908, 112 S. Ct. 1268, 117 L. Ed. 2d 495, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 1438 (1992)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Pizzuto v. State, 127 Idaho 469, 903 P.2d 58, 1995 Ida. LEXIS 102 (Idaho, 1995)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Pizzuto v. State, 134 Idaho 793, 10 P.3d 742, 2000 Ida. LEXIS 97 (Idaho, 2000)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Pizzuto v. State, 2007 Ida. LEXIS 209 (Idaho, Nov. 23, 2007)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Pizzuto v. State, 146 Idaho 720, 202 P.3d 642, 2008 Ida. LEXIS 39 (Idaho, 2008)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Pizzuto v. State, 2010 Ida. LEXIS 54 (Idaho, Mar. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Idaho County. Honorable George Reinhardt, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from convictions of murder in the first degree, felony murder and robbery, and from sentences imposed. Affirmed. Robbery merged with felony murder convictions and robbery sentence vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of first degree premeditated murder, two counts of first degree felony murder, robbery, and grand theft. The jury found him guilty, and the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Idaho County, sentenced him to death for the murders and imposed prison terms for the other convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed two people at a camping facility and beat them to death. At trial, the state offered testimony that defendant robbed another person shortly after the murders and that the robbery was carried out in a similar manner. The state also presented photographs of the victims. Defendant claimed that the testimony concerning the second robbery was inadmissible and that the photographs were inflammatory. He also claimed that it was improper for him to be sentenced for both robbery and felony murder. The court upheld defendant's convictions and sentences for murder but vacated the sentence for the robbery conviction. The court ruled that (1) the testimony complained of was admissible because it was relevant to show defendant's intent and that the crimes were part of a common scheme; (2) the probative value of the testimony and of the photographs was not substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice; and (3) all of the elements required to sustain a conviction of robbery were also within the elements needed to sustain a conviction of felony murder, and the robbery conviction therefore merged with the felony murder conviction.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the sentence imposed for the robbery conviction and affirmed the convictions and sentences for first degree premeditated murder and felony murder.

DISPOSITION: Appeal from the imposition of the death penalty following remand for resentencing. Sentence vacated and case remanded for resentencing with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which imposed the death penalty after a remand for resentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the crime of murder. His conviction was upheld on appeal but his death sentence was vacated and remanded for resentencing. On remand, the trial court sentenced defendant to death again. On appeal, the court again vacated the death sentence and remanded with instructions to guide the trial court concerning the decedent's husband's victim impact statement. The trial court was also instructed to weigh the aggravating and mitigating circumstances and to state specifically whether other impact statements were considered. In addition, the court held that the trial court properly considered prior evidence on remand and that Idaho Code § 19-2515(c) was not violative of the Eighth Amendment individualized sentencing requirement. The court declined to reconsider previously decided issues.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the sentence and remanded for resentencing with instructions to weigh the aggravating and mitigating circumstances and to state specifically whether certain testimony was considered in resentencing.

 

133 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Missamore


No. 18179, 1990 Opinion No. 91


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


119 Idaho 27; 803 P.2d 528; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 210



December 21, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication January 14, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 28, 1990. Rehearing Denied December 21, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ida. LEXIS 211.


PRIOR HISTORY: FILED APRIL 24, 1990, IS HEREBY WITHDRAWN AND THIS OPINION IS SUBSTITUTED THEREFOR.

Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Honorable James F. Judd, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from trespass conviction and sentence, reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the appellate court (Idaho), which affirmed her conviction and sentence for criminal trespass. Defendant contended that disputed testimony was improperly admitted and that the sentence was improper and constitutionally invalid.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by complaint for trespass, convicted by a jury, and sentenced. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that: 1) the trial court erred when it permitted the victim to testify that defendant's intent in trespassing was to harass because defendant's intent was irrelevant under the "willful" requirement of Idaho Code § 18-7008(8); 2) the same testimony did not fulfill the opinion testimony requirement of Idaho R. Evid. 701 because there was no basis for the victim's opinion; 3) the testimony was clearly prejudicial and thus defendant was entitled to a new trial; 4) the trial court properly refused to instruct the jury that mistake of fact was a defense to trespass; 5) the decision of whether to charge defendant by means of citation or complaint was a matter of prosecutorial discretion and the dual charging system employed was not a violation of equal protection; and 6) the Colo. Misdemeanor Criminal Rules' sentencing guidelines could properly encourage guilty pleas and did not infringe upon the right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction and sentence for trespass.

Crane Creek Country Club v. Boise


S. Ct. No. 17533


Supreme Court of Idaho


121 Idaho 485; 826 P.2d 446; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 187



November 19, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 24, 1992, Reported at 1992 Ida. LEXIS 33.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable James J. May, District Judge.

The City of Boise and the Boise City Council appeal the district court's issuance of a peremptory writ of prohibition barring the City from annexing the Crane Creek Country Club.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, which granted respondent country club's petition for a writ of prohibition that barred the city from annexing the country club.


OVERVIEW: The city proposed an ordinance to annex the country club. The country club filed a petition for a writ of prohibition to restrain the city from annexing it. The trial court determined that the city was precluded from annexing the country club and issued a permanent writ. On appeal, the court reversed. The court stated that the statute that granted authority to the trial court to issue a writ of prohibition was Idaho Code § 7-40, and that the writ was to be issued with caution. The court stated that the city's proposed annexation was not without merit or was in excess of the city's jurisdiction. The court stated that annexation was a legislative act of the city and was not subject to prohibition. The court stated that because of that the trial court erred when it issued a writ of prohibition because the trial court did not have jurisdiction to do so.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of the country club's petition for a writ of prohibition that restrained the city from annexing the country club.

 

135 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Cowles Publishing Co. v. Magistrate Court


No. 18629


Supreme Court of Idaho


118 Idaho 753; 800 P.2d 640; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 175; 18 Media L. Rep. 1273



October 23, 1990  
October 23, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication November 14, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended October 24, 1990. Second Amendment November 7, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: This is an original proceeding. Petitioner Cowles Publishing Co. filed a petition for writ of mandamus for the purpose of determining the constitutionality of I.C. § 19-811, and to mandate that the magistrate court open preliminary hearings to the public. An Alternate Writ of Mandate was issued by the Supreme Court of Idaho ordering Honorable Peter Hutchinson, Magistrate, First Judicial District Court, Kootenai County to hold a hearing or to show cause.



DISPOSITION: Writ of Mandate issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the underlying criminal proceeding, petitioner publishing company was denied access to the preliminary hearing. The publishing company sought a writ of mandamus to determine the constitutionality of Idaho Code § 19-811, and to mandate that respondent magistrate court open this and all other preliminary hearings to the public. An alternate writ of mandate was issued by to the magistrate court to hold a hearing or to show cause.


OVERVIEW: The publishing company claimed that § 19-811 infringed the free press provisions of U.S. Const. amend. I and the open court mandate of Idaho Const. art. 1, § 18. The court rejected this claim and held that Idaho Code § 19-811 did not violate either constitutional provision. However, the court granted the writ of mandate and ordered the magistrate court to conduct a hearing to determine the effect of public access to the preliminary hearing on the criminal defendant's fair trial rights and if there were alternatives to closure. The court found that the policy and traditional practice in Idaho was to open preliminary hearings and held that in Idaho, a qualified first amendment right of public access attached to preliminary hearings. However, the court also held that when a criminal defendant requested closure of a preliminary hearing pursuant to § 19-811, the magistrate court was required to determine if there was a substantial probability that defendant's right to a fair trial would be prejudiced by publicity that closure would prevent. The magistrate was then required to determine if there were alternatives to closure that would protect defendant's fair trial rights.


OUTCOME: The court issued the writ of mandate to the publishing company.

Stuart v. State


No. 17014


Supreme Court of Idaho


118 Idaho 865; 801 P.2d 1216; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 173



October 16, 1990  
October 16, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication December 28, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Dissenting Opinion Dated October 17, 1990. As Corrected October 17, 1990. Petition for Rehearing Withdrawn December 28, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Clearwater County. Hon. Ron Schilling, District Judge.

Rehearing of an appeal from denial of petition for post conviction relief.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of March 12, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ida. LEXIS 37.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Clearwater County, which denied and dismissed defendant's petition for post conviction relief from his conviction and death sentence for first degree murder by torture of a three-year-old child.


OVERVIEW: The court had earlier affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's petition for post conviction relief. After a rehearing the court again affirmed and substituted this opinion for its prior opinion. Defendant had sought post conviction relief on several grounds and submitted affidavits alleging factual matters relating to evidence not presented at trial. The court found that (1) the use of a preliminary hearing transcript at defendant's sentencing hearing was not unlawful where no formal sentencing hearing was requested as required by Iowa Code § 19-2516; (2) there was no merit to defendant's contention that by entering into plea bargaining negotiations his constitutional right to a jury trial had been violated; (3) newly discovered evidence in the affidavits submitted to the trial court did not create a material issue of fact which would affect defendant's conviction or sentence and thus he was not entitled to a new trial; and (4) the trial court did not err by weighing the mitigating circumstances against the aggravating circumstances collectively, rather than separately, in that there was no weighing process performed because the trial court found nothing in mitigation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court denying and dismissing defendant's petition for post conviction relief. The court withdrew its prior opinion and substituted this opinion.

State v. Searcy


No. 17835


Supreme Court of Idaho


118 Idaho 632; 798 P.2d 914; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 156



September 5, 1990  
September 5, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication September 27, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Fremont County. Hon. H. Reynold George, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from judgments of conviction for first degree murder and robbery, and the enhancement of the sentences for use of a firearm in the commission of a felony. Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentence entered by the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Fremont County, for first degree murder and robbery, and the enhancement of the sentences for use of a firearm in the commission of a felony. Defendant argued that Idaho Code § 18-207 unconstitutionally deprived him of his right to due process by forbidding him to plead an independent defense of insanity.


OVERVIEW: At trial a jury found defendant guilty of murder in the first degree by finding both premeditation and by finding that defendant killed while committing a robbery. Defendant was also found guilty of robbery and of using a firearm while committing a felony. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, finding that neither the federal nor the state constitutions contained any language setting forth any such to present an insanity defense as defendant argued. The court rejected the claim that the disallowance of the insanity defense under Idaho Code § 18-207 deprived defendant of one of the fundamental principles of liberty and justice that were at the base of all civil and political institutions and thus denied him due process of law. Further, the court ruled that the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to strike a victim impact statement which was allegedly used as a basis for arriving at the sentence. The court did however vacate and remand the sentence imposed upon defendant in his absence in violation of Idaho Crim. R. 43(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction entered by the trial court, finding defendant guilty of first degree murder and robbery. The court also vacated the trial court order correcting the sentence imposed on defendant in his absence, and remanded the cause to the trial court for imposition of a valid sentence with the defendant present as required.

State v. O'Neill


No. 17547


Supreme Court of Idaho


118 Idaho 244; 796 P.2d 121; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 122



August 1, 1990  
August 1, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication August 23, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. The Honorable Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.

Appeal from a judgment of conviction entered by the district court against James Francis O'Neill for the crime of sexual abuse of a child under the age of sixteen years in violation of I.C. § 18-1506.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of Ada County (Idaho), which convicted defendant of the crime of sexual abuse of a child under the age of 16 years in violation of Idaho Code § 18-1506.


OVERVIEW: The issue framed and presented was whether a statute of limitation could be extended prior to the expiration of the original statute of limitations without being violative of the ex post facto law provisions. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. As the statute of limitations in effect at the time of the commission of the acts with which defendant was charged had not run, the extension of that time by the legislature was not an ex post facto law. The court found that defendant pled guilty to violating § 18-1506 upon the same facts alleged in the original information and the amended information. Violation of § 18-1506 was a lesser included offense when an individual was charged with violations of Idaho Code § 18-1508. Thus, the amended information did not violate provisions of Idaho Code § 19-1420 or Idaho Cost. art. 1, § 8.


OUTCOME: An order of the trial court convicting defendant for sexual abuse of a child under the age of 16 years was affirmed.

Olvera v. Del's Auto Body


No. 17809


Supreme Court of Idaho


118 Idaho 163; 795 P.2d 862; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 110



July 2, 1990  
July 2, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication August 31, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 13, 1990. Rehearing Denied August 31, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho.

Claimant was injured while painting cars at an automobile repair shop and sought worker's compensation benefits. Claimant appeals from the Industrial Commission's decision that determined he was an independent contractor and not entitled to worker's compensation benefits.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker's compensation claimant challenged an order of the Industrial Commission (Idaho) that, based on the evidence that the claimant was an independent contractor, determined that respondent client was not liable for the benefits that the claimant sought as to an industrial accident.


OVERVIEW: The evidence of an independent contractor relationship included the claimant knowing, prior to beginning the work, that he would be responsible for his own taxes and insurance, no deductions being made from the payments that the claimant received, an IRS 1099 Form being issued, the claimant mostly using his own equipment, and his working irregular hours and hiring assistants to help him. The court affirmed the Commission's order, concluding that substantial competent evidence supported the finding that the claimant was an independent contractor. The referee acknowledged the Commission's responsibility to liberally construe the facts in favor of the claimant, and found that the client never assumed the right to control the time, manner, and method of the claimant's work. Also, the claimant was compensated at a much higher rate than employees who did comparable work in the area, and the client's other workers were independent contractors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's order that stated that the claimant was an independent contractor, rather than an employee.

Bon Appetit Gourmet Foods v. State


No. 17122


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 1002; 793 P.2d 675; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 95



June 14, 1990  
June 14, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: 117 Idaho 1002 at 1006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing on appeal from the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho.

Original Opinion of August 31, 1989, Reported at 117 Idaho 1002, 1989 Ida. LEXIS 145.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Rehearing was granted with respect to the court's original opinion, which had reversed an order from the Industrial Commission (Idaho) that required appellant employer to pay unemployment compensation tax on independent contractors under the provisions of Idaho Code § 72-1316(d)(2).


OVERVIEW: The employer operated a food business and contracted with independent contractors to market its products. Respondent department of employment held that the independent contractors were "covered employees" under Idaho Code § 72-1316(d)(2). On appeal, the Industrial Commission upheld this determination. On further appeal, the court reversed the Commission's order. On rehearing, the court adhered to the views expressed in its original opinion. The court agreed with the employer's assertion that § 72-1316(d)(2) denied the employer equal protection under both the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Idaho Const. art. 1, § 2. The court found that § 72-1316(d)(2) singled out independent contractors engaged in distributing meat, vegetables, fruit, bakery, or beverage products or conducting laundry or dry cleaning business from all others in the business of door-to-door marketing. The court found no legislative statement of policy or public purpose and no explanation or justification for the legislative distinction. The court concluded that it had correctly applied the rational basis test to § 72-1316(d)(2) and found § 72-1316(d)(2) unconstitutional on its face.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the Commission and remanded.

State v. Paz


No. 17452


Supreme Court of Idaho


118 Idaho 542; 798 P.2d 1; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 96



June 13, 1990  
June 13, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication September 25, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 25, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ida. LEXIS 163.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Honorable Dennis E. Goff, District Judge.

Appeal of conviction for first degree murder, the trial court's denial of appellant's motion for post-conviction relief and death sentence.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, convicting him of first-degree murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, and sentenced to death. He filed a post-conviction motion for relief, which was denied. Defendant's main contention on appeal was that the trial court erred in ruling that he had not established a prima facie case of underrepresentation, and in not requiring the state to offer responsive evidence to his evidence at the hearing on his motion to quash the jury pool and panel. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court found that the statutes limited those eligible to serve on a jury to United States citizens who were able to read, speak, and understand the English language. Exclusion of Hispanics may have resulted from the application of those statutes, simply because the population of non-citizens and non-English speaking persons in Idaho was largely Hispanic. The court held that the jury selection process causing the disparity was supported by a significant state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and his sentence of death.

Mercado v. Baker


No. 17476


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 777; 792 P.2d 342; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 69



May 23, 1990 


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication June 14, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Cassia. Honorable J. William Hart, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an injured employee, appealed from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Cassia, which granted defendant manufacturer's motion for summary judgment in a products liability and personal injury case based on the Idaho product liability statute of repose, Idaho Code § 6-1403(2).


OVERVIEW: The injured employee brought an action against defendant employer and defendant manufacturer, for personal injuries she sustained when her right foot and toes came into contact with an unguarded drive mechanism on a potato harvester. The trial court granted the manufacturer summary judgment based on the statute of repose, Idaho Code § 6-1403(2), because the machinery was more than 10 years old. The injured employee appealed, arguing in part that the trial court improperly excluded an affidavit submitted in opposition to the summary judgment motion. The court held that summary judgment was properly granted and the affidavit was properly excluded because: (1) the affidavit was untimely and (2) the affidavit did not rebut the fact that the accident occurred beyond the useful safe life of the machinery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment of the lower court granting summary judgment for the manufacturer.

 

146 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Olsen v. J.A. Freeman Co.


No. 17471


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 706; 791 P.2d 1285; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 59; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,485



May 7, 1990 


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication May 30, 1990


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Blaine County. Honorable James J. May, District Judge.

Appeal from an order granting summary judgment for the defendants in a products liability action on the ground that the plaintiff's claim was foreclosed by the Idaho products liability statute of repose.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Blaine County, granted defendant manufacturers' motion for summary judgment in a products liability action on the ground that plaintiff injury victim's claim was foreclosed by the Idaho products liability statute of repose, Idaho Code § 6-1403. The victim appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the victim was attempting to repair his employer's hay baler's jammed pickup roller, an object struck him in the face causing retinal hemorrhaging and blindness in one eye. The victim brought suit against the manufacturers and his employer. The accident occurred almost 18 years after the hay baler was delivered to its first purchaser. The hay baler had been rebuilt at least twice with parts borrowed from other machinery. The victim did not establish how his injury occurred and offered no evidence to oppose the manufacturers' motion for summary judgment. The victim alleged Idaho's statute of repose was unconstitutionally vague and violated his rights to due process. The court held the statute of repose was constitutional, and the manufacturers were entitled to summary judgment. The victim failed to present any evidence that the baler's useful safe life had not expired. The statute met the rational basis test of having a reasonably conceived objective advancing the legitimate legislative goal of finality in legal relationships and establishing a maximum length of time the manufacturers were subject to liability. The language of the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order granting summary judgment to manufacturers on the ground that victim's claim was barred by the Idaho products liability statute of repose.

 

147 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Moosman v. Idaho Horse Racing Comm'n


Nos. 17771, 17772


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 949; 793 P.2d 181; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 55



May 1, 1990 


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication July 10, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 10, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, County of Ada. Hon. George D. Carey, District Judge.

Appeal from an order of the district court reversing a decision of the Idaho Horse Racing Commission on the ground that the rule upon which the Commission relied in imposing penalties on the trainers and owners of race horses was unconstitutionally vague. Affirmed on other grounds, as to the redistribution of the purses to which the owners were entitled; reversed, as to the fines and probation imposed on the trainers.

Cross-appeal from an order of the district court denying the petitioning trainers and owners attorney fees. Reversed and remanded, as to the owners; affirmed as to the trainers.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Idaho Horse Racing Commission (Commission) sought review of a judgment from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the County of Ada (Idaho), which reversed the Commission's decision that imposed penalties on respondents, race horse trainers and owners, and ordered the redistribution of purses. The trainers and the owners cross-appealed on the district court's denial of their request for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: After the horses had placed in races, urine samples revealed that they had polyethylene glycol in their systems. Respondents received notices that violations of Commission's Rule 725, which prohibited the administration of "non-approved" medications to race horses, had occurred. The Commission fined the trainers and ordered that the owners' purses were to be redistributed. The court reversed the district court decision that reversed the Commission's determination that imposed penalties on the trainers because Rule 725 was not unconstitutionally vague. Rule 725 was a substantive, prohibitory rule and the term "non-approved medication" was sufficiently explained by Rules 716 and 725. Rule 2802 provided that the trainers were responsible for the condition of the horses. The court affirmed the portion of the district court's judgment that reversed the Commission's order to redistribute the purses because Rule 725 did not include a penalty provision. The owners were entitled to attorney fees pursuant to Idaho Code § 117(1) because the Commission had no authority to order the redistribution of the purses.


OUTCOME: In the Commission's action for the administration of "non-approved" medications to race horses, the court affirmed the district court's denial of the trainers' motion for attorney fees and the district court's reversal of the Commission's order that ordered the redistribution of the purses. The court reversed the district court's order that reversed the Commission's imposition of penalties on the trainers.

 

148 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Hawley v. Green


No. 17591


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 498; 788 P.2d 1321; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 38



March 19, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Dennis Goff, District Judge.

Appeal from granting of summary judgment in favor of defendants in medical malpractice action. Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of the decision of the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County, which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant doctors based on the statute of limitations in Idaho Code § 5-219(4) in the patient's medical malpractice action for the doctors' alleged failure to diagnose a tumor.


OVERVIEW: The patient had a chest X-ray taken preliminary to surgery for an unrelated medical condition. One of the doctors reviewed the X-ray. Then, after an eye examination, she was referred to a neurologist, who reviewed a neck X-ray and a CT scan. The doctors informed the patient that all tests were negative. Subsequently, the patient began experiencing neck and shoulder stiffness and discomfort. She had a chest X-ray and CT scan performed, which revealed a large tumor. She was informed that the tumor was visible in her X-rays and CT scan taken by the doctors. The patient filed a complaint alleging that the doctors were negligent for not diagnosing the tumor. The district court held granted the doctors' motion for summary judgment and held that because the tumor was visible on the X-rays, there was ascertainable damage at that time, and § 5-219(4) barred her claim. The court reversed the statute of limitations issue, but affirmed the ruling that the § 5-219(4) was constitutional. The doctors failed to prove that the tumor which appeared on the X-rays was progressive or otherwise dangerous in order to establish that the patient had incurred some damage at that time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's ruling with respect to the constitutional claims and reversed the grant of summary judgment against the patient's claim against the doctors for medical malpractice on the basis of the statute of limitations.
