Mead v. Arnell


No. 18231


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 660; 791 P.2d 410; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 34



March 13, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1990


PRIOR HISTORY: Original jurisdiction.

This is an application for Alternative and Peremptory Writs of Mandamus and Prohibition and Declaratory Judgment in Mandamus, brought before the Supreme Court on its original jurisdiction by the Idaho Board of Health and Welfare. Writ of mandate issued only as to respondents District VII Health Department.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The applicants, the Idaho Board of Health and Welfare (board) and related parties, filed an application for alternative and peremptory writs of mandamus and prohibition and declaratory judgment in mandamus against respondents, a district health department, related parties, and state legislators, requesting the court to find House Concurrent Resolution-29 (HCR-29) and Idaho Code § 67-5218 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Idaho Code § 39-1, the board promulgated rules and regulations for individual and subsurface sewage disposal systems, Idaho Admin. Code 16.01.3001-999 (1985). After the board issued thousands of permits, the state legislature adopted HCR-29, rescinding the new rules and instructing the board to promulgate the rules that were in effect prior to the adoption of the new rules. Although the board refused to follow this mandate, the district health department complied. The board brought an action to declare HCR-29 and its governing statute, Idaho Code § 67-5218, unconstitutional. The court refused to hold § 67-5218 unconstitutional, finding it promulgated properly and holding that the legislature could rescind the rules if the proper method was followed. However, the court held HCR-29 of no effect due to the legislature's failure to declare the new rules violative of the legislative intent in the enabling statute. Thus, a writ of mandate was issued against the district health department.


OUTCOME: The court issued the writ of mandate to the district health department, refusing to award costs to any party.

 

150 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stiffler


No. 17846


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 405; 788 P.2d 220; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 33



March 6, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. George D. Carey, District Judge.

Appeal from the refusal by the district court to instruct the jury in a statutory rape case that the defendant's lack of knowledge or his reasonably mistaken belief as to the age of the female with whom he had sexual intercourse would be a defense. The Court of Appeals affirmed. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Idaho), which affirmed the district court's ruling that it was not a defense to a charge of statutory rape that defendant reasonably believed that the female with whom he had sexual intercourse was at least 18 years old.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to his conviction for statutory rape, defendant appealed. The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's ruling that it was not a defense to a charge of statutory rape that defendant reasonably believed that the female with whom he had intercourse was at least 18 years old. On further appeal, the court affirmed. Since the prevention of illegitimate teenage pregnancies was cited as one of the objectives behind Idaho Code § 18-6101(1) (1987), and the state's strong interest in furthering this objective was noted, the court was unable to conclude that statutory rape should be construed to require proof of any specific intent. Examples within the design of the statute indicated to the court that the legislature understood the distinction between general criminal intent and specific criminal intent and chose not to require specific criminal intent to convict of a violation of Idaho Code § 18-6101(1) (1987). If the court accepted the applicability of the defense, it would have had to conclude that statutory rape was a crime requiring proof of specific intent to have intercourse with a female under the age of eighteen years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying defendant an instruction that his lack of knowledge or reasonable mistake as to the age of the female with whom he had intercourse would have been a defense.

Petry v. Spaulding Drywall


No. 17798


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 382; 788 P.2d 197; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 25



February 28, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho.

Elwyn Petry appeals the Industrial Commission's finding that he is not entitled to Worker's Compensation benefits because his Notice of Injury and Claim for Benefits was not timely filed. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant employee appealed the finding of the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho that he was not entitled to worker's compensation benefits because his notice of injury and claim for benefits was not timely filed.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who worked as a drywall hanger, was lifting a piece of sheetrock when he slipped and felt a pain in his right shoulder. After resting, he continued to work for the rest of the day. He notified his employer of the accident, but declined the employer's suggestion that he see a doctor. Over the next year, he continued to experience pain in his shoulder. While moving a propane tank at home, the employee again felt severe pain in his shoulder and sought medical attention. Surgery for an impingement syndrome due to a rotator cuff tear was recommended. The employee filed a notice of injury and claim for benefits form with the employer's insurance company. The claim was denied. The Industrial Commission found in favor of the employer and its surety because the claim was not timely filed. In affirming, the court held that the employee's claim for benefits was barred by his failure to comply with Idaho Code § 72-70, as the claim was not filed for 18 months after the accident. The employer was not required to file a report with the commission pursuant to Idaho Code § 72-602(1) because the employee did not seek medical attention and did not miss any work due to his injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the industrial commission's holding that the employee's claim for worker's compensation benefits was not timely filed.

 

152 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Northcutt v. Sun Valley Co.


No. 17679


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 351; 787 P.2d 1159; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 27



February 27, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Blaine County. Hon. James J. May, District Judge.

Appeal from order granting summary judgment to Sun Valley Co. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, skier and his wife, challenged an order from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Blaine County, which granted summary judgment to defendant ski area operator in plaintiffs' action to recover for damages the skier incurred when he collided with a signpost erected on the premises of the operator's ski area.


OVERVIEW: The skier was severely injured when he struck a signpost after an unidentified skier collided with him. A member of the ski patrol who administered first aid to the skier permitted the unidentified skier to leave the scene without requiring him to identify himself. Plaintiffs filed an action against the operator to recover damages for the skier's injuries. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the operator. On appeal, the court affirmed. Even assuming that the operator might not have properly located the sign or properly designed, constructed or padded the signpost, Idaho Code §§ 6-1101 through 6-1109 excluded any liability caused by those activities. The responsibility for the collision between the skier and the unidentified skier was theirs and not the operator's. The unidentified skier had the duty to identify himself following the accident. The operator's only duty was to provide a ski patrol with qualifications meeting the standards of the national ski patrol. Because there was no evidence that the operator failed to follow the duty set forth in Idaho Code § 6-1103(8), it was not liable for the failure to determine the identity of the unidentified skier.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the ski area operator.

State v. Bainbridge


No. 16808


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 245; 787 P.2d 231; 1990 Ida. LEXIS 14



February 5, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing of appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Robert M. Rowett, District Judge.

Defendant Bainbridge appeals his murder conviction, asserting constitutional violations of his right to be free from illegal seizures, his right to a meaningful cross-examination of witnesses, i.e., an issue of admission of pre-hypnotic testimony, and his right to counsel. Bainbridge also alleges prosecutorial misconduct.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County that convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. On appeal, he asserted constitutional violations of his right to be free from illegal seizures, his right to a meaningful cross-examination of witnesses, i.e., an issue of admission of pre-hypnotic testimony, and his right to counsel, and prosecutorial misconduct. The court held that after reviewing the entire record and analyzing the arguments presented there was no prejudicial error. The conviction and sentence were affirmed. The court ruled that the threshold factor that defendant was properly informed of his Miranda rights, combined with his lengthy private discussion with his parole officer interrupting any police activity, outweighed considerations that militated in favor of excluding his statements made after his conversation with the parole officer. Therefore, the statements that he made in the station house interrogation were properly admitted at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment that convicted defendant of murder.

State ex rel. Richardson v. Pierandozzi


No. 17863


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 1; 784 P.2d 331; 1989 Ida. LEXIS 157



December 19, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District for Bear Lake County. Honorable Wallace M. Transtrum, District Judge.

Dante and Janet Pierandozzi appeal a decision of the District Court upholding the revocation of their liquor license by the Department of Law Enforcement.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensees challenged a decision of the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District for Bear Lake County (Idaho), which upheld the revocation of their liquor license by respondent Department of Law Enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The licensees sought judicial review after the Department revoked their liquor license for allowing nudity on the licensed premises in violation of Idaho Code § 23-1010A. The district court upheld the revocation, and the licensees appealed. The court held that: (1) the notice of the hearing was adequate; (2) the due process rights of the licensees were not violated where the hearing examiner was chosen from a list maintained by the Department and compensated on a case by case basis; (3) the fact that the licensees explained to the dancers the type of performance which would not be permitted under the law did not absolve them of responsibility for the dancers' conduct as the licensees were present at the performance and did not attempt to stop or control the performance when dancers began to expose portions of their anatomies in violation of § 23-1010A; (4) in the narrow context of liquor licensing the state has the power to regulate nude and explicit conduct in licensed establishments without offending the First Amendment; and (5) anatomical references in § 23-1010A were not unconstitutionally vague and were applicable to male dancers. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the Department's revocation of the licensees' liquor license for violations of the statute prohibiting the licensees from allowing nudity on the licensed premises.

Bon Appetit Gourmet Foods v. Department of Employment


No. 17122


Supreme Court of Idaho


117 Idaho 1002; 793 P.2d 675; 1989 Ida. LEXIS 145



August 31, 1989  
August 31, 1989, Filed


NOTICE: Released for Publication July 6, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On Rehearing June 14, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ida. LEXIS 95; Rehearing Granted October 23, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Industrial Commission, State of Idaho.

An appeal from a decision holding that certain independant contractors are covered employees under I.C. § 72-1316(d)(2) and thus the employer is required to pay unemployment compensation.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a decision from the Industrial Commission, State of Idaho, holding that certain independent contractors were covered employees under Idaho Code § 72-1316(d)(2) and thus the employer was required to pay unemployment compensation.


OVERVIEW: Respondent department of employment declared that certain independent contractors that assisted the employer were covered employees, thus, the employer was required to pay unemployment compensation tax. The Industrial Commission upheld this determination, and the employer challenged the decision on the ground that Idaho Code § 72-1316 violated the equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Idaho Const. art. 1, § 2. The court noted that an act of the legislature was presumed constitutional, but whether the act was reasonable, or arbitrary, or discriminatory was a question of law. In addition, a classification for tax purposes was reviewed on the rational basis test. After an independent analysis to ascertain a legitimate basis for what on its face was a discriminatory tax, the court found no such rational basis. The court found the particular provisions of § 72-1316 to be unconstitutional on its face, and as applied, because it denied the employer equal protection of the laws in violation of the federal and state constitutions.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Industrial Commission upholding a tax assessment against an employer for unemployment compensation was reversed and remanded for entry of an appropriate order.

Miles v. Idaho Power Co.


No. 16614


Supreme Court of Idaho


116 Idaho 635; 778 P.2d 757; 1989 Ida. LEXIS 135



August 8, 1989 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ratepayer sought declaratory relief, on behalf of himself and other similarly situated ratepayers, to have declared unconstitutional the implementing legislation to an agreement between appellee government and appellee public utility commission (PUC) regarding electric rates and water rights. The district court (Idaho) dismissed the case for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The ratepayer sought review.


OVERVIEW: The ratepayer claimed that the controversy was justiciable because it did not involve a political question, he had standing, and it was ripe for adjudication. He also claimed that the implementing legislation violated the equal protection and the due process clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court held that the claim was justiciable, but rejected the other arguments, and affirmed the lower court's dismissal. The court held that the claim regarding the constitutionality of the implementing legislation was not an impermissible political question and that the ratepayer had standing because he had a personal stake in the outcome of the case. The court further held that the case was ripe because deferral to the PUC's administrative procedures would not add anything material to the resolution of the legal issues. However, the court held that the legislation was constitutional. The court held that the ratepayer did not have a protected property interest within the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and that the legislation substantially furthered a specifically identifiable legislative end and thus did not violate the equal protection provisions of this amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's dismissal of the ratepayer's declaratory judgment action.

Dexter v. Idaho State Bar Bd. of Comm'rs


No. 17488


Supreme Court of Idaho


116 Idaho 790; 780 P.2d 112; 1989 Ida. LEXIS 119



July 20, 1989 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney sought review of the decision of the Idaho Board of Bar Commissioners, which denied his application to sit for the Idaho bar examination.


OVERVIEW: The Commission denied the attorney's application to sit for the Idaho bar examination. The Commission found that the attorney exhibited an inclination to violate reasonable rules of conduct and that he failed to exercise substantial self-control which met the standard for disqualification set forth in Idaho Bar Comm'n R. 208(e)(7), (8). On review, the court remanded the matter to the Commission with instructions that the Commission make findings of fact stating particularly what acts or omissions of the attorney made him unfit to practice law in Idaho. The court found that the Commission's failure to make findings of fact deprived the attorney of his right to due process of law. The court noted that the attorney's interest in practicing law in Idaho was a substantial interest and that the administrative cost of making findings of fact would have been minimal. The court concluded that the Commission had a duty to formulate findings of fact and conclusions of law so that a reviewing court could have a basis to conduct meaningful review. The court noted that there would have been no ancillary disruptive effect on the administrative efficiency of the Commission.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter to the Commission with instructions that the Commission make findings of fact stating particularly what acts or omissions of the attorney made him unfit to practice law in Idaho.

State v. Lankford


Nos. 15759, 16192


Supreme Court of Idaho


116 Idaho 860; 781 P.2d 197; 1989 Ida. LEXIS 117



July 10, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 31, 1989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of a district court (Idaho), which found defendant guilty of two counts of murder and sentenced him to death, following which the court denied defendant's amended petition for post-conviction relief of his second motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court gave erroneous jury instructions and abused its discretion when it compelled him to be a witness against himself at a psychiatric examination, that imposition of the death penalty with no participation by the jury in the sentencing process was unconstitutional, and that imposition of the death penalty was arbitrary. The court affirmed the convictions and death sentence, holding that: (1) the trial court ensured that defendant's waiver of his right to counsel was made knowingly and intelligently and tried to dissuade him from proceeding pro se; (2) the jury instruction was proper as the robbery not only supplied the malice element, but also made it a murder in the first degree as defined in Idaho Code § 18-4003(d); (3) the list in § 19-2515(f) provided defendant with requisite notice of all possible aggravating circumstances; (4) defendant was not entitled to jury participation in the sentencing process; (5) the psychiatrist did not violate defendant's constitutional rights when he orally advised defendant of his Miranda rights and accepted an oral waiver; and (6) the death penalty was properly imposed based on a proportionality review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and the death sentence imposed.

State v. Fain


No. 15414


Supreme Court of Idaho


116 Idaho 82; 774 P.2d 252; 1989 Ida. LEXIS 52



April 4, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 30, 1989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a decision of the trial court (Idaho), which convicted appellant of first degree murder, lewd and lascivious conduct with a minor, and first degree kidnapping, and sentenced appellant to death.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of first degree murder, lewd and lascivious conduct with a minor, and first degree kidnapping, and sentenced appellant to death. On appeal, the court held that, after reviewing the testimony adduced at the preliminary hearing, there was competent evidence, including reasonable inferences therefrom, to show probable or sufficient cause that the crimes charged had been committed and that the defendant was guilty of their commission. Further, the court determined that the state did not deprive appellant of due process by failing to preserve the semen samples it had obtained. The court held that the circumstantial evidence presented, and from which the jury clearly drew the inference of appellant's guilt, was sufficient to sustain a conviction. The court concluded that although the evidence against appellant was circumstantial, it was nonetheless significant and weighty. However, because the trial court incorrectly weighed all of the mitigating circumstances against all of the aggravating circumstances, collectively, rather than individually, the court vacated the sentence and remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction; however, the court vacated the death sentence and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Charboneau


Nos. 16339, 16741


Supreme Court of Idaho


116 Idaho 129; 774 P.2d 299; 1989 Ida. LEXIS 53



April 4, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 25, 1989.
Later proceeding at State v. Charboneau, 1989 Ida. LEXIS 92 (Idaho, May 25, 1989)
Writ of certiorari denied Charboneau v. Idaho, 493 U.S. 922, 107 L. Ed. 2d 267, 110 S. Ct. 287, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 4914 (1989)
Writ of certiorari denied Idaho v. Charboneau, 493 U.S. 923, 107 L. Ed. 2d 270, 110 S. Ct. 290, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 4962 (1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and death sentence in the Ada County Court (Idaho) for the first-degree murder of his former wife.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his conviction was invalid because he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The reviewing court disagreed. The test for determining whether a defendant has been denied effective assistance of counsel under the Constitution of the United States is: First, a claimant must prove that counsel's performance was deficient. Second, a claimant must show that this deficient performance prejudiced his or her case. Here, while defendant's testimony at the motion to dismiss hearing may have been unwise, it was a strategic decision by counsel that could not be second-guessed. Evidence of grand theft and kidnapping were properly admitted against defendant, despite the fact that those charges were dropped, because they tended to show his motive or intent. Idaho R. Evid. 404(b). However, the death penalty was vacated on numerous grounds, including the fact that a victim impact statement was introduced at the sentencing phase of the capital murder case, which had been declared unconstitutional by the United States Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but the death sentence was vacated and remanded for resentencing.

Kootenai County Property Ass'n v. Kootenai County


No. 17328


Supreme Court of Idaho


115 Idaho 676; 769 P.2d 553; 1989 Ida. LEXIS 16; 29 ERC (BNA) 1218



February 8, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. Richard G. Magnuson, District Judge.

Appeal from grant of summary judgment in favor of respondent.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant association sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County, which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent county and held that the county's solid waste disposal charge on residential dwellings did not unconstitutionally discriminate against property owners as opposed to actual users.


OVERVIEW: The district court also held that the disposal charge was a reasonable "fee" for services as authorized by Idaho Code § 31-4404 and was not an invalid "tax" within the meaning of the Idaho Const. art. 7, §§ 4, 5. Pursuant to Idaho Code § 31-44 the county commissioners ordered the establishment of a solid waste disposal system whereby the county would have the responsibility for providing for all solid waste disposal including landfill sites. On appeal, the court concluded that the solid waste disposal fee for residential dwellings was reasonably related to the services rendered by the county in acquiring, establishing, maintaining, and operating its solid waste disposal system. The court held that the fee was authorized by Idaho Code § 31-4402(2) and was not an illegal tax in violation of the Idaho Const. art. 7, §§4, 5. The court held that the commissioners' choice to set the commercial unit charge according to actual use did not negate the reasonableness of not also using the approach for residential dwellings. The court pointed out that the county was authorized to enact either a solid waste disposal tax or a solid waste disposal fee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

165 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Blangers v. Department of Revenue & Taxation


No. 16404


Supreme Court of Idaho


114 Idaho 944; 763 P.2d 1052; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 210



October 28, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 114 Idaho 944 at 960.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of May 25, 1988, Reported at 114 Idaho 944.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Idaho State Tax Commission, filed a petition for rehearing after the court held that a sufficient nexus did not exist to justify the imposition of income taxes on plaintiff railroad employees.


OVERVIEW: The railroad employees were nonresidents of the state and had obtained their employment with the railroad company in another state. The commission sought to impose income tax on the railroad employees on the ground that they traveled through the state in connection with their employment. After the court held that the railroad employees were not subject to income taxation, the commission filed a petition for rehearing. In denying the petition, the court reaffirmed its holding that the railroad employees were not subject to state income tax because there was not a substantial nexus between the railroad employees and the taxing authority. The court rejected the commission's contention that only multi-state corporations were entitled to the protection of the nexus requirement. Moreover, the mere fact that the railroad employees traveled through the state did not create a substantial nexus because presence alone was insufficient. The railroad employees were entitled to the protection of the commerce clause because they worked across state boundaries and were involved in interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court denied the commission's petition for rehearing.

 

166 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Blangers v. Department of Taxation


No. 16404


Supreme Court of Idaho


1988 Ida. LEXIS 138



October 28, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. Watt E. Prather, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Idaho State Tax Commission petitioned for rehearing. The court had rendered an original opinion, finding that the Idaho Income Tax Act, by imposing a tax on the income of train crew on through trains, violated the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment or the Commerce Clause. The commission challenged the earlier judgment from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County.


OVERVIEW: The commission argued that the concept of nexus should not be applied in the same fashion to multi-state corporations and to nonresident individuals. The commission maintained that the court erred in looking to principles of nexus developed in cases dealing with multi-state corporations in determining whether a sufficient nexus existed in the case to justify the imposition of income taxes on the train crews. The contention suggested that individuals were not entitled to the same protection of the nexus requirement as corporations were under the due process clause and the commerce clause. The commission argued that while the train crews were working in Idaho they were receiving the benefits of Idaho's organized society and should therefore be subject to Idaho income taxes. The court re-iterated that the relationship of the train crews was with their employer, not with Idaho. The fact that they were paid for duties they performed on the trains while the trains were traveling through Idaho did not amount to their benefiting from the fruits of civilization in Idaho. Idaho did not provide them with the opportunity for employment; only their employer provided them with that opportunity.


OUTCOME: The court denied the commission's petition for rehearing.

In re Snake River Basin Water Sys.


Nos. 17267, 17275


Supreme Court of Idaho


115 Idaho 1; 764 P.2d 78; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 129



October 13, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. Daniel C. Hurlbutt, Jr., District Judge.

Appeal from an order of the district court which included the Boise River and Weiser River sub-basins within the boundaries of the Snake River basin water adjudication.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant irrigation districts sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Twin Falls County (Idaho) made in favor of respondent State of Idaho ex relatione Director of the Idaho Department of Water Resources after the Director petitioned to adjudicate the rights to use of all surface and ground waters of the Snake-River-basin water system within Idaho, upstream from a certain point.


OVERVIEW: The United States and all claimants to the use of water from the Snake River Basin Water System were also respondents. Idaho Code § 42-1406A authorized the Director to petition the trial court for an adjudication under the McCarran Amendment (MA), 43 U.S.C.S. § 666, of the water rights of the Snake River basin. The MA gave consent to sue the United States in any suits for the adjudication of the rights to the use of water of river systems or other sources. At issue was the inclusion by the trial court of the Boise River and Weiser River sub-basins in defining the boundaries of the water system to be adjudicated. The court held that Idaho Code § 42-1406A(3)(b) did not require the special consent of the United States external to the MA for the exclusion of those sub-basins from the adjudication, however, the court ruled that the inclusion of those sub-basins was required to obtain jurisdiction over the United States under the MA. The court ruled that the legislative history of § 42-1406A(3)(b) showed that by the words "any adjudicated tributary" the legislature intended to refer to the Boise, Payette, Weiser, and Lemhi rivers.


OUTCOME: Ruling against the irrigation districts, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Fetterly


Nos. 16540, 16541


Supreme Court of Idaho


115 Idaho 231; 766 P.2d 701; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 108



September 9, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissent on Denial of Rehearing December 13, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the District Court of the Third Judicial District, State of Idaho, Canyon County. The Honorable Edward J. Lodge, District Judge.

Appeals from denial of motions to reduce sentence and to disqualify judge from post conviction proceedings, and a denial of petition for post conviction relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgments from the District Court of the Third Judicial District, State of Idaho, Canyon County, which denied his petition for post conviction relief, denying his Idaho Crim. R. 35 motion for a reduced sentence, and denied his Idaho Crim. R. 25 motion to disqualify the trial judge from the post conviction proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his codefendant were convicted of first degree murder, burglary, and grand theft, and were sentenced to death. Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed on appeal. When defendant filed his petition for post-conviction relief and his motion for a reduced sentence, he sought to disqualify the trial judge. The district court denied all of the relief requested by defendant in the petition and motions. The court affirmed the judgments. Because the issues raised in the post conviction relief petition were adjudicated on direct appeal, there was no error in the district court's res judicata ruling in denying the petition. The new cases cited by defendant in support of his claim that his sixth amendment right to counsel was violated did not apply. When faced with a motion to disqualify in post conviction proceedings, the trial judge was required only to have concluded that he could properly perform the legal analysis that the law required. The determination that it was necessary to reduce the interminable delay in capital cases was a rational basis for the imposition of the 42-day time limit for post-conviction relief petitions set forth in Idaho Code § 19-2719.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgments, which denied defendant's petition for post conviction relief, denied his motion for a reduced sentence, and denied his motion to disqualify the trial judge from the post conviction proceedings.

 

169 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Bergman v. Henry


No. 17011


Supreme Court of Idaho


115 Idaho 259; 766 P.2d 729; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 113



September 9, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Kootenai. Honorable Richard G. Magnuson, District Judge.

Action against licensed vendor of alcoholic beverages for wrongful death of and personal injuries to passengers in car struck by vehicle driven by intoxicated customer.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of dismissal on the pleadings for failure to state cause of action; Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of a judgment entered by the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Kootenai, which dismissed her claims against respondents, a hotel and its employees, in the wife's action against for wrongful death and personal injuries.


OVERVIEW: The wife's husband was killed when his pickup was struck by a vehicle that was operated by respondent driver. Prior to the accident, the driver had been drinking at the hotel. The wife, who was also injured in the crash, commenced an action for wrongful death and for her own injuries against several parties including the driver, her estate, the hotel, and its employees. The trial court dismissed the wife's claims against the hotel and its employees on the ground that Idaho did not recognize dram shop liability at the time of the accident. The wife appealed from that order, which was reversed. The matter was remanded. The dram shop and social host liability act, Idaho Code § 23-808, was not applicable because the accident occurred before its effective date. However, prior to the enactment of § 23-808, a cause of action existed when a purveyor of spirits continued to serve an obviously intoxicated person who was under the legal drinking age. The court concluded that there was no reason to distinguish between a minor and an adult when either was obviously intoxicated. Therefore, the wife stated claims against the hotel and its employees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which had dismissed the wife's claims against the hotel and its employees. The wife was awarded costs.

 

170 of 696 DOCUMENTS


David Steed & Assocs. v. Young


No. 17252


Supreme Court of Idaho


115 Idaho 247; 766 P.2d 717; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 111



September 6, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding in Mandamus and Prohibition to compel granting of jury trial.



DISPOSITION: Party to an equity action has right to jury trial on legal causes of action asserted in his compulsory counterclaim. Alternative writ made permanent and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner borrower filed a writ of mandamus to require the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho to vacate its order, which granted respondent bank's motion to strike the borrower's demand for a jury trial on the legal causes of action asserted in its compulsory counterclaim against the bank, which had instituted a mortgage foreclosure action against the borrower.


OVERVIEW: In response to the bank's foreclosure action, the lender filed a separate action against the bank, alleging causes of action grounded both in law and equity. The district court consolidated the cases and denominated the lender's claim a compulsory counterclaim pursuant to Idaho R. Civ. Proc. 13(a). The district court then granted the bank's motion to strike the borrower's demand for a jury trial. On appeal, the court reversed. The court noted that a party's right to jury trial was "inviolate" pursuant to Idaho Const. art. 1, §7, and that Idaho R. Civ. Proc. 13(a) would be unconstitutional if it compelled a party either to waive his right to a jury by pleading the counterclaim or waive the claim by not pleading it. The court held that a party to an equity action had a right to jury trial on legal causes of action asserted in his compulsory counterclaim, unless there was a clear showing of "imperative circumstances" which would cause the equity claimant irreparable harm while affording a jury trial in the legal cause. The court determined that the bank had made no such showing.


OUTCOME: The court made permanent the alternative writ insofar as it required the district judge to vacate his order striking the demand for jury trial, and the court remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with its ruling that a party to an equity action had a right to jury trial on legal causes of action asserted in its compulsory counterclaim.

Hansen v. White


No. 17139


Supreme Court of Idaho


114 Idaho 907; 762 P.2d 820; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 112



August 31, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 20, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certified question from the Ninth Circuit Court of Appeals. On appeal from the District Court for the District of Idaho. Honorable Marion G. Callister, United States District Judge. Question answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant civil service employees challenged the judgment from the District Court for the District of Idaho, which returned a verdict in favor of appellees, sheriff and county. After the employees appealed the case to the United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit, the appeals court certified a question to the court.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court considered whether the county commissioners had the authority to institute a merit system binding county officers, particularly the sheriff, under which such officers could not terminate deputies and other employees in their department except for cause. In response, the court first held that the board of county commissioners had been granted authority by the Idaho legislature to establish a merit system binding the sheriff. The court determined that such an act was a valid exercise of the legislature's express power. Secondly, the court determined that the merit system at issue did not abridge the sheriff's constitutional right to appoint deputies. The court held that fundamental to its decision was the fact that the Idaho Constitution addressed only the right of the sheriff to appoint deputies, not a right to discharge them at will. Thus, the court held that a sheriff's constitutional right to appoint deputies was not abridged where county commissioners instituted a merit system prohibiting the dismissal of deputies without cause, so long as the merit system was reasonable under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question from the appeals court by holding that the sheriff's constitutional right to appoint deputies was not abridged.

Coleman v. State


No. 16767


Supreme Court of Idaho


114 Idaho 901; 762 P.2d 814; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 96



August 11, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the district court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. The Honorable Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court decision that ten-day ban on inmate's access to law library unconstitutionally abridges right of access to the courts affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State of Idaho (state) appealed the judgment of the district court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, which reversed the magistrate's denial of respondent inmate's writ of habeas corpus in which he challenged a 10-day restriction of his access to the law library.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was incarcerated in a prison. He was thereafter confined to 30 days in disciplinary detention for possessing a homemade knife. The prison had a policy at that time, which did not allow an inmate physical access to the law library for the first 10 days of detention. The inmate pursued a habeas corpus proceeding in which he challenged the restriction. The magistrate denied the writ, and, on appeal, the district court reversed the magistrate's order and declared the restriction unconstitutional. On the state's appeal, the court affirmed the district court's judgment. The fundamental constitutional right of access to the courts required the prison authorities to provide the inmate access to the law library. Moreover, the fact that the court could not grant affirmative relief to the inmate due to his subsequent access to the courts did not prevent the court from granting the writ because the restriction was unconstitutional on its face. The restriction was subject to strict scrutiny, and the state failed to demonstrate any compelling penological interest that was served by the restriction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment, which reversed the magistrate's denial of the prisoner's writ of habeas corpus and declared that the state's 10-day restriction on access to the prison's law library unconstitutional.

Deonier v. Public Employee Retirement Bd.


No. 16706


Supreme Court of Idaho


114 Idaho 721; 760 P.2d 1137; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 56



June 17, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 21, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho.

Appeal from decisions of the Industrial Commission upholding an order of the Public Employees Retirement System Board requiring that disability retirement benefits be offset by worker's compensation benefits received by two fire fighters employed prior to 1980 merger of Firemen's Retirement Fund and Public Employee Retirement System.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, appellant firefighters sought review of the decision of the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho (commission), which upheld an order of respondent, the State of Idaho (state) Public Employee Retirement System Board (board), requiring that disability retirement benefits be offset by prior worker's compensation benefits. The state cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The firefighters negotiated lump sum monetary worker's compensation settlements for work-related injuries. After their involuntary retirements, the firefighters sought disability retirement benefits. The board granted the benefits but offset the amount of the lump sum worker's compensation benefit. The commission affirmed the setoff. Both parties appealed. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that retirement benefits under the Firemen's Retirement Fund (FRF) were deferred compensation and that requiring the firefighters to contribute to the cost of their worker's compensation benefits violated Idaho Code § 72-318. Further, offsetting under the FRF impaired the constitutional right to contract because the altered interpretation of Idaho Code § 72-1414 materially changed the firefighters' contractual expectations regarding their vested rights to receive FRF retirement benefits. Moreover, § 72-1414 was violative of equal protection of the law because the statute arbitrarily classified voluntary and involuntary retirees and membership in the FRF versus board systems. Finally, because the offset provisions of § 72-1414 were unconstitutional, the state's cross-appeal was moot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that was in favor of the state requiring that disability retirement benefits be offset by prior worker's compensation benefits. The court held that the state's cross-appeal was moot. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Beam


Nos. 16542, 16543


Supreme Court of Idaho


115 Idaho 208; 766 P.2d 678; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 65



June 16, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissent on Denial of Rehearing December 30, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Edward J. Lodge, District Judge.

Appeals from denial of motion for correction or reduction of sentence and denial of motion for post conviction relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County, which denied his petition for post conviction relief from his death sentence, his motion to reduce his sentence pursuant to Idaho Crim. R. 35, and his motion to disqualify the original trial judge from sitting in the post conviction and sentence reduction proceedings.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's conviction for murder and his death sentence were affirmed on appeal, he filed a petition for post-conviction relief, and motions for a sentence reduction and disqualification of the original trial judge. The trial court denied the petition and the motions, and defendant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that while many of the issues raised by defendant in the petition were barred by res judicata, others were appealable. Idaho Code § 19-2719, which set a 42 day limit on filing of a death sentence challenge, did not violate the equal protection clause because it had a rational basis in the legislative goal to prevent unnecessary delays in capital cases. The trial judge's refusal to disqualify himself was proper because Idaho Crim. R. 35 directed that post-conviction proceedings be heard by the trial court that rendered the original sentence. Although the trial judge had strong opinions regarding defendant, that did not constitute prejudice or bias that would require disqualification. Finally, defendant's death sentence was imposed within the statutory limits of his crime, and it was in proportion to similar sentences within a broad spectrum of murder cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which denied defendant's petition for post conviction relief from his death sentence, his motion to reduce his sentence, and his motion to disqualify the original trial judge from sitting in the post conviction and sentence reduction proceedings.

State v. Henderson


No. 16852


Supreme Court of Idaho


114 Idaho 293; 756 P.2d 1057; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 59



June 15, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.

Order of District Court, on appeal from magistrate's judgment of conviction for DUI, upholding denial of motion to suppress evidence obtained at roadblock.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which denied his motion to suppress evidence and convicted him of driving while under the influence of alcohol (DUI). Defendant contended that the roadblock at which he was stopped and arrested was an unreasonable search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped at a police roadblock designed to detect and deter drunk driving and was subsequently arrested for DUI. At trial, defendant submitted a motion to suppress all evidence of his intoxicated condition obtained during the stop, on the basis that the evidence resulted from an unlawful seizure. Following a denial of that motion by the magistrate, defendant entered a conditional plea of guilty. The district court, acting in an appellate capacity, affirmed the magistrate's judgment and sentence. On appeal, the court reversed and held that where police lacked express legislative authority, particularized suspicion of criminal wrongdoing, and prior judicial approval, roadblocks established to apprehend drunk drivers could not withstand scrutiny under Idaho Const. art. 1, § 17. In so holding, the court noted that although the government interest in reducing alcohol-related accidents was great, that end was not necessarily best served by a warrantless roadblock search, which yielded fewer DUI arrests than did the usual procedure, which first detected criminal wrongdoing.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that because the evidence used to convict defendant was unconstitutionally obtained pursuant to a warrantless search, prior to which the police lacked individualized suspicion of criminal wrongdoing and authority to establish a roadblock, the magistrate and trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress. Accordingly, defendant's DUI conviction was reversed. No costs were assessed on appeal.

Westerberg v. Andrus


No. 16910


Supreme Court of Idaho


114 Idaho 401; 757 P.2d 664; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 57



June 7, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Gerald F. Schroeder, Destrict Judge.

Appeal from judgment of the district court finding that lottery initiative violates Article III, § 20, of the Idaho Constitution.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Idaho State Lottery Commission and others, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District (Idaho), which ruled in favor of plaintiffs, taxpayers and others, and determined that a lottery initiative violated Idaho Const. art. III, § 20.


OVERVIEW: The governor signed a lottery initiative after 60 percent of the voters voted in favor of the initiative. Plaintiffs subsequently filed actions claiming that the lottery initiative was unconstitutional. The trial court granted a judgment in favor of plaintiffs. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court held that Idaho Const. art. III, § 20, which prohibited the legislature from authorizing a lottery or gift enterprise also prohibited the electorate from enacting a lottery through the initiative process. The court rejected defendants' argument that only the legislature was prohibited from authorizing a lottery where the Idaho Constitution read as a whole indicated that the purpose behind art. III, § 20 was to prohibit the authorization of a lottery. In addition, the court found that there was nothing in the legislative initiative provision, Idaho Const. art. III, § 1, that suggested an intent to affect the legislative prohibitions contained in other sections of the Constitution. The court concluded that legislative acts and legislation by referendum were on equal footing and were subject to the same limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that determined a lottery initiative violated the state constitution.

Blangers v. Department of Revenue & Taxation


No. 16404


Supreme Court of Idaho


114 Idaho 944; 763 P.2d 1052; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 44



May 25, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On Denial of Petition for Rehearing October 28, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. Watt E. Prather, District Judge.

Appeal from a declaratory judgment granted in favor of the respondents, Tax Commission, holding appellants subject to Idaho income tax.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railway employees sought review of a judgment entered by the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County, which declared the railway employees subject to the Idaho state income tax.


OVERVIEW: The primary issue on appeal was whether the state could impose an income tax on nonresident railway employees on nonstop transcontinental freight trains traveling across the panhandle of Idaho. The court reversed the declaratory judgment holding that while the laws of the state required the railway employees to pay the tax, imposition of the tax violated the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and the commerce clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. The railway employees' wages while traveling through the state were not attributable to any economic activity within the state and that neither the state's markets or its commerce affected the railway employees' income in any degree. They were present in the state because the trains on which they were employed necessarily traversed the panhandle of the state while traveling to their ultimate destinations. The state did not give anything to the railway employees for which it could ask a return and the mere presence of the railway employees in the state did not provide the nexus necessary to allow the income tax to be imposed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that declared the railway employees were subject to the state income tax.

McNichols v. Public Employee Retirement Sys.


No. 16796


Supreme Court of Idaho


114 Idaho 247; 755 P.2d 1285; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 49



May 20, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.

Appeal from the district court's grant of summary judgment which reinstated McNichols and Smith as police officer members of the Public Employee Retirement System.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Public Employee Retirement System of Idaho sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent employees and thereby reinstated them as police officer members, rather than general members, of the Public Employee Retirement System.


OVERVIEW: One employee worked as a patrol officer until he was injured at which time he worked as a supply officer. The other employee worked primarily as a clerical employee and also acted as a matron, in which case she had to carry a gun. The employer determined that the employees both qualified in hazardous law enforcement duties and, thus, qualified as police officer members, rather than general members, with regard to pension benefits. PERSI disagreed. The trial court held the legislature could not prospectively reduce the rate at which the employees earned retirement benefits. The court disagreed. Despite both employee's being given the classification of being engaged in hazardous law enforcement duties, neither had engaged in them for some time. The court held that it was not logical to hold that once an administrative agency misinterpreted a legislative mandate that the legislature was powerless to alter or amend the misinterpretation. Thus, from the date of the amendment of Idaho Code § 59-1302A, which sought to equalize pension benefits to state employees holding the same positions, although in other departments, the employees would earn benefits only at the general member rate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded.

Miles ex rel. Ratepayers of Idaho Power Co. v. Idaho Power Co.


No. 16614


Supreme Court of Idaho


1988 Ida. LEXIS 47



May 20, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As amended May 31, 1988; Petition for rehearing granted July 26, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.

Appeal from a dismissal in favor of respondent, Idaho Power, on grounds of a lack of a justifiable controversy. Affirmed on other grounds. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ratepayer sought review of a judgment from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which dismissed the ratepayer's complaint against respondents, power company, state, state officials, public utilities commission (commission), and department of water resources. The ratepayer's complaint sought to have certain implementing legislation, 1985 Idaho Sess. Laws ch. 14, § 3, declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The legislation implemented an agreement between the power company and the state, which resolved concerns over competing water rights in and around the Snake River. In part, the implementing legislation directed the commission to accept the agreement as reasonable and in the public interest. The district court dismissed the action on the grounds that the ratepayer lacked standing and that the controversy was not ripe for judicial resolution. The court affirmed the judgment on other grounds. The court found that the controversy was justiciable, rejecting respondents' arguments regarding the political question, standing, and ripeness doctrines. The court concluded that the implementing legislation did not violate the due process guarantees of the federal or state constitutions. The court rejected the ratepayer's assertion that he had a due process property interest in the rates paid for electricity. The court also held that the right to equal protection was not violated because the legislation was substantially related to the objective of settling adverse claims to water. Finally, the state constitution's prohibition against certain types of special legislation was not offended.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the ratepayer's action seeking to have the implementing legislation related to a water rights agreement declared unconstitutional.

 

180 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Coeur D'Alene Garbage Serv. v. Coeur D'Alene


No. 16712


Supreme Court of Idaho


114 Idaho 588; 759 P.2d 879; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 48



May 20, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. Watt E. Prather, District Judge.

Appeal from the district court's partial summary judgment determining that the defendant, City of Coeur d'Alene (the City), had taken property of plaintiff, Coeur d'Alene Garbage Service (Garbage Service), without just compensation and the district court's judgment awarding just compensation to Garbage Service with interest from the dates of taking.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of the order from the First Judicial District Court (Idaho), which entered partial summary judgment in favor of plaintiff garbage service determining that the city had taken property of the garbage service without just compensation. The district court awarded just compensation with interest from the dates of taking.


OVERVIEW: Before the city's annexation of some areas, which the garbage service was operating, the garbage service obtained written contracts with its customers in the areas proposed for annexation. After the completion of the annexation, the city gave the areas to its contractor. The garbage service filed for an injunction, to obtain just compensation for the taking of the property, and for damages for interference with contracts. The district court entered partial summary judgment in favor of the garbage service determining that the city had taken the property without just compensation and awarded just compensation with interest from the dates of taking. On appeal, the court held that if the city had merely regulated the operation of the garbage service in the annexed areas by requiring it to comply with reasonable standards established by the city, there would have been no taking, but it chose to take from the garbage service any opportunity to service its customers in the annexed areas. The court held that this exclusion entitled the garbage service to just compensation, with interest, and affirmed the district court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court.

Fairway Dev. Co. v. Bannock County


No. 16734


Supreme Court of Idaho


113 Idaho 933; 750 P.2d 954; 1988 Ida. LEXIS 29



February 23, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bannock. Honorable George W. Hargraves, District Judge.

Appeal from property tax assessment of fifty-six unit condominium complex solely on market data approach to value where forty-seven of the units had been utilized only as rental apartments for a period of years.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company sought review of the judgment of the Sixth Judicial District Court for Bannock County (Idaho), which granted summary judgment to defendants, county, county commissioners (Commissioners), county assessor (Assessor), and county treasurer (Treasurer), on the company's complaint for review of decisions by the Board of Tax Appeals (Board) and by the Commissioners, which upheld the Assessor's property tax evaluation.


OVERVIEW: The company owned and operated an apartment complex. It filed a Declaration of Condominium (Declaration) for the complex and attempted to sell the units as condominiums, while continuing to rent the unsold units as apartments. To date, 9 of the 56 units had been sold as condominiums. Since the Declaration, the county had appraised each unit as a condominium, using the market data method. As a result, the appraised value of each unit increased drastically. The Board and Commissioners upheld the Assessor's property tax evaluation. The company filed a complaint for review of these decisions, and the lower court granted summary judgment to the county, Commissioners, Assessor, and Treasurer. The court affirmed in part the judgment, holding that the classification of the complex as a condominium was constitutionally valid because the filing of the Declaration triggered the new classification, pursuant to the Condominium Property Act, Idaho Code § 55-1501 et seq. The judgment was reversed in part because the trial court failed to address the issue of whether the county's assessment scheme considered the complex' "actual and functional use," as required by Idaho Code § 63-202.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part the judgment, which granted summary judgment to the county, Commissioners, Assessor, and Treasurer, on the company's complaint for review of decisions by the Board and by the Commissioners, which upheld the Assessor's property tax evaluation of the company's complex.

H & V ENGG., INC. v. IDAHO STATE BD. OF PROFESSIONAL ENGRS. & LAND SURVEYORS


No. 16442

113 Idaho 646; 747 P.2d 55; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 356



November 4, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 7, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Robert M. Rowett, District Judge.

Appeal from the district court's decision and judgment affirming the disciplinary orders entered by respondent Idaho State Board of Professional Engineers and Land Surveyors.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant engineers challenged a judgment from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District (Idaho), which had refused to affirm or reverse a disciplinary order entered by respondent State Board of Professional Engineers and Land Surveyors.


OVERVIEW: Engineers sought review of the order of a district court, which had declined to affirm or reverse a disciplinary order entered by the State Board of Professional Engineers and Land Surveyors (Board). The engineers argued that the district court should have reversed the Board on the grounds that its order violated due process because the then-applicable regulations proscribing "misconduct" and "gross negligence" failed to adequately warn them as to what conduct would subject them to discipline. The court reversed and held that the district court was without jurisdiction to affirm the disciplinary order imposed by the Board after having initially ordered a remand, from which order the engineers perfected their appeal. Jurisdiction was vested in the court and the case should have been reversed because the standards upon which the Board disciplined the engineers did not warn them of prohibited conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the trial court, which had refused to affirm or reverse a disciplinary order against the engineers.

George v. Donovan


No. 16462


Supreme Court of Idaho


114 Idaho 388; 757 P.2d 651; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 345



October 1, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On Rehearing June 23, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, Hon. Robert M. Rowett, District Judge.

Appeal from order of district court issuing Writ of Mandate and enjoining defendants from disrupting disability benefits.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Idaho Department of Health and Welfare and State officials, sought review from an order of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which issued a writ of mandate and enjoined defendants from disrupting disability benefits and enjoined them from discontinuing disability benefits to plaintiffs, three developmentally disabled children.


OVERVIEW: The children were all developmentally disabled within the meaning of the Idaho Developmental Disabilities Services and Facilities Act of 1978, Idaho Code § 39-4604(2) (1985). The Department informed the children that benefits would be discontinued due to lack of funding. The Department submitted an affidavit to the trial court attesting to the lack of funds. The trial court held based on the pleadings, and Department documents that there were funds available for the provision of the services being denied the children in out Department programs. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court concluded that the trial court compelled the Department to do an act, which was in contravention of the Idaho Constitution. The court found that the Department appropriated funds on the particular program that provided benefits to the children and that the Department ran out of funds. The court held that a transfer of funds from one appropriation to another as the trial court held, without legislative consent, was in violation of the Idaho Const. art. 7, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded to the trial court.

State v. Lankford


Nos. 15760, 16170


Supreme Court of Idaho


113 Idaho 688; 747 P.2d 710; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 341



July 29, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 20, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Idaho County. Hon. George R. Reinhardt III, District Judge.

Appeal from conviction on two counts of first degree murder and the sentence of death imposed thereon, and appeal from denial of petition for post conviction relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Idaho County sentenced defendant to death after the jury convicted him of two counts of first-degree murder. Defendant appealed the convictions, the death sentence, and the denial of his petition for post conviction relief. The appeals were consolidated pursuant to Idaho Code § 19-2719.


OVERVIEW: Fearing that his probation for a Texas robbery conviction would be revoked, defendant fled to Idaho with his older brother. In order to further their flight from the Texas authorities, defendant and his brother decided to ditch their vehicle and steal a van. While defendant stood by armed with a shotgun, his brother crushed the victims' skulls with a nightstick. Rejecting defendant's defense theory that he was only an accessory after the fact, the jury convicted him of two counts of first-degree murder committed during the course of a robbery. Although defendant agreed to testify against his brother, the trial court nonetheless sentenced him to death. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that defendant's assignments of error either lacked merit or were not preserved for review. Moreover, the district court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant and there were no significant errors in the sentencing procedure. Furthermore, the trial court properly denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief. Finally, the court's automatic review of the death sentence did not reveal any reason to overturn the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for two counts of first-degree murder and the sentence of death imposed thereon.

 

188 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Nebeker v. Piper Aircraft Corp.


No. 16078


Supreme Court of Idaho


113 Idaho 609; 747 P.2d 18; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 332



June 25, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 8, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Jefferson County. Hon. Grant L. Young, District Judge.

Appeal from district court decision dismissing minor children of decedent as improper parties.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant brought a wrongful death action against defendant aircraft company and others in connection with the death of the claimant's wife in a plane crash. The claimant brought the action on behalf of himself and as guardian ad litem for his three minor children. The claimant appealed the judgment of the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District (Idaho), which dismissed the claim on behalf of the children.


OVERVIEW: The claimant challenged the trial court's decision finding that the children were not proper parties in the action. On appeal, the court held that because the entire estate of the deceased spouse was community property, the surviving spouse was the only proper party plaintiff in the action. The court stated that Idaho Code § 5-311 (1980) provided that a decedent's heirs or personal representatives were permitted to bring an action for damages against the person whose wrongful act or neglect caused the decedent's death. The court found that the statutory term "heirs" was determined by reference to the statutes of descent and distribution in effect at the time of the decedent's death. Under Idaho Code §§ 15-2-102 and 15-2-103, children were not considered heirs unless the decedent had left separate property with a value in excess of $ 50,000. The court found that this interpretation of the wrongful death statute was supported by legislative history. The court also found that the limitation on the number of persons who may bring a wrongful death action was not violative of the equal protection provisions in the Idaho and United States constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment, which dismissed the wrongful death claim on behalf of the children.

 

189 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Bingham Memorial Hosp. v. Idaho Dep't of Health & Welfare


No. 16597


Supreme Court of Idaho


112 Idaho 1094; 739 P.2d 393; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 328



June 19, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Gerald F. Schroeder, District Judge.

Appeal from a decision of the district court affirming a disallowance of certain reimbursement charges by the Department of Health and Welfare.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner hospital sought review of an order of the District Court of Ada County (Idaho), which affirmed the disallowance of certain reimbursement charges by respondent Idaho Department of Health and Welfare. The hospital argued that the Medicare charges were improperly calculated and that the regulations under which the calculations were made were unconstitutionally void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: The Department was obligated to pay the lowest of three alternative rates for certain hospital charges and the hospital disagreed with the department as to which rate was the lowest. A subsidy paid by the county was added to one of the rates, which increased it enough that it was not the lowest. The court affirmed and held that the Department in its audit used only Medicare Part A charges to determine the reimbursement and did not use Part B charges. The hospital argued that Part B charges should have been used and that the regulations were so vague that it was unclear that the reimbursement rate was limited to Part A charges. The court held that 42 C.F.R. § 450.30 clearly provided that the Medicare reimbursement rate was limited to Part A and was not void for vagueness. The Provider Reimbursement Manual regulations expressly excluded ancillary services from the calculation of Medicare Part A and to include the ancillary charges would have impermissibly inflated the reimbursement rate by permitting the hospital a double recovery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

 

190 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Edmonson


No. 16332


Supreme Court of Idaho


113 Idaho 230; 743 P.2d 459; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 318



May 29, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Latah County. Hon. John Bengston, District Judge.

Eric Roy Edmonson appeals from an order denying his motion seeking dismissal of a grand jury indictment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Permission to appeal by certification was granted after the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Latah County, denied defendant's motions for dismissal of a grand jury indictment charging him with racketeering, grand theft, conspiracy to engage in racketeering, conspiracy to engage in grand theft, and the falsification of corporate books and records. Defendants' co-conspirators were charged by information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the system used in Idaho of allowing the prosecutor unfettered discretion to initiate criminal proceedings by indictment or information without regard to any systematic or coherent policy violated his right to equal protection. The court, however, held that a prosecutor could proceed by either alternative, indictment or information. The court further held that where legally sufficient evidence would sustain an indictment, improperly admitted hearsay evidence would not overturn the grand jury's indictment. Furthermore, the prosecutor's allegedly improper comments regarding the credibility of witnesses and the weight and sufficiency of the evidence did not warrant a reversal when the record failed to indicate that prosecutor's comments infringed on the grand jury's decision-making function. Moreover, the unauthorized presence of a deputy clerk and an attorney before the grand jury did not necessitate a reversal when defendant failed to show that their presence prejudiced the independence and secrecy of the grand jury proceedings. The court concluded by noting that while there were some errors in the proceedings, none rose to a level requiring dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order and remanded the matter back for trial.
