Shurtliff v. Shurtliff


No. 16354


Supreme Court of Idaho


112 Idaho 1031; 739 P.2d 330; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 312



May 26, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bannock. Honorable W. H. Woodland, District Judge.

Appeal from a district court decision affirming a decree of divorce entered by magistrate court granting spousal support, distributing community property, and awarding attorney fees and costs.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband challenged a decision from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Bannock, which affirmed a decree of divorce entered by the magistrate court in respondent former wife's divorce action that granted spousal support, distributed community property, and awarded attorney fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: The former wife was granted a divorce with a disparate property settlement, spousal support, and attorney's fees. The former husband, who was found guilty of adultery, asserted that a disparate division was not warranted, the award of spousal support was improper, payment of educational expenses for five years was excessive; and the award of attorney's fees to the former wife was incorrect. The court affirmed the trial court's order because it determined that: (1) there was sufficient evidence of the factors under Idaho Code § 32-712 that demonstrated that the award was not an abuse of discretion; (2) spousal support was proper under Idaho Code § 32-702 because the innocent spouse lacked sufficient property for her reasonable needs and was unable to support herself through employment; (3) educational expenses as a part of spousal support were necessary to limit the overall spousal obligation by providing the innocent spouse with the means to become self-supporting; and (4) the financial disparity of the parties indicated that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in requiring the former husband to pay the attorney's fees as part of the community debt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and decree of divorce.

 

192 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Marek


No. 16178


Supreme Court of Idaho


112 Idaho 860; 736 P.2d 1314; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 306



April 17, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Nez Perce County. Honorable John H. Maynard, District Judge.

Appeal by defendant Leonard J. Marek, a Nez Perce Indian, from a conviction of Aggravated Battery after a jury trial and verdicts finding him guilty of Aggravated Battery and Felony Injury to Children. Defendant asserts that the State of Idaho lacked jurisdiction to try him for the crime of Aggravated Battery because such crime is within federal jurisdiction under the Major Crimes Act, 18 U.S.C. § 1153.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, affirmed in part, and remanded for further Proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a Native American, appealed his conviction for aggravated battery in violation of Idaho Code § 18-907(a) on the ground that the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Nez Perce County lacked jurisdiction to try him for the crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated battery in violation of § 18-907(a) and felony injury to a child in violation of Idaho Code § 18-1501(1). The jury returned a verdict of guilty on both counts. The trial court entered a judgment of conviction for aggravated battery and sentenced defendant to prison. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's conviction for aggravated battery. The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to enter a judgment of conviction for felony injury to a child and to sentence defendant accordingly. The court held that defendant was subject to federal prosecution for aggravated battery pursuant to the Major Crimes Act (Act) because defendant and the victim were Native Americans, the crime occurred in "Indian country," and aggravated battery was listed in § 1153 of the Act, 18 U.S.C.S. § 1153. The court determined, therefore, that the state lacked jurisdiction to try defendant for aggravated battery. The court held that the state's jurisdiction to try defendant for felony injury to a child was not preempted by the Act, and that a federal prosecution for aggravated battery would not subject defendant to double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and vacated his sentence for aggravated battery. The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to enter a judgment of conviction against defendant for felony injury to a child and to sentence him accordingly.

 

193 of 696 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Moran


No. 16161


Supreme Court of Idaho


112 Idaho 703; 735 P.2d 1014; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 301



April 6, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bannock County. Hon. Peter D. McDermott, District Judge.

Appeal from the district court's dismissal of the appellants' complaint as being untimely filed under the Statute of Limitations for professional malpractice actions, I.C. § 5-219(4).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an injured patient and her husband, sought review of an order of the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bannock County, which granted summary judgment to defendants, a doctor and cancer clinic, because the statute of limitations had run on the injured patient and husband's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: An injured patient was allegedly hurt somewhere between February and April of 1982, when her spinal cord was either exposed to an excessive dose of radiation or otherwise was irradiated during a cancer treatment. In early 1983, the injuries manifested themselves. A claim was filed in July of 1984, and suit was commenced against the doctor and cancer center in December of 1994. The doctor and cancer center moved for summary judgment. The trial court dismissed the case on the ground that the action was time-barred by Idaho Code § 5-219(4). The injured patient and her husband sought review. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that: (1) the district court properly applied Idaho Code § 5-219(4) to the instant case, and Idaho Code § 5-242 did not apply; (2) under Idaho Code § 5-219(4), the statute of limitations did not run until the physical injury "occurred"; and (3) there was a factual question when the damage "occurred," and the accident did not "occur" until the fact of injury became "objectionably ascertainable."


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that granted summary judgment to the doctor and cancer clinic and permitted the injured patient and her husband's medical malpractice action to continue.

Appeal from the appellate decision of the district court affirming the magistrate's award of spousal maintenance to Elaine Theiss.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband sought review of an appellate decision of the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County, which affirmed a magistrate's award of spousal maintenance to respondent former wife.


OVERVIEW: In a divorce case involving the award of temporary spousal maintenance, the former husband appealed the district court's award of maintenance to his former wife. However, the court found that the district court had not considered all of the relevant factors necessary to a fair, just and equitable award. The court noted that it was beyond dispute that the wife could find employment as a bank teller or in another clerical position. The question to be determined on remand was whether this type of clerical job would enable the wife to meet her reasonable needs, taking into consideration the criteria set forth in § 32-705(2).


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and remanded for further findings.

Supreme Court of Idaho


112 Idaho 508; 733 P.2d 729; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 278

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable W. E. Smith, District Judge.

This is an appeal granting the defendant-respondent State Tax Commission and 20 Idaho counties summary judgment on their cross-motion for summary judgment and denying the cross-motion for summary judgment of plaintiffs-appellants V-1 Oil Company, Weathertite Block Company, Six B, Inc., S. H. Bennion, Faye J. Bennion, and V-1 Self Service.



DISPOSITION: District court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, the Idaho State Tax Commission and 20 Idaho counties, in the taxpayers' action seeking a declaratory judgment that the procedures of certain counties in accumulating budget surpluses were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court granted partial summary judgment determining that taxpayers' properties were taxable, the parties settled questions regarding valuation, taxes and penalties. The settlement agreement reserved to the taxpayers the right to litigate two issues: (1) whether the counties must take surpluses into account when establishing current budgets so as not to impose excessive levies, and (2) whether tax rates as between real and personal property as between the counties must be uniform. The parties stipulated that the two issues could be determined by cross-motions for summary judgment without trial. The court granted summary judgment in favor of the State and the counties. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that summary judgment was proper. Even though the trial court found the taxpayers' facts as alleged to be true, those facts only indicated that the counties had surpluses for the years in question. There was no showing as to whether the counties considered the surpluses in the following year's budget process. The court also held that Idaho Code § 31-1605A was constitutional because it was designed to carry out the intent of Idaho Const. art. VII, §§ 15 and 16.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.

 

197 of 696 DOCUMENTS


McBride v. McBride


No. 16369


Supreme Court of Idaho


112 Idaho 959; 739 P.2d 258; 1987 Ida. LEXIS 262



January 7, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On Rehearing June 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Latah County. Honorable John H. Bengtson, District Judge.

Appeal from an order of the district court granting the defendant husband's motion to dismiss the plaintiff-wife's motion to vacate a divorce decree pursuant to I.R.C.P. 60(b).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife sought review of an order from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Latah County (Idaho) that granted defendant husband's motion to dismiss the wife's motion which sought to vacate a divorce decree.


OVERVIEW: The wife consulted with an attorney concerning a divorce and the wife's attorney drafted a property settlement and separation agreement. The husband and wife signed the agreement and the wife filed an action for divorce and prayed that the trial court approve the property settlement and separation agreement. The husband defaulted and the trial court entered a decree of divorce and approved the parties' agreement. Thereafter, the wife filed a petition to modify and vacate the divorce decree and sought one half interest in the husband's military retirement pay. The husband filed a motion to dismiss the wife's motion and the trial court granted the husband's motion. The wife appealed and the court affirmed the trial court's order and held that a divorce decree was final, res judicata, and no jurisdiction existed to modify the property provisions. Enactment of the Uniformed Services Former Spouses' Protection Act, 10 U.S.C.S. § 1408, did not provide justification for modification of the decree. Further, relief under Idaho R. Civ. P. 60(b)(4) or 60(b)(5) was unavailing because the decree was not void, no mistake was claimed, and the decree was not prospective or inequitable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that granted the husband's motion to dismiss the wife's motion that sought to vacate the parties' divorce decree.

 

198 of 696 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bennion


No. 15717


Supreme Court of Idaho


112 Idaho 32; 730 P.2d 952; 1986 Ida. LEXIS 544



December 18, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonneville County, Honorable H. Reynold George, District Judge.

Appeal from the district court's denial of a motion for jury trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of the judgment of the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonneville County, which denied appellant's motion for a jury trial after appellant was accused of disobeying an official traffic control device in violation of Idaho Code § 49-611(1).


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver challenged the constitutionality of the Idaho Traffic Infractions Act (ITIA), Idaho Code § 49-3401, and the denial of his right to a jury trial pursuant to Idaho Const. art. I, § 7, following a magistrate's ruling that appellant was guilty of disobeying a traffic control device in violation of Idaho Code § 49-611(1). Appellant argued that Idaho Const. art. I, § 7 guaranteed him a jury trial and that although the ITIA defined infractions as civil public offenses for purposes of constitutional analysis, the infraction was criminal. The court affirmed, holding that the ITIA was not unconstitutional. The court held that Idaho Const. art. I, § 7 guaranteed a jury trial whenever the possible sanction included imprisonment and that the infraction of which appellant was accused was not punishable in this manner. The court held that even if appellant refused to pay the fine imposed, the worst he would suffer was the suspension of his license. The court held that the sanction imposed, a fine not exceeding $ 100, did not rise to the level of a punitive, criminal sanction rather it was remedial in nature and served as a form of damages for the state's enforcement costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant driver's motion for a jury trial. The court held that although the prosecutions of all public offenses were criminal actions, it was not unconstitutional to preclude a trial by jury so long as the offense charged was not punishable by imprisonment or other criminal sanction.

 

199 of 696 DOCUMENTS


McGhee ex rel. McGhee v. Glenns Ferry


No. 16147


Supreme Court of Idaho


111 Idaho 921; 729 P.2d 396; 1986 Ida. LEXIS 540



November 26, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Elmore County. Hon. Robert M. Rowett, District Judge.

Appeal from trial court's granting of summary judgment to respondent, City of Glenns Ferry.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an injured child and her mother, appealed from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Elmore County, which in an action based on theories of negligence and strict liability granted summary judgment to respondent city on the ground that the city was immune from liability pursuant to Idaho Code § 36-1604.


OVERVIEW: The injured child was injured when she fell from a swing located at a park in the city. Her mother brought an action against the city, the owner of the park, based on theories of negligence and strict liability. The district court granted summary judgment to the city. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court noted that § 36-1604 provided limited liability to landowners who gratuitously allowed others to use the land, or equipment attached to or used on the land, for recreational purposes. The court found that the city was an "owner" within the meaning of the statute, found that the park was "public land" within the meaning of the statute, and ruled that the statute applied to public entities. The court also ruled that the operation of a city park was for "recreational purposes" within the meaning of the statute and that use of a park swing was a "recreational purpose" within the meaning of the statute. The court said that although the statute listed several activities in the definition of "recreational purposes," the statute expressly provided that the list was not exhaustive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's summary judgment granted to the city in the injured child and her mother's action for negligence and strict liability against the city.

 

200 of 696 DOCUMENTS


K Mart Corp. v. Idaho State Tax Comm'n


No. 16234


Supreme Court of Idaho


111 Idaho 719; 727 P.2d 1147; 1986 Ida. LEXIS 519



September 18, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 7, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for the County of Ada. Honorable Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.

Appeal from the district court's order discharging a deficiency judgment against respondent for use taxes allegedly due on newspaper advertising inserts.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Idaho State Tax Commission sought review of a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which held that respondent advertiser's newspaper inserts were not subject to the use tax. The trial court held that the inserts fell within the production exemption of Idaho Code § 63-3622(d) and that the sales tax regulation interpreting the applicable statutes violated equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The advertiser's out-of-state printer shipped advertising inserts to newspapers selected by the advertiser. Through contracts with the newspapers, the advertiser designated the number of inserts to be distributed as well as the date of distribution. The court determined that the advertiser was subject to use tax on the inserts under Idaho Code § 63-3621 because the advertiser owned the inserts until it gave them away to newspaper purchasers and it exercised such control of the inserts under its contracts with newspapers to constitute "use" of the inserts within the meaning of Idaho Code § 63-3615(b). The court also found that the advertiser did not qualify for the production exemption under Idaho Code § 63-3622(d) because it was primarily devoted to retailing, not manufacturing, processing, mining, farming, or fabricating. The court concluded that the advertiser was liable for the use tax even if the tax regulations interpreting the use tax statutes were unconstitutional. The advertiser owed tax under a statutory scheme that was constitutional, and assessment of the use tax pursuant to a regulation that did not comport with the constitution did not defeat its statutory liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment with costs to the Commission. The court did not award attorney fees.
